
### Overview

Although not the topmost level of the dungeon, the Halls of Thoth are the most accessible level to the surface (via the Grand Pyramid of Thoth at AV-15, which leads to 3-1). As a result, it sees a fair amount of traffic, particular in its central areas (3-1 to 3-20 or so). It contains numerous points of egress and access to Levels 1, 2, 4, and 5, as well as to several sub-levels. In addition to being significant for its accessibility, the level is also notable for its size; it is one of the largest levels of the entire complex.

The northern, worked areas of the level (3-1 to 3-162) were mostly constructed by the priesthood of Thoth during the period of Archontean domination, although the rival priesthood of Set delved the westernmost section that leads directly to the Forum of Set (4-2). Today, the precincts of Thoth are divided into smaller regions, many controlled by one of the factions of Arden Vul.

A group of evil, grimalkin extortionists led by Parames Plumthorn (3-5) has but recently set up operations (including a poison manufactory – see 3-4) just outside the entry chamber (3-2); they claim suzerainty over areas 3-2 to 3-35 and demand tribute from any who enter this territory.

The grimalkin have run into trouble with the goblins of King Weskenim, whose main hold lies below (SL4), but who have established a foothold on Level 3 (area 3-7) as well as on Level 5 
(5-43 to 5-51). The goblins resent the newly arrived halflings, and actively seek allies in their extermination.

To the west, the priesthood of Set has re-established its influence in its ancient demesne (3-89 to 3-111) and conduct dire rituals in their upper temple (3-90).

The central regions of the level, which originally served as the administrative hub of the priests of Thoth, is now home to the highly disciplined cohorts of the beastmen of Deino (3-120 to 3-162). The beastmen have cleared all the areas east of the Great Hall (3-120), and conduct frequent patrols both north, towards the rest of the old precincts of Thoth, and south into the Great Cavern (3-163, 3-172).

The unworked, natural, portions of the level are dominated by the massive Great Cavern, which itself is bisected by a subterranean river (the Seamly Run - see 3-217, 3-230 and 3-231) and a small lake (3-164). No one faction calls this area home, although the deranged magician Trocadero of Newmarket (3-176), who thinks himself the reincarnation of Ptarmis of Thoth (3-174), is trying to lay claim to the southern Great Cavern through his hold over the fungal foresters. 

General Construction Notes
* Heqeti areas: 3-51, 3-117, 3-192.
* Rudishva areas: 3-39
* Archontean areas: all worked areas (except 3-39, 3-51, 3-117, and 3-192).

Iconic Areas
* The Glory of Thoth (3-2)
* The Great Chasm (3-38)
* The Great Hall (3-123)
* The Great Cavern (3-163, 3-172)

		* Pakhneter Plumthorn
* Beastmen
	* Count Skleros, beastman leader (3-151)
	* Count Trisko the Natty, beastman and commander of the Long Range Cavern Patrol (3-154)

* Sir Simonet, a Sun-Scarred Knight (3-131)
* Trocadero of Newmarket, crazed magic user (3-176)


Significant Regions of Level 3

1. Northern Region: Precincts of Thoth (3-1 to 3-70)
The halls in this region were the center of the public rituals held in 
honor of Thoth. The great statue of Thoth (the Glory of Thoth - 3-2), 
the three mystery chambers (3-9, 3-10, and 3-11), and the mortuary 
centers for devotees (3-16 and 3-22) were among the ‘sights’ visited 
by the faithful. Of course the priests of Thoth also kept some sites 
carefully hidden, as befit the god of hidden knowledge. 
Factions: The band of evil halfling thugs and brigands led by the 
notorious Phlebotomas Plumthorn (3-5) occupies a key (and 
highly defensible) section of the region adjacent to the main entry 
point from the surface (areas 3-3 to 3-6). They claim authority over 
the entire region and attempt to extort licenses and tribute from all 
who pass through area 3-2.

Construction: Almost all construction in this region is Archontean, 
with 10’ ceilings and iron-bound wooden doors. The Thoth pri-
ests preferred to sheath the stone walls with plaster, on which 
they painted elaborate frescoes celebrating Thoth. Many of the 
frescoes are still visible and might reveal some general or even 
useful information to those unfamiliar with Thoth. Considering 
a 10’x10’ section of wall for a turn might reveal some useful and 
comprehensible information (25% chance). If so indicated, the 
GM should roll d100 on the table on the next page to determine 
what the art-lover has learned.
Environment: Cool and dry

2. Western Region: Hidden Temples (areas 3-71 to 3-117)
To the west of the public areas of the cult of Thoth was the great 
private temple of the Thoth priesthood (3-71). Quite nearby is 
the main temple to Set, which was restored over the past several 
decades by a rejuvenated Set cult. Although the two temples were 
distinct in antiquity, the modern Set cult has connected the two 
areas via new construction and is contemplating expansion into 
the empty halls of their former rival. 
Factions: The cult of Set fully controls important sections of this 
region (3-89 to 3-110). Reckless incursions into Set’s territory will 
be met swiftly by deadly force. 
Construction: All worked areas are Archontean, with 10’ ceilings 
and iron-bound wooden doors. Thothian areas were plastered 
in antiquity and covered in frescoes (see table in region 1); the 
Set cult preferred to decorate the stone directly, and adopted no 
general artistic scheme (hence no table). 
Environment: Cool and dry

3. Central Region: Precincts of the Beastmen (3-120 to 3-162)
In antiquity this was the administrative and residential district for 
the priest of Thoth, centering around the iconic Great Hall (3-123), 
which extended upwards to Sub-Level 3. Today the non-secret 
areas form the domain of the beastmen and their foul mistress, 
Deino (3-158).

Factions: The beastmen are the dominant players in this region. 
They patrol the area regularly in banda (patrols) of six plus a 
sergeant. They are always willing to negotiate first, but are quick to 
defend themselves. The will warn those visitors whom they like or 
admire not to seek audiences with their mistress. 
Construction: All worked areas are Archontean, typically with 
10’ ceilings and iron-bound wooden doors. The beastmen have 
worked hard to scrub away any of the old images of the cult of 
Thoth, leaving the walls bare of decoration in most places.
Environment: Cool and dry

Generic Wall Iconography for Northern Region: Precincts of Thoth

D100 Description of Image(s) GM Notes

01-20
Ibis-headed Thoth worshipped by orange-robed priests

One of the most common images of Thoth was as an ibis-headed person (c.f. his cult statues at AV-15 and 3-2). Orange robes with cylindrical headdresses indicate Thoth priests

21-30
A large ibis flanked by servitor baboons wielding clubs

Thoth was commonly represented by ibises and baboons

31-35
Baboons beat a black boar with clubs

The black boar is a symbol of Set, the rival of Thoth

36-45
Ibis-headed Thoth points with left arm to a Mithric glyph. Two words in Mithric script spew fromThoth’s mouth on a slip of parchment

The Glyph is that for magic. The words say “I am.” To readers of 
Mithric, this is simple: “I am magic”, that is, Thoth is the source 
of magic. The placement of the left arm is a clue to the working 
of the statues in 3-2, 3-15 and 3-40

46-55
Loops of parchment spew from ibis-headed Thoth’s 
mouth and into the hands of numerous human beings, 
some in orange robes. Words are visible on the parchment

Thoth was the source of writing. The words say
“Writing is power” in Mithric

56-65
A standard image of ibis-headed Thoth has been
defaced, and graffiti in the form of a boar (50%) or
a dog-like animal with curved snout, square ears
and a forked tail (50%)

The boar and the Set animal are common representations of 
Set. The modern cult of Set (see 3-89 to 3-117 and much of 
Level 4) is responsible for the graffiti.

66-75
A baboon crouching in the ‘scribe’ position (knees pulled 
to chest), with a book open on its knees. The left paw of 
the baboon is raised in greeting.

A reference to Thoth’s role as recorder of the deeds of the dead, 
and in his baboon form. The placement of the arm is a clue to 
the working of the statues at 3-2, 3-15 and 3-40

76-80
Ibis-headed Thoth walks beside a woman bearing a white feather in her hand; to either side are sarcophagi.

Thoth was associated with Maat, whose image was the white 
feather. A clue to the efficacy of the feathers of Maat found at 
3-19 in repelling the undead of the catacombs (3-22)

81-90
Ibis-headed Thoth holds the reins of a chariot in
his outstretched left hand. At Thoth’s side is a
rayed orb. The chariot travels through the sky,
above adoring orange-clad priests

The Archontean cult of Thoth associated him with bringing 
the light of knowledge, and saw him as the driver of the solar 
chariot. A reference to the Litany of Light (see 2-2 through 2-5).

91-95
Unusually, ibis-headed Thoth stands with both 
arms raised above his head. In front of him, human 
worshippers fall into a pit.

A clue to the danger of manipulating the statue of Thoth at 
UP-1 and 3-15 in the wrong way

96-100
Humans bearing gifts of gems, cloth, golden statuettes 
and scrolls approach ibis-headed Thoth, whose left
hand is outstretched in benediction

An important clue to manipulating the statues at 3-2, 3-15 and 
3-40 so as to locate the treasure room (3-23). Also a hint about 
the benefits of offering Thoth (3-2) gifts.



4. Southern Region: Great Cavern and Surrounding Caves (3-163 to 3-230)
South of the Great Hall of Thoth lies the enormous Great Cavern 
(3-163, 3-172), bisected by an underground river called the Seamly 
Run (3-217, 3-230, 3-231) and a small lake (3-164). Numerous side 
caves and tunnels connect to the Great Cavern, and a few tombs
crafted by the paranoid in antiquity may be found scattered among 
those caves. Ptarmis, a priest of Thoth, discovered the Great 
Cavern during the glory years of Archontean Arden Vul. It was 
he who cultivated the giant species of mushroom that form the 
current fungal forest, it was he who introduced the fungal foresters 
as cultivators of the mushrooms, and it was he (and his men) who 
built the hematite gates (3-177) and the parvis with its great chair 
(3-175, 3-176). So enamored was Ptarmis by the Great Cavern that 
he commanded his tomb be prepared here (see 3-174).
Factions: No faction controls this region. The fungal foresters 
patrol the fungal forest, but are not territorial. The beastmen’s Long 
Range Cavern Patrol frequents the Great Cavern in order to bring 
food and other supplies to Deino and their comrades. A fearsome 
hag has a small domain among the river caves (3-204 to 3-206, 
3-219, 3-221 to 3-224). The cult of Set has a tiny foothold to the far 
west (3-193 to 3-195, 3-211 to 3-212).
Construction: The few worked areas are Archontean, albeit with 
stone doors.
Environment: The area is substantially more humid than the rest of 
the area, and some sections (e.g. the Great Cavern) are quite warm.


## Level 3: 1 - 15

### 3-1: Entrance Stairs (up to UP-5)

* The stairs down from the Great Pyramid (UP-5) are steep and cramped, descending  350’ and exiting into 3-2.
	* They were once flanked with brightly colored frescoes outlining the glories of Thoth.
	* Now blackened with soot, grime, and desecration. Little is left: a flash of gold paint, a blue beak, some broken runes.
	* A variety of graffiti, some informational and some obscene, 1d4 instances of graffiti scratched onto each 10’ section of wall.

D20 Graffiti GM Notes

1-4
A name: e.g., Gil, Aethelwulf, Hoss, Flet, Jilken, Tom the Mighty, Rache, Dalton, Roger the 
Rapier, Anna the Archer, etc. 

The GM could or should add names to this list that reflect figures from his/her own 
campaign. In the samples, Dalton and Roger the Rapier are both leaders of rival NPC adventuring groups. The language/script in which the names are written varies, either at choice of GM or as appropriate to a name. For example, Dalton and Roger are both Archontean and thus their names are in that language

5
One of the dog troopers warned us not to seek an audience with his mistress, the powerful sorceress Deino. Why not?

A reference to the beastmen (3-138 to 3-162) and the dangers posed by any meeting with Deino (3-158). Language: Archontean

6
Thoth’s knowledge - and his wealth - remains hidden. But I know how to unlock it. Look to the arms!

A reference to the puzzle involving the statues at 3-2, 3-15, and 3-40, which if manipulated correctly reveal the path to the hoard at 3-23/3-24. Language: Elvish

7
I hate grimalkin! (written 7’ upthe wall)

A reference to the band of halfling thugs who dominate parts of Level 3 (3-2 to 3-6). Language: Wiskin

8
The feathery blessing of Maat fends off the walkers! Do not ignore her soft offering!

A hint about how use of the feather of Maat (3-19) will render the user immune from the undead of the catacombs of Thoth (3-22). Language: Mithric

9-10
Plumthorn Rules these Halls!  Obey Him!

Written 3’ from the ground. A reference to the leader of the halflings who inhabit 3-2 to 3-6. 
Language: Archontean

11
The Darlings are stupid. They left the portcullis open again. I hope they all die horribly.

Refers to the portcullises at 3-21, and the inadvisability of leaving them open (so undead can access the eastern areas). Darlings is a reference to Dalton’s Darlings, one of the suggested rival NPC adventuring parties (see NPC appendix). Language: Archontean

12
The Darlings claim this level! All the treasure is ours! So long, suckers!

A reference to Dalton’s Darlings, one of the suggested rival NPC adventuring parties (see NPC appendix). Language: Archontean

13
Wulf - Wait for me in the pyramid room. If you don’t see me, I will have ascended. 
[Signed] Edgar

A reference to the small pyramid in 3-11, and its ability to teleport explorers to 2-8.
Language: Thorcin

14
Grimalkin rule ok! (Written at halfling height)

A positive reference to Phlebotomas Plumthorn and his band of extortionists (see 3-2 to 
3-6). Language: Archontean

15
A faint and primitive sketch of a biped with huge thighs and an amphibian head. 
An arrow points to its eye, with the caption ‘danger’

An image of a pukel-mander (see new magic items, see 2-56C, 3-11, etc.). Placing a tear of Kauket (see new magic items)in the pukel-mander’s eye canbe quite dangerous! The
caption is in Mithric

16
A crude map of 3-2, 3-15 and 3-16 with an ‘x’ and ‘look here’ scrawled next to the intersection at 3-15 

Self-explanatory, with an oblique hint as to the significance of the statue of Thoth at 3-15.
Language: Archontean

17
We shall return.  The secrets of  the Paleologue will not remain hidden. Look to Gog for directions.

A reference to the lost tomb of Hithra Paleologos (3-36) and the fact that Gog (5-2) can give 
directions to many locations (but not to 3-36). Language: Elvish

18
We followed the arrogant, red-armored fools into the great temple of Thoth, but then we 
lost them … and half our party.

A hint that the cult of Set is located west of the Great Temple of Thoth (3-71), i.e. at areas 3-89 to 3-117. Also an oblique reference to the danger of the slime kraken in 3-71. 
Language: Thorcin

19
Grumak went for a boat ride in the lake. Big mistake.

Refers to the lake (3-164) that bisects the Great Cavern (3-163 and 3-172), and is an oblique 
hint about the giant crabs that infest the waters of the lake.  Language: Wiskin

20
KK is watching us all the time! Don’t trust the talking puppets!

A reference to Kerbog Khan (see SL12-25) and one of his many types of automatons.
Language: Archontean

### 3-2: The Glory of Thoth

* At the foot of the long staircase from the surface, this 30' high chamber was originally the main public site for the veneration of Thoth.
	* Lit by guttering torches (placed by the grimalkin) in sconces along the north, south and west walls.  They shed dim light, but don't fully illuminate the room's center.
	* The wall plaster is badly damaged, but the ceiling plaster is still intact.
		* If able to see the ceiling clearly, there is an image of humans bearing valuable goods – gems, cloth, golden statuettes, scrolls – to ibis-headed Thoth.
			* Thoth is pointing with an outstretched left hand, while his right hand is flat against his thigh (a clue concerning the puzzle of 3-2a).
	* Substantial debris - wrecked furniture, destroyed armor and equipment, bits of bone and leather - has accumulated in the four corners of the chamber.
		* There is dust everywhere, but clear paths lead from the stairs to 3-3, 3-12, 3-15, and 3-31, and no dust is found around the central statue.
	* A grand statue of Thoth stands in the center of the chamber (3-2a).
	* The body of a recently slain adventurer slumps against the west wall.
		* The grimalkin have already looted it, but missed a clerical talisman (find traps) stuffed into his boot.
* The Poisoner Extortionists
	* Any lights or noise (such as experimenting with the statue) will bring some shouts from 3-3, followed by the arrival of a group of 6 grimalkin, led by Rosk Winterclaw.
		* Rosk and his thugs interrogate the party, and inform them that in order to explore the dungeon each of them must buy an ‘adventuring license’ from the ‘big boss’ of this area, his ‘good friend,’ Parames Plumthorn (3-5).
		* Licenses cost 25 gp up front, plus 10 gp per sortie into 3-2, plus a 10% tithe of any treasure (including magic items) found in the dungeon.
			* If they pay up, the grimalkin treat them neutrally, although they are extra-vigilant so as to secure any subsequent ‘fees’.
			* If they refuse to pay, but look powerful, the thugs retreat to 3-3 to join their comrades; then engage in guerrilla warfare against the PCs from this point onward.
			* If they refuse, but look weak, Rosk and his men attack.  They'll take prisoners for ransom, sale to the Setites, or as a Mortality test subject.

Rosk Winterclaw, 5th-level grimalkin thief: SZ S; AL CE; AC 5; MV 90’; HD 5, HP 22; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (short sword) or 2-5 (dagger). Abilities: STR 16, INT 9, WIS 10, DEX 17, CON 10, CHA 15. Special: thief skills are PP 60%, OL 62%, F/RT 50%, MS 52%, HS 57%, HN 25%, CW 77%, RL 30%. Special attacks: poison; both weapons are coated “Mortality” poison (see 3-4), which has an onset of 2-8 rounds, and does 20 HP damage, or half if a save is made.
* Possessions: leather armor; short sword; dagger; potion of invisibility.

5 1st-level grimalkin fighters: SZ S; AL NE; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1; HP: 10, 9, 8, 8, 7; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (spear), 2-7 (club), or 2-5 (sling). Possessions: studded leather armor and shield; spears; clubs; slings; 3-18 sp each.

14 / 22, def 15, atk 17
0 / 10, def 14, atk 12
0 / 9

##### 3-2a: Statue of Thoth 

* This massive onyx statue of the ibis-headed god is 15’ tall stands on a granite pedestal (3’ tall), facing north.
	* Thoth’s ibis head is made of white marble. His eyes are empty sockets.
	* A perfectly proportioned and lifelike human body, right foot is advancing slightly in classic Egyptian fashion.
	* His arms hang at his sides, but rotate on stone pins.
		* They can be pulled upward and forward to any position between 0 (arm at his side) and 180 degrees (hand pointing straight up at the ceiling).
	* If the floor around the statue is closely examined, 2-in-6 chance to notice scoring, as if a heavy stone object (such as the statue) had been dragged across the floor.
* At the foot of the statue is a large stone chest that is part of the pedestal.
	* Worshipers would deposit their offerings into the chest.
	* If a magic scroll (arcane or divine) is placed in the chest and the name of Thoth is invoked (in any form whatsoever, as long the name is mentioned), the donor gain +1 to Int or Wis (random).  The scroll vaporizes instantly.
		* If the spell was 1st to 3rd level (magic user or clerical): lasts 1 week.
			* Can be gained once per week.
		* If the spell was 4th level or above: permanent.
			* Int and Wis can each be increased once, ever.  Which stat is gained is still random, so it may take more than just 2 scrolls to boost each stat.
		* Any symbol of Set placed in the chest produces a column of black flame (5d6 damage) engulfing everything within 25’ of the statue. 
* The statue is also the key to an important puzzle that opens the hidden treasury.
	* If the arms of all three statues of Thoth on Level 3 (at 3-2, 3-15, and 3-40) set so the left hand is parallel to the floor (90 degrees) and the right is at his side (0 degrees), the pedestal here grinds backwards to reveal a set of stairs leading downwards toward the north.
		* After 1 hour of inactivity, the arms reset to default (both facing down).
		* The grimalkin have not figured out the puzzle (but know there's a secret door of some kind under the statue), and the Setites are too afraid of the statue to manipulate it.
	* Hidden Staircase and Passageway: descend 10' down dusty, cobweb-choked stairs to a 5' wide, 7' tall tunnel northwest.
		* The walls are plaster covered with colorful images: Thoth in majesty, Thoth receiving wisdom, languages of various sorts being spewed from the mouths of ibises and baboons, etc. 

### 3-3: Portcullis and Grimalkin Guardpost

* The passage has been fitted with an iron gate, in the center of which is a (grimalkin-sized) iron door.
	* The two door guards keep the key.  The lock is cheap (+10% to pick).
	* They will never allow the PCs to pass on their own; if a parlay is required, either Rosk (3-2) or Parames himself (3-5) will come to the gate to negotiate.
* 2 guards man the post.  If unaware of approach, they will be chatting idly.
* Nearby a horn hangs from a peg hammered into an image of Thoth.
	* If the party is known to be hostile, or if they show hostility, a guard sounds it, calling grimalkin from from 3-4, 3-5 and 3-6 who begin arriving in 1d4 rounds.

2 1st-level grimalkin fighters: SZ S; AL NE; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1; HP: 8, 9; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (spear), 2-7 (club), or 2-5 (sling). Possessions: studded leather armor and shield; spears; clubs; slings; 3-18 sp each.

### 3-4: Ancient Tombs and Halfling Camp

* This was a burial chamber for notables in the cult of Thoth, and has been badly treated by time; the walls stained with soot, urine, and worse.
	* Three massive stone sarcophagi sit empty in the center of the room, lids pried open long ago, lying shattered on the floor.
	* The chamber is lit by three large candelabra, each placed near a sarcophagus, as well as a small cookfire in the northwest corner and a tripod of heating in the southeast corner.
	* The northeast corner of the room is open to the chasm (3-38).  A small parapet of rubble (3’ high) has been erected across that opening.
		* Covered passage (north): led to 3-40, filled with rubble, bricked up, and plastered over in antiquity.  The grimalkin haven't noticed it yet.  Detect as secret door.
	* The poison manufactory is set up along the south wall.
		* A rickety table with a set of glass alchemical equipment (500 gp), including two alembics, a retort, two crucibles and a mortar and pestle.
		* Beside the table, a burlap sack with 6 glass bulbs of clear, viscous liquid (spider venom, 30 gp each) and 3 sacks of herbs, dyes, and alchemical powders (45 gp each).
		* On the other side, a padded strongbox (locked) with 18 small glass vials with the word “Mortality” etched on the side (the street name of Parames’s poison), filled with a sticky, green substance.
			* Mortality: 2d4 rounds onset, 20 damage, save for half.
			* Each vial holds 3 doses and sells for 100 gp to the right buyer.
			* Because it is so valuable, Parames does not automatically issue it to his rank and file thugs, reserving it for himself, Rosk (3-2), and Blandveg (3-5).
			* If Parames realizes that his crew is under concerted attack and has time, he will issue poison to the 1st-level fighters and 2nd-level thieves.

* In time, the grimalkin may erect an unsteady, makeshift rope bridge anchored to the sarcophagi across the chasm between 3-4 and 3-40 (20’ span) to explore further.

* Tactical Note: The grimalkin here and elsewhere fight from behind the tombs, using them as cover (75%).

5 1st-level halfling fighters: SZ S; AL NE; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1; HP: 10, 9, 8, 8, 7; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (spear), 2-7 (club), or 2-5 (sling). Possessions: studded leather armor and shield; spears; 
clubs; slings; 3-18 sp each.

5 2nd-level halfling thieves: SZ S; AL NE; AC 5; MV 90’; HD 2; HP 11, 10, 10, 9, 9; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6 (short sword), 1-4 (dagger), or 2-5 (sling). Special: the thieves have DEX 17, and the following thief skills: PP 45%, OL 44%, F/RT 30%, MS 36%, HS 35%, HN 15%, CW 71%. Possessions: leather armor; short swords; daggers, slings; 3-18 sp each.

### 3-5: More Ancient Tombs, with Halfling Leaders

* This room is almost identical to 3-4: formerly gilded luxury paintings now stained with soot and other unknown substances.  The three leaders of the Poisoners reside in this chamber.
	* Three stone sarcophagi lie broken and looted in the center of the chamber.
		* A false bottom in the southern sarcophagus has escaped detection.
			* A silver, bejeweled holy symbol of Thoth (850 gp); 575 ancient copper bits and 352 ancient silver pennies; a moldering illusionist scroll (phantasmal force, phantom armor, invisiblity); 2 arrows of striking (new).
	* The northeastern corner of the chamber is open to the chasm.
		* A 3’-tall parapet of debris is piled across the edge, with noisy bells and bits of metal tied to strings as a crude alarm if something comes out of the chasm.
	* A locked, iron-banded wooden chest and an iron lock (key held by Parames).
		* 432 copper pieces; 243 sp; 957 gp; two ancient holy symbols of Thoth in the form of baboons (150 gp); a holy symbol of Set in the form of a crocodile (100 gp); six gems (10, 20, 30, 10, 50, and 130 gp); 3 codices (Great Villains of Archontos, part IV: Larsinius the Exarch, Thorcin Poisons and their Cures, and Emperors of Archontos, Volume I)
		* Blandveg’s spell book: enlarge, friends, jump, magic missile, jump, magic aura, read magic, shield, sleep; Frigg’s jelly legs (new), knock, mirror image, scare.
	* Supplies: 2 large casks of ale, several sides of curing meat (deer), several bags of turnips, apples, and potatoes, and a large sack of rock-hard biscuits.
	* Although Rosk Winterclaw has his bedroll here, he is usually in 3-2.

* Negotiating with Plumthorn
	* Phlebotomas does not typically negotiate with newcomers, leaving the mundane business and dirty work to his lieutenant, Rosk.  Only in the case of pressing need, or if visitors have convinced the guards at 3-3 that they have valuable information, will Plumthorn deign to parlay.
	* He might be willing to trade information. Parames knows the following information about the Halls:
		* a. Parames suspects there is a secret door connected to the statue in 3-2.
		* b. there is at least one room across the chasm (i.e., 3-40).
		* c. goblins lurk to the southeast (3-7); they would like to control area 3-2, but the grimalkin have stymied them.
		* d. occasional groups of hooded figures have been seen moving between the west and the south. (Set worshipers)
		* e. dangerously large spiders lurk in the chasm
		* f. Parames’s men report strange whoops, hoots, and barks drifting down from higher up in the chasmg. The guards have witnessed some dangerous undead moving around to the west of 3-2. (ghouls)
		* h. dangerous, highly-organized beastmen are encamped to the south: ruthless, disciplined and best avoided. They worship a goddess called Deino (3-158).
		* i. the risky stairs at 3-21 lead to a level above this one.
		* j. the lower halls are creepy and dangerous, not carved by the ibis priests. The stair to Level 5 (3-12) leads to a cave next to a cursed, pillar-ridden hall.

Parames Plumthorn, 4th-level halfling fighter: SZ S; AL NE, AC 2; MV 90’; HD 4; HP 35; #AT 1; Dmg 1-8 (battle axe), 1-6 (short bow). Abilities: STR 16, INT 11; WIS 13; DEX 16, 
CON 11, CHA 15. Special attacks: poison; his axe is coated with “Mortality” poison, which has an onset of 2-8 rounds and inflicts 20 HP damage or half if a save is made. Possessions: chain mail and shield; battle axe; short bow; potion of invulnerability; potion of the berserk (see new magic items) For details see 3-4.

Blandveg, 3rd-level Archontean magic user: SZ M; AL CE; AC 7; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 12; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger). Abilities: STR 8, INT 17, WIS 11, DEX 17, CON 15, CHA 6. Special attacks: 
poison; his dagger is coated with “Mortality” poison, which has an onset of 2-8 rounds and inflicts 20 HP damage or half if a save is made. Possessions: dagger; potion of polymorph self; potion of singing birds (see new magic items); scroll of fireball; a Lexicon of Mithric (see Arden Vul books). Memorized spells: sleep, shield; scare.

#### 3-5a: Halfling Guard Post

* After the halflings drove the goblins out of area 3-6, Parames set up a 4’-tall barrier with firing steps in case his men need to retreat from 3-6. 

### 3-6: Ancient Tomb and Halfling Barracks

* This smoky room is nearly identical to 3-4 and 3-5, with ruined wall images and three plundered sarcophagi.
	* Lit by three candelabra, oozing oily smoke in the center of the room. 
	* Rough, hand-carved tunnels exit in the northwest and southeast corners.
		* The ceiling has caved in slightly in each of these corners.
	* The grimalkin have piled up a low barrier of debris across the entrance to 3-7. 
		* 2 grimalkin are always located at the barrier in the SE corner.
	* All of the non-leader grimalkin sleep in this chamber (in shifts).
		* Seven bedrolls are in the unfinished tunnel in the northwest corner. The other bedrolls are scattered along the western wall.

5 1st-level halfling fighters: SZ S; AL NE; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1; HP: 10, 9, 9, 8, 8, 8; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (spear), 2-7 (club), or 2-5 (sling). Possessions: studded leather armor and shield; spears; clubs; slings; 3-18 sp each.

5 2nd-level halfling thieves: SZ S; AL NE; AC 5; MV 90’; HD 2; HP 11, 10, 9, 9, 8; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6 (short sword), 1-4 (dagger), or 2-5 (sling). Special: the thieves have DEX 17, and the following thief skills: PP 45%, OL 44%, F/RT 30%, MS 36%, HS 35%, HN 15%, CW 71%. Possessions: leather armor; short swords; daggers, slings; 3-18 sp each.

### 3-7: Goblin Outpost, w/ access to 5-44a

* This small chamber is merely an widened area at one end of the 250’ long tunnel connecting 3-6 with 5-44A.  It is unlit.
	* The goblins had begun work on an extension (the spur in 3-6) before the grimalkin arrived and drove them out of the level.
	* Weskenim, the goblin king (SL4-22), has an uneasy detente with Parames and has stationed some warriors at 3-7 behind a barricade.
		* If not alerted by noise or light in 3-6, +1 to surprise the goblins.  Otherwise, they are aware, prepared, and using the barricade for concealment.
		* The goblins do not necessarily want to fight, and are open to negotiation.

6 goblins: SZ S; AL LE; AC 6; MV 60’; HD 1-1; HP 7, 6, 5, 4, 3, 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Possessions: 3-18 sp each.

1 goblin sergeant (as orc): SZ M; AL LE; AC 6; MV 60’; HD 1; HP 7; #AT 1; Dmg 2-8 (morning star). Possessions: morning star; 18 sp and a 100 gp aquamarine.

### 3-8: Robing Room

* Accessed by a flight of steps which descend 15’ to a simple wooden door. 
* This chamber was a robing room for priests serving in one of the three chambers of mystery (3-9, 3-10, 3-11).
	* Inside is a thick layer of trash - bits of leather, ruined clothing, scraps of metal, and a foul-smelling bolus of decaying animal matter.
		* Searching 2 Turns finds a white glass activation square.
* Secret Door (south): easy to detect (1 in 4), opens by sliding a 4’-square panel into the wall.
	* This leads to a narrow hallway of plain rock and a set of rough-hewn stone steps leading upward to 3-67.

### 3-9: Chamber of Painful Knowledge

* A mystery chamber, designed to demonstrate to the faithful that the acquisition of knowledge is difficult and sometimes painful.
	* Dark, but numerous (empty) sconces line the walls.
	* A harmless layer of grey-green mist rises 3’ from the floor throughout the chamber. 
		* Dissipates if the pool in 3-10 is cleansed.
	* Three stone benches face a sunken area, 8’ below the level of the floor (the mist is thus 6’ deep here).  Five steps lead into the sunken area.  At the center is a 15' high onyx pillar.
	* The usual mixture of trash clutters the room, along with almost completely obliterated wall frescoes.
		* High on the western wall,  partly obscured by grime is inscribed (Mithric): Thou May Ask of Thoth What Thou Will, Provided Thou Accept His Judgment.
* Pillar of Truth
	* One can grip the onyx pillar and speaks aloud a question (1 per user per month).
		* The question must involve the past (not the future), and be primarily factual (i.e., nothing like ‘what were so-and-so enemies thinking ...’).
		* Such questions have a 50% chance of being answered, but an electrical jolt deals 1d6 per 2 levels of the asker (1d3 for an odd-numbered levels).

### 3-10: Pool of Youth

* The second of the chambers of mystery of the cult of Thoth, this room was originally designed to impress devotees with the curative powers of the god. 
	* Badly damaged wall frescoes are impossible to make out, except near the ceiling.
	* A continual light spell was cast in the center of the ceiling centuries ago.
	* A harmless grey-green mist rises 3’ above the floor throughout the chamber.
* A 20’-diameter pool rimmed with a 1’-tall, blue-granite lip, not fully obscured by the mist.
	* The liquid is a dark, sludgy brown, and reeks with a foul and disgusting odor.
		* Despite its vile appearance, aroma, and taste, it still holds some magic.  Wading into the pool and drinking from it cures 1d8 HP and has a 50% chance of curing all diseases.
			* Refills 1d6 draughts per week
		* It has been used as a latrine by monsters and by passing Set guardsmen for many decades, affecting its appearance and the efficaciousness.
* Cleansing the Pool
	* It can be cleansed by mixing 3 vials of holy water into the sludge, using a potion of sweet water, or by casting purify water or purify food and drink on it.
	* If the pool is cleansed, it turn back to a deep azure color, and the mist disperses after 1-6 hours.  It heals 3d4 HP and always cures disease (still 1 per weak per user).

13 / 20
1 cubic foot of water = 4 draughts
pool purified!

### 3-11: Pyramid of Venerable Age

* The room is shaped like a huge isosceles triangle. with a 50' ceiling beyond torchlight.
	* It is unlit, although numerous wall sconces await torches. 
	* A layer of harmless grey-green mist rises 3’ from the floor and covers the floor around the pyramid.
		* It dissipates after the pool in 3-10 is cleansed.
	* The chamber is dominated by a massive, 40’-tall triangular pyramid of closely fitted granite with a truncated tip, creating a platform.
		* On all three sides, stairs cut into the granite lead up to a central platform, where the mystery was accomplished.
		* The platform has a triangle of lapis-lazuli at its center.  In 3-11 a steel control rod sticks up from the center.
			* Standing on the lapis triangle and depressing the bar causes a cloud of dense smoke to engulf the pyramid's top, and anyone there is teleported to 2-8.  The smoke disperses in about 15 seconds.
				* Rotating a pair or ornamental Thoth figures on the bar's handle before activating it teleports one into the hidden chamber instead.
	* Frescoes on the walls illustrate Thoth’s conquest of aging and death, with creatures of all sorts - including humans - rising up from the ground and shedding the symbols of age (robes, beards, canes).
* Hidden Chamber
	* The pyramid is hollow (triangular, 20’x20’x30’) and conceals a hidden chamber containing an enormous soapstone heqeti pukel-mander (new items) which rests on the original stone floor of the complex.
		* The priests of Thoth found it here and build around it.
	* A one-way secret door allows return to the main chamber.

#### 3-11a: The Mouth of Thoth

* A magic mouth was placed on the south wall during the Archontean glory days.
	* Approaching within 15’ triggers the mouth, which speaks (secret tongue of the cult of Thoth): “Behold the Glory of Thoth! Mysteries of past, present and future are known to those who speak his name and direct his arms. Knowledge is power!”

#### 3-11b: Set’s Mouth

* Semi-recently, some priests of Set decided to mock the Mouth of Thoth with their own permanent magic mouth.
	* This mouth is also activated by anyone approaching within 15’ of its location, so there is a good chance anyone coming down the western passage from 3-12 activates both simultaneously.
	* The mouth appears sneering and contemptuous, announcing (Archontean): “The followers of the ibis are dead and gone; their power is faded and their secrets lost. Neither power nor knowledge is to be shared with the unworthy. Beware!”

### 3-12: Concealed Door, w/ access to 5-1

* A fresco (6' tall, 4' wide) of a baboon, squatting on the ground and staring forward with bared teeth covers the wall, worn but still recognizable.
	* If covers a secret door (+3 to detect).  Pressing both of the baboon’s eyes will cause the wall to grind inwards, revealing a staircase leading down 250’ to 5-1.

### 3-13: Trashed Chamber

* Holds a larger pile of trash than usual for this level: broken bits of wood, moldy pieces of plaster, several skulls and broken bones, broken pieces of metal, torn strips of cloth. 
	* 33% occupied: (d4) 1-2 giant rants, 3 scared adventurer, 4 giant fire beetles.
	* Lodged inside a skull (3-6 Turns of searching): a sapphire (1,500 gp)

3-12 giant rats: SZ S; AL N(E); AC 7; MV 120’; HD 1-4 HP; HP 4(x3), 3(x3), 2(x3), 1(x3); #At 1; Dmg 1-3. Special attacks: 5% chance of disease.

A scared adventurer (choose from NPC appendix)

2 giant fire beetles: SZ S; AL N; AC 4; MV 120’; HD 1+2; HP 8, 5; #AT 1; Dmg 2-8

### 3-14: False Corridor

* The wooden door from 3-2 leads to a short hallway, with a turn to the left ending in a false, trapped door.
	* Trap (covered pit): 20’ deep (2d6 dmg), triggered by opening the false door.

### 3-15: Thoth the Recorder

* The hallway from 3-2 is lined with frescoes
	* These show Thoth as an implacable ibis-headed scribe recording the virtues and sins of believers.  Around him numerous humans and demi-humans shout requests for mercy and favor.
* The second of the three major statues of Thoth stands in this intersection, atop an 8’-diameter circular pedestal of onyx that mostly blocks the center of the intersection.
	* The statue is an ibis-headed scribe, seated traditional Egyptian pose, using a quill to record the deeds of the dead on a book in his lap.
		* The ibis head, book, and quill are ivory.
		* The left hand holds the book down, while the right holds a quill pen.  The forearms of the statue rotate on stone pins (as in 3-2).
			* Each arm has 3 positions (thus 9 total combinations): down (default position, with hands holding pen and book); pointing straight ahead to the east, and up (above his head).
				* After 1 hour of inactivity, the arms reset to default (down-down) and all pits close.
		* The ibis head has no gemstones in it, merely 2" empty eye-holes (purposely designed to show the unfathomable and limitless nature of knowledge).
			* If staring into the eye-holes, become dazed for 1d4 rounds by the cosmic reach of Thoth’s knowledge.
	* Secret Door (west): opens with a catch concealed in the nostril of a fresco of Thoth; once released, the door slides into the south wall.

Arm Positions: Left Arm Right Arm Effect
* Down Down None (default position)
* Down Straight Opens pit at 3-15A
* Down Up Opens pit at 3-15B
* Straight Down Unlocks mechanism to secret door in 3-2C
* Straight Straight Opens chute at 3-15C
* Straight Up None
	* opens secret door to the west...oops!
* Up Down None
* Up Straight None
* Up Up Simultaneously opens both pits and the chute

#### 3-15a and 3-15b: Pit Trap

* This 10’x10’ by10'-deep spiked pit trap (2d6 dmg) opens when certain combinations of Thoth’s arms are ‘dialed’.

#### 3-15c: Chute

* Anyone standing in front of Thoth the Recorder (3-15) when either straight-straight or up-up is ‘dialed’ is dropped into a chute to 5-2.
	* The chute is a zig-zag tunnel of magically oiled stone.  Despite sliding more than 250’ down, it only deals 3d6 damage when unceremoniously dumped at the end.

## Level 3: 16 - 30

### 3-16: Halls of Thoth’s Beloved

* This darkened hallway is 15’ high, its walls filled with burial niches reserved for favored worshipers of the cult of Thoth.
	* Niches are 5’ long (two niches per 10’ length of hallway) and 3’ high (five niches from floor to ceiling)
		* Each originally had a stone plug on which family names and images of Thoth were painted.
			* All are smashed, except one in the northwest corner (3-16a).
			* A niche in the southern hall hides secret tomb entrance (3-17), 2-in-6 to notice the trash is disturbed.
		* The niches are mostly bereft of valuables.  Takes 8-12 hours to search them all, and each hour there is a 1-in-6 chance of finding something (see table).
	* The floor is littered with bits of masonry, bones, and general pieces of trash (difficult terrain, -10% move silent).
		* Searching finds 1d4 sp per hour (max 200 sp).
	* The halls slope downward noticably;  the western hall is 20' below the eastern hall.
	* A group of giant rats nests in the darkness of the southwest hallway corner.
		* They only attack a party that moves through their nesting area.
			* They leap from niches at head and chest level, getting +1 to surprise.
		* The nest contains: 59 sp, four citrines (50 gp each), a large pearl (500 gp), two aquamarines (100 gp each), a lapis lazuli and gold ring (500 gp), and a cursed blacklight torch (new). 

9-12 giant rats: SZ S; AL N(E); AC 7; MV 120’; HD 1-4 HP; HP 4(x3), 3(x3), 2(x3), 1(x3); #At 1; Dmg 1-3. Special attacks: 5% chance of disease.

##### 3-16a: Burial Niche

* Only one untouched burial niche remains in the Halls of Thoth’s Beloved, 12' up.
* Its plug covered with soot.  Cleaned, it shows...
	* An image of Thoth pointing straight forward with his left hand, while the right hand is at his side (a hint about that statues and opening 3-2a).
	* A symbol of the occupant's family: a black tower with a single window shining forth light into the darkness (still used by Krakteros, one of the Five Families). 
* Breaking the plug requires strength, tools implements, and a way of working while 12' up.
	* Inside is an intact skeleton dressed in disintagrated scraps of linen.
	* The skeleton animates and attack (w/ +1 shortsword)
	* Grave goods: 3 black pearls (360 gp each); jade necklace with the Krakteros sigil (500 gp), short sword +1 (wielded by the skeleton).

1 tough skeleton: SZ M; AL N; AC 7; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 20; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (short sword+1). Special defenses: immune to sleep, charm, hold, and cold; cutting and piercing weapons do half damage; turned as a ghoul.
* +1 shortsword

### 3-17: Hidden Tomb

* 2-in-6 chance when passing this section of the Halls to notice the trash here has been disturbed in a regular pattern.
	* The secret chamber is accessed through a 3’x5’ panel at the rear of the third niche up from the floor (+1 to spot by anyone looking inside the niche)
	* The panel slides easily to the left. 
	* Anyone entering is set on by the ghouls, who have +2 surprise unless the party has listened carefully first.
  * The chamber is an elaborate burial chamber for two of the earliest Thoth worshipers.
	  *  Two basalt sarcophagi with burst lids occupy the center.
		  * Inscribed with scenes of humans worshiping Thoth and of baboons beating crocodiles with sticks. Incredibly heavy (500 lb each) finely carved (2,500 gp each).
	  * Grave goods line the walls
		  * 4 large (4’ high, 50 lb each) alabaster urns (225 gp each)
		  * Two rings (each a ring of friendly defense (white gold) (new), inscribed Ruritanus and Aethelgifu, respectively, command word: ‘Amici’)
		  * 16 ancient gold solidi, 2,316 ancient copper bits, and 1,135 ancient silver pennies.  Two silver torcs, inscribed with ibis head and cornucopia (70 gp each, 280 gp as a pair).
		  * A spear +1 with lapis inlay on the haft
		  * The rest - sacks of food, wooden furniture, and elaborate costumes - have decayed into dust and fragments.
	  * Pristine wall frescoes depict 6 large images, which shine with vibrant color once illuminated.
		  * Ibis-headed Thoth worshipped by orange-robed priests.
			  * Orange robes with cylindrical headdresses indicate Thoth priests.
		  * Humans and baboons beat crocodiles with clubs while a serene ibis watches the scene.
			  * Meant to show the triumph of Thoth (the baboons) over Set (crocodile).
		  * A baboon crouching in the ‘scribe’ position (knees pulled to chest), with a book open on its knees. The left paw of the baboon is raised in greeting. Thoth was associated with Maat, whose image was the white feather.
			  * A clue to the efficacy of the feathers of Maat at 3-19 in repelling the undead of the catacombs (3-22).
		  * A stream of humans bringing goods to the feet of an orange-robed pair of Thoth priests, over whom looms another enormous ibis.
			  * The intention is simple: the devout followers of Thoth should prepare suitable donations to his priests. 
		  * Ibis-headed Thoth walks beside a woman bearing a white feather in her hand; to either side are sarcophagi.
			  * Thoth was associated with Maat, whose image was the white feather. A clue to the efficacy of the feathers of Maat found at 3-19 in repelling the undead of the catacombs (3-22).
		  * Ibis-headed Thoth holds the reins of a chariot in his outstretched left hand. At Thoth’s side is a rayed orb. The chariot travels through the sky, above adoring orange-clad priests.
			  * The Archontean cult of Thoth associated him with bringing the light of knowledge, and saw him as the driver of the solar chariot. A reference to the Litany of Light (see 2-2 through 2-5).

4 ghouls: SZ M; AL CE; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 2; HP 13, 12, 11, 11, 10; #AT 3; Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-6. Special attacks: paralysis. Special defenses: immune to sleep and charm.

### 3-18: Hall of Judges

* This oval chamber served as entry point to the main mortuary areas (at 3-21 and 3-22).
	* Four massive, imposing pillars carved into god statues 30' hold up a domed roof.
		* Each is a god of the dead: NE is Osiris (a bearded human with tall conical cap, holding two scepters across his chest), NW is jackal-headed Anubis holding a heart, SW is Ma'at (bearing a feather), and SE is ibis-headed Thoth holding a book.
	* Light may be glimpsed through the open archway to the north.
	* Frescoes depict the judgment of the dead and the rule of Osiris in the afterlife.

### 3-19: Feathers of Justice

* This chamber is brightly lit from continual light cast on the dais.
* All three walls are painted with brightly colored frescoes.
	* Each  shows a female deity (Maat) with an ostrich feather in her hair handing a feather to a small human worshipper. Other humans bear the feathers before them as they walk into a crypt. In the background is Thoth the recorder.
	* The upper register of each wall shows worshippers beseeching Maat with outstretched hands; the lower registers show demons, monsters and crocodiles.
	* In the center of the chamber is a white marble dais rising 3’ above the floor.  On top of the dais is a solid 10’x5’ onyx table.
		* Suspended in the air above the center of the table is a white ostrich feather.
			* It can easily be grasped; if removed from its place, another feather appears immediately.
			* They repel undead, though only within in the precincts of the temple of Thoth. A feather should be placed in the hair or carried in one’s outstretched hand. 

### 3-20: Antechamber

* Four slim stone columns separate this former guard post from the hallway.
	* An adventurer’s corpse lies in the darkness, undiscovered and unlooted by the grimalkin.
		* Leather armor, 16 gp, 34 sp, 44 cp, potion of invisibility, potion of diminution.

### 3-21: Catacombs Entrance, w/ stairs up to 2-15

* This circular hall is the gateway for entering or leaving Thoth’s catacombs (3-22).
	* In the center of the room is a low dais out of which protrude three iron levers.
		* Each lever controls one portcullis (stiff; 5% per use of breaking).
	* Portcullises: all three are currently down.
		* The portcullises currently prevent the waking dead from infesting the rest of the complex.
	* The four curved sections of wall each feature the same image.
		* Ibis-headed Thoth presenting a scroll to woman carrying an ankh and wearing a headdress shaped like a throne (Isis).  Represents the belief that Thoth conveyed to Isis the secret words allowing resurrection of the dead.
	* Southern hallway:  leads to a long staircase rising 125’ to 2-15.

Southern lever has been broken off open (gate raised).

### 3-22: Catacombs of Thoth

* Lesser, but still honored, devotees of Thoth were buried in this twisting maze of passages.
	* The 15’-high corridors contain eight burial niches per 10’x15’ section of wall; these niches lack plugs and are thus open to the passages.
	* The niches contain bones, the occasional mummified corpse, and bits of lesser grave goods.
		* 1d4+2 Turns of searching exhausts a 10’-wide wall section, top to bottom. Each person-Turn searching gives a difficult (d8) Search check to find something (see table).
	* The walls and floors of the catacombs are remarkably free from dust and general trash (due to the gelatinous cube). 
* The dead in the Catacombs of Thoth do not rest easily.
	* 1d4 Turns after any living creatures have spent time in the Catacombs, and each Turn thereafter, the dead start waking.
		* Roll a type of undead and a distance they arise.
		* The waking of any undead is accompanied by a loud clatter and a thump.
	* Use of a feather of Maat (from 3-19, in hair or carried) prevents that person's presence from rousing the dead, but woken dead will still attack them if they are the best target.
* In the far west, there is a hole up to 3-113 into which the Set cultists sometimes dump garbage.
	* A rope ladder hangs down from the hole, but the bottom part has been dissolved by the cube.
		* Updates: the Setites have laid multiple heavy stone slabs over the hole down to the catacombs.
* A very old gelatinous cube roams these corridors.
	* It begins at "GC", near the garbage hole it frequents.  It is attracted by noise (like combat), and pursues intruders relentlessly.
	* If the portcullises at 3-21 be left ajar, the gelatinous cube should be added to the list of random encounters for Level 3.

* The halflings are aware of the undead in this region, but do not know of the cube. The Set cultists know of both the undead and the cube. The beastmen know of neither.

##### 3-22a: Stairs Down to SL12-20

* The secret door is difficult to detect from the catacombs (d8) side.
	* It is a 3'-square panel located within one of the burial niches.
	* It opens inward from the catacomb side (toward 3-22a) by pushing a 1/2”-diameter rod into a hole in the door.
		* Kerbog Khan’s automatons have such rods as part of their makeup to open the door to return to the workshops.
	* Stairs descend about 200’ before reaching SL12-20.
		* Halfway down the stairs is the corpse of a magic user; his spirit is now a wraith, which lurks on the ceiling.

1 wraith (see text at SL12-20): SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 120’, 240’ flying (Class B); HD 5+3; HP 36; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: energy drain. Special defenses: silver or magic weapons to hit; immune to sleep, charm, hold, cold, poison, and paralysis.

### 3-23: Treasure Hoard

* This complex holds the hidden treasury of the cult of Thoth, undiscovered in the 1,200 years since the collapse of Arden Vul, and the amount of wealth and magic here is prodigious. 
	* When all three cult statues (3-2, 3-15, and 3-40) have their left arm parallel to the ground and right arm down, the statue at 3-2 slides back, revealing stone stairs leading down 20’ to a narrow tunnel. 
	* The tunnel is 5’ wide by 5’ tall and undecorated, at first seeming unimportant.
	* After an hour all three statues revert to their original, ‘start’ positions, and the statue at 3-2 glides back to cover the staircase.
	* An iron lever at the foot of the stairs allows those within the treasure chambers to force all three statues back into ‘open’ position.

##### 3-23a: Antechamber 

* The tunnel from 3-2 ends in a simple door covered with a fresco of an ibis.
	* Opening the door triggers a poison dart (1d3 damage plus save vs degraded poison; a failed save only causes 1d4 hours unconsciousness, awakening with 1 hp). 
* Inside is a guardian of Thoth (new). 

1 guardian of Thoth (see new monsters): SZ M; AL LN; AC 5; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 20; #AT 3; Dmg 1-4/1-4/1-6. Special attacks: shriek. Special defenses: darkness 3/day.
* shriek: 50' radius, mortals save vs transform or disoriented d4 rounds (can't attack or cast, but can flee)
* magical darkness doesn't block darkvision?  doesn't say anything about it in spell

def 15, atk +3

##### 3-23b: Hall of Thoth 

* The walls of this 20’-tall chamber contain a repetitive fresco of a baboon staring straight at the viewer. The floor is literally covered with coins.
	* 200,000 ancient copper bits, 15,000 ancient silver pennies, 5,000 ancient gold solidi. 
	* Among the wealth are 2 cursed pennies (new).
	* The halflings (3-3 to 3-6) will certainly notice attempts to move such a massive quantity of loot. 
* A statue of Thoth in blue marble with an alabaster ibis-head stands in the center of all the coins, brooding, hunched over with chin in both hands.
	* Two jet black gems gleam in the eye-sockets (1000 gp)
		* Impart a curse upon anyone (prier, holder, seller) who possesses them.  They will a) always be surprised in combat; and b) always lose initiative in combat.  it can be removed by a Remove Curse spell cast at 12th level or higher. 
* Secret Doors (northeast): Two of the staring baboon frescoes conceal secret doors which open when the eyes of the baboon are pressed simultaneously.

###  3-24: Secret Treasury 

* Behind the secret doors lie the major treasures of the cult of Thoth. 
	- 3 solid gold statuettes; a cat, an ibis, and a baboon (900 gp, 15 lbs each)
	- A gilt wooden bed, now decayed (75 gp gilding)
	- 6 jade canopic jars (185 gp, 10 lbs each)
	- 8 crystal vases, from 1’ to 5’in height (100-600 gp each, but fragile)
	- 12 death-masks of hammered silver adorned with crystals;, made for the first 12 high priests of Thoth (500 - 2000 gp each to imperial collectors/historians; 1% chance per mask that a demon is trapped in it).
	- 2 Set animal masks taken from their rivals in antiquity (new)
	- Enameled reliquary #1
		- Scenes of the deeds of Arden and Vul, containing a femur said to be that of Arden (fake, but easily sold for 350 gp).
	- Enameled reliquary #2
		- Shows the three mysteries of Thoth (3-9, 3-10, and 3-11) and contains a human hand and some odd dust (dust of dryness). Worth 175 gp.
	- Enameled reliquary #3
		- Showing the three obelisks in the city; a ray emanates from each and the three join at a sunken door. The bottom panel depicts a silver ankh (250 gp).
		- Inside are 2 fully charged rudishva lesser power supplies (new) and 2 silver ankh-keys.
			- A hint to the operation of the obelisks of AV-5, AV-41, and AV-28, which opens the doors at AV-34 to the Chamber of the Beacon (SL14-1).
	- 6 elaborately wrought eggs of platinum, gold, and lapis (1,000 gp each).
		- One is a puzzle-egg; if the puzzle is solved, it opens to reveal a massive black pearl (5,000 gp).
	- 13 potions: extra healing x3; invisibility; invulnerability; growth; treasure finding; super-heroism; elixir of youth; clairaudience; speed; fire breath; watery form (new)
	- harp of charming, of ebony inset with ivory (8’ tall and heavy).
	- gauntlets of ogre power
	- tome of understanding
	- A deluxe, folio copy of the Litany of Light (see areas 2-2 through 2-5; worth 475 gp)
	- A huge codex "The First History of the Order of Thoth in Arden Vul"
	- A parchment codex listing the names of all 239 high priests of Thoth, a few with annotations (250 gp).
	- A treatise "On the Errors of the Sortians"
	- clerical talismans
		- holy name (new), spiritual weapon, remove curse, dispel magic, cure serious wounds, raise dead, neutralize poison, sun’s gift (new)
	- magic user scrolls
		- Frigg’s caustic kisses (new), ray of enfeeblement, blink, fireball, tiny hut, wall of fire, dimension door, stone shape, Pol’s improved eye (new)
	- illusionist scrolls
		- darkness, gaze reflection, improved phantasmal force, ultravision, fear, wraithform, emotion phantasmal killer, maze

### 3-25: Skeletal Baboons

* A former priest’s chamber, with ruined furniture.
	* A wooden cupboard is the only piece to have survived, and only barely.
		* Inside are bits of parchment, including one inscribed as a scroll (sanctuary). 
	* The priest’s two baboon guards have risen as skeletons; they will rush the same character.

2 skeletal baboons: AC 7; MV 120’; HD 2, HP 15, 15; attacks: 1; Damage: 1-6 (bite); 1/2 damage from edged or piercing weapons.

### 3-29: Antechamber

* An antechamber, undisturbed for centuries, with brilliant frescoes of Thoth decorating its walls and a thin layer of dust on the floor.
	* A wooden desk and chair occupy the center and gleam with a gold leaf veneer.
		- They crumble into dust if touched (bits of gold leaf remain, 150 gp, if carefully collected).
	- North door: leads to an undecorated stone passage ending in a one-way stone door into 3-26.

* A thick layer of trash fills this former guard post.
	* Walls of unadorned, but neatly fitted, stonework.

## Level 3: 31 - 45

### 3-31: Empty Guardpost

* A thick layer of trash fills this former guard post.
	* Walls of unadorned, but neatly fitted, stonework.
	* A rotted pouch lies buried under trash in the SE corner (13 sp, 100 gp aquamarine).

### 3-32: Guardpost

* A thick layer of trash fills this former guard post.
	* Walls of unadorned, but neatly fitted, stonework.
	* A thick layer of dust covers the floor, but grimalkin-sized footprints lead north towards 3-34.
	* An elf skeleton staked to the wall in the eastern niche (inanimate), stripped of all possessions, labeled with a plaque of wood (Archontean and Thorcin) "tax dodger".

### 3-33: Floating Head

* A 2’-deep pile of trash completely covers the floor of this small side room.
	* Floating 5' above the junk is a life-sized, bronze bust.
		* It appears as a bearded man of noble mien, with empty eye sockets; his lips are pursed as if in the midst of speech.
		* A Sortian portable sage seized by imperial authorities in the last days of Arden-Vul.  The temple and archonal authorities lacked the command word and couldn't move the head, so it was abandoned here.
			* The command word is on the corpse found in 3-169.
			* Major Fields and sub-fields: Humankind (Archontean politics & genealogy) and Supernatural & Unusual (divination)
	* Underneath the pile of trash is a Thothian teleportation ring (address: YE-BL-GR-RE-BK-WH).  No activation squares are present. 

### 3-34: Scrutiny of Thoth

* The 15'-tall chamber is plastered, and features sixteen large (15’-tall by 5’-wide) images of ibis heads staring at the center of the chamber.
	* A continual light spell was cast here years ago, on a large bronze seal at the center of the ceiling (50 lbs, stoneshaped to hold it in position).
		* The seal is also a scrying amplifier (+1 to sense magic on things sitting on it, +20% to learn sphere and school, +2 to level to overcome target)
	* The sapphire-blue eyes of each ibis are painted such that each pair appears to be staring at the same point (marked X on the map).
		* The four ibis heads on the north wall flanking the door to 3-35 have peep holes about 5’ up (easily identified by anyone examining the fresco). 
	* There is a thick layer of dust, with grimalkin-sized footprints leading south (to 3-32) and west (through the door at 3-30).
* The bronze double-doors to the north are elaborately carved, with ibises, baboons, humans, scrolls, and strange objects.
	* There is a bronze keyhole on the right-most valve; from its size, the key must be very large (8 inches or more) (held by the Set deacon in 3-89a).
	* The doors are locked, and stuck (hard to pick, -10%, and Difficult).

lock picked!

	* The bronze double doors (3-34) on the south wall are locked (the key is in 3-89a).
	* A 2”-thick layer of dust covers the floor.
		* No footprints are evident, even though the recently slain corpse of an adventurer lies against the south wall, and a brazen halberd leans against the north wall.

		* Corpse: a gaudy gold signet ring with “Gregor” inscribed around a smiling face (100 gp), a full flask of water, and a potion of gaseous form.
		* Brazen Halberd: an enchanted weapon known as Set’s Bane (new).
			* Engraved on it is Ma'at's feather and Thoth striking down a crocodile

### 3-36 Tomb of Hithra Paleologos

##### 3-36a: Tomb of Hithra Paleologos: Hidden Vestibule

* At the very tip of the chasm, concealed behind the spiders’ webs (3-37), is a concealed door leading to a narrow passage of simple granite, roughly shaped.
* At the end is a small chamber, devoid of furnishings, with a 7’-diameter hole in the floor.
	* It leads down 25’ to the ancient and deadly tomb of Hithra Paleologos.
	* Scrawled on the wall behind the hole (Mithric) “Danger! Do not Pass!” and more recently (Archontean) “Return with the Fruits of Lord Priscus’s Wisdom before further Exploration.”

##### 3-36b: Tomb of Hithra Paleologos: Tiled and Trapped Entrance

* The hole from 3-36a drops into a cramped triangular chamber sheathed in 1”-square orange and purple tiles.
	* In 18 locations on the walls, the tiles are arranged in patterns of 64 alternating squares (i.e., a chessboard). Many of the tiles are inscribed with runes representing traditional Archontean chess pieces.
		* Each board has a different arrangement of pieces, but on all 18 boards, the pieces are arranged so that an orange High Priest will take a purple Sorcerer and thus enable an orange Legionary to place the purple archon into checkmate.
			* It takes expertise in chess, or a roll of 3d8 under INT to recognize this fact. 
* The door on the west wall (to 3-36c) is 5’-diameter circle made of blue granite.
	* The door is magically barred with hold portal (cast by a 12th-level mage).
		* Any touching it casually receive a jolt of magical force for 1-3 damage.
		* Touches the glyphs in the wrong order deals 1d6 per failed attempt (resetting after an hour).
	* Several inscriptions and images appear on the door.
		* At the top of the circular plug are a pair of orange, heavily-lidded eyes which appear to stare at visitors.
		* Just below the phrase is incised with gold fill into the stone (Mithric): “Hithra the Paleologos Rests Within. Visitors are Unwanted.”
		* Below the inscription are two rows of five glyphs; the top row of glyphs glows with orange light, while the bottom row glows with purple light.
			* The glyphs in each row depict, in order, 
				* a rod of command (Archon = king), 
				* a sinuous winged serpent (Dragon = queen), 
				* a robed figure making a blessing (High Priest = bishop), 
				* a robed figure performing an incantation (Sorcerer = knight), and 
				* Cataphract (rook)
				* a gladius (Legionary = pawn). 
		* The glyphs must be touched in the proper sequence for the door to open: orange High Priest, purple Sorcerer, orange Legionary, purple Archon.

##### 3-36c: Tomb of Hithra Paleologos: Main Tomb

* The star-shaped tomb is brightly lit by a continual light spell; it's walls are white marble and its floor is particolored marble.
	* The central 20’x20’ section of floor resembles a chessboard: 2.5’-square tiles of alternating orange and purple marble.
		* Brightly painted, 3’-tall terracotta game pieces in the Archontean style stand in their home positions on each side of the board.
	* 5’-diameter stone doors occupy the three truncated points of the star.
	* In the center of the board, lying between the two sets of pieces, stands a 6’x4’x4’ stone bier atop which rests a corpse dressed in the orange ceremonial robes of Thoth. The entire area radiates magic, and, from the bier, evil.
		* The corpse is not Hithra Paleologos (who rests in 3-36e), but a skeleton warrior,  Kalifer, bound by Hithra and languishing here for more than a millennium.
* Secret Door (southwest): normal to detect, but opens only when the purple Archon chess piece is destroyed.

Chess Trap
* Each chess piece is beautifully shaped and painted, and is hollow and fairly fragile.
	* Within each is a huge pearl (1,000 gp each, 32 in all) and a quantity of fine powder.
		* Each type of piece has a different powder, and if broken spreads a 10’-radius cloud.
	* Archon (=king, Poison save at +4 or die)
	* Dragon (= queen, Paralysis: save at +2 or be held for 1 turn)
	* High Priest (bishop, Sleep: save at +2)
	* Sorcerer (knight, Confusion: save at +4)
	* Cataphract (=rook, Choking: save at -1 or -3 to all rolls)
	* Legionary (=pawn, Obscuring: save or -1 to all rolls, vision obscured to 10’)
* If any chess piece is moved to another square on the board...
	* A volley of 8 steel darts fire from the ceiling at random squares on the board.
		* Each dart is aimed at a different square, and unerringly hits whatever is there (adventurers for preference over chess pieces).  A dart hitting a piece shatters it.  Hitting a creature, it deals 1d4 damage.
		* The magazine holds 96 darts total (12 volleys of 8).
	* The stone doors to areas 3-36d swing open, releasing their inhabitants.
* Chess pieces may be removed from the board entirely without triggering the trap.
	* Both the inhabitants of 3-36d and Kalifer know of the powders and will certainly take the time to destroy pieces adjacent to them in combat; they may also (50%) elect to spend a combat round specifically destroying 1-3 pieces.

Kalifer
* Kalifer is aware as soon as the chamber is entered, but waits, unmoving, to take the intruder's measure. 
* He desperately and single-mindedly desires the return of the golden circlet with which Hithra bound him, and all his actions are directed towards this end.
* How he reacts depends on what the intruders do:
	* Intruders poke or otherwise disturb his body: Kalifer attacks
	* Intruders activate guardians in areas 3-36d by moving chess pieces to new squares: Kalifer bides his time
	* Intruders take no action within 2 turns, or appear exceptionally cautious and/or intelligent: Kalifer sits up and negotiates with intruders for their assistance in obtaining his circlet
* Kalifer is immune to the powders, so in combat smash open as many pieces as possible.

Kalifer, a skeleton warrior: SZ M; AL N(E); AC 0; MV 60’; HD 9+2; HP 66; #AT 1; Dmg 1-10 (two-handed sword); MR 90%. Special attacks: +3 to hit; cause fear. Special defenses: cannot 
be turned.
* Possessions: Kalifer’s sword (see new magic items); earring of protection +2 (new).

(Possibly): creatures from 3-36D

##### 3-36d: Tomb of Hithra Paleologos: Side Chambers

* The doors to these three triangular chambers are 5’-diameter circular plugs of stone, each locked. 
	* If any chess pieces in 3-36c are moved to a different square on the board, all three doors open and the Archontean animated constructs (chessmen) (new) attack.
		* In combat, the chessmen may (50% per round) destroy 1-3 of the terra cotta pieces instead of striking a living opponent.
	* If the doors are picked open, it reveals three identical chambers of natural stone, each holding a 4’-tall stone chessman (each the High Priest).

3 Archontean animated constructs – chessmen (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 2; MV 60’; HD 6; HP 45, 39, 35; #AT 1; Dmg 4-11; MR 25%. Special defenses: immune to elemental magic, poison, and mind-affecting spells; +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from slashing or piercing weapons. 

##### 3-36e: Tomb of Hithra Paleologos: Secret Tomb and Treasury

* The secret door from 3-36C leads to a small chamber.
	* The body of Hithra Paleologos rests on a 3’-tall stone bier.
		* Next to the body stands an elaborate gold and opal goblet (250 gp), from which Hithra sipped the poison that ended his long life.
		* Hithra wears the orange silk robes of a high priest of Thoth, but instead of his cylindrical headdress of office, he wears a golden circlet inset with huge emeralds (the control circlet for Kalifer the skeleton warrior in 3-36c). 
		* His desiccated left hand bears a large, gaudy, silver poison ring with an immense topaz (650 gp). A secret compartment behind the topaz contains two doses of lethal poison.
		* Hithra’s right hand clutches a rudishva useful palm (size adjustment; new) with 3 charges.
		* Despite what intruders may fear, Hithra’s body remains inanimate.
	* On one side of the bier is a low wooden bookcase, rotted with age.
		* In it rest a dozen notebooks, each labeled “Games and Strategies of Hithra the Paleologos, vol. 1 to 12”.
	* On the other side are 3 heavy and large alabaster jars (500 gp each, 70 lbs).
		* Jar 1: 8,000 ancient silver pennies. Mixed in among them is a silver ankh-key.
		* Jar 2: 4,000 ancient gold solidi, and a dozen rubies (500-6,000 gp each).
		* Jar 3: six potions in a leather carrying case (climbing, heroism, healing, fire resistance, human control, sweet water), a Thothian passkey, a mace +2, a suit of chain mail +2.

Chess Notes
* These volumes contain detailed notes and moves from scores of chess games that Hithra played over a period of 40 years, all of which took place about 1,200 years ago in the period when the city and temples of Arden Vul fell into chaos.
	* He doodles observations of the growing chaos, the Theosophs and Sortians in the margins as he details the much more important games.
* Volume 12 is devoted to games against “Kel Bormol the Overseer, that cheating, untrustworthy snake!.”
	* The last 10 games versus Kel Bormol are all losses, and the final entry includes a few frustrated notes: “He anticipates my every move! He must be cheating! We shall see how he likes a dose of my Useful Palm! I will offer to play him in his chambers above the Great Hall, and will even let him play orange for once. Let him attempt to cheat the Paleologos once more! He shall regret it ….”
	* GM Note: reference to Hithra’s betrayal of his sometime friend, Kel Bormol (SL3-2A).

### 3-37: Spiders from Above

* The northwest point of the Great Chasm (3-38) is the lair of some spiders who have woven a web about about 20’ above the level of the dungeon floor.
	* The nest includes six spiders, five huge and one giant.
	* They roam throughout the chasm and any caves accessible from it; adventurers are likely to encounter only some of the spiders at any given time:
		* d6: 2 huge spiders (1), 3 huge spiders (2), 4 huge spiders (3), 1 giant spider (4), 1 giant spider and 2 huge spiders (5), the whole nest! (6)
	* In webbing: 110 gp in two belt pouches, a white opal worth 200 gp, a potion of frost cage (new), and a scroll with 3 magic user spells (magic missile, sleep, ray of enfeeblement).

5 huge spiders: SZ M; AL N; AC 6; MV 180’; HD 2+2; HP 16, 15, 15, 13, 11; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: surprise 1-5; poison (+1 to saves); can leap up to 30’.

1 giant spider: SZ L; AL CE; AC 4; MV 30’, 120’ in web; HD 4+4; HP 32, 29, 25; #AT 1; Dmg 2-8. Special attacks: poison.

3 huge spiders are dead, 15 and 13 hp ones remain

### 3-38: The Great Chasm

* One of the iconic features of the Halls, this massive fissure extends through most of the dungeon levels.
	* The fissure is generally shaped like a triangular prism, with its apex about 50’ above Level 2. The triangular prism extends downward 1,600’ through the Halls until it levels out at the floor of the chasm (9-1) many hundreds of feet below.
* From Level 3 it requires some careful spelunking to traverse the chasm upwards or downwards; ropes, pitons, and/or fly spells.
	* Lower down the chasm (e.g., 5-34) the prevalence of cave vines, creepers, and lichen mats provides some assistance to such ventures, but at this height plant life is relatively rare. 
* On Level 3 use the Upper Zone encounter table; rolling every 3 turns, 1-in-6 chance of an encounter.

### 3-39: Tomb of Artax-Ris

* The wall of the chasm here is covered with creepers (benign) which conceal the opening to this tomb (detect as concealed).
* The entrance is a circular stone, 10’ in diameter.
	* On it is carved the rudishva glyph for protection, along with some rough letters (Archontean): “Artax-Ris does not wish to be disturbed.”
	* Depressing the protection glyph causes the entire disk of stone will roll to the right, opening the tunnel into the tomb.
		* Touching the glyph with flesh or metal triggers an electric discharge (3d6 damage), 20' radius.  Cloth or other material is safe to use.
		* After 1 hour the disk will grind shut.
* Both the entrance and the tomb are 20’ tall.
	* The entrance hallway and inner chamber are each tiled with 6”-square lapis lazuli tiles, lacking the usual Archontean / Thothian motifs.
	* Each tile has a golden bead in its center, the beads reflect any illumination in an almost blinding way. 
* The 10’-long entrance passageway holds four desiccated skeletons.
	* Two are ancient Thothian priests.
		* 2 silver holy symbols of Thoth (15 gp each).
	* The other two are of more recent adventurers.
		* A suit of scale mail, long sword +1, 35 sp, 45 gp, a potion of healing.
* The entrance hall opens into a 20’x15’ chamber.
	* Some of the lapis tiles on the east wall had their golden beads removed, and a crude inscription is painted across them (Mithric) “Do not disturb Lord Artax-Ris. The Prior forbids it.”
	* Under the inscription is a large stone chair, too big for humans (just right for giant rudishva skeletons).
	* In the middle of the chamber is a strange ‘sarcophagus’ 8’ long and 4’ wide
		* It is made of orange material that is very hard and very shiny (plasteel), with a clear glass (i.e., plasglass) lid.  An unusual clasp holds the lid shut.
		* Within rests Artax-Ris, now a giant rudishva skeleton.
			* It clutches a large two-handed sword; and other goods can be seen inside.
				* 1,122 ancient gold solidi, 3,478 ancient copper bits, a ring of levitation (new), a staff of blue light (new) wrapped in blue silk; two scrolls (wizard lock, slow), boots of springing and striding
			* If the clasp of the sarcophagus is opened, Artax-Ris springs up, ready to defend his meager hoard. He shouts (guttural Rudishva): “Who bothers lord Artax-Ris? Leave now or die!” 
		* The sarcophagus is a rudishva hyperbaric chamber, powered by a greater power supply built into the device.
			* Examination of the underside reveals Rudishva glyphs and an access panel from which the power supply can be removed.

* Development: If ‘awakened’ but not slain, Artax-Ris decides to leave his chamber, using his ring to levitate down to area 5-35.
	* He seeks other rudishva (giant skeletal ones or actual survivors). He may set himself up as a tyrant over the goblins, commandeering area 5-46 from Killik while contemplating how to gather allies so as to reassume his rightful status over the varumani (e.g., at 5-54).
* GM Note: Artax-Ris survived the heqeti attack.  The plague was slowly killing him, but he spurned the elven transformation, instead experimenting with Psalor-Ki (5-74) using the hyperbaric chambers.  Believing he could modulate the effects and save his life (Psalor-Ki vehemently disagreed), he stole a chamber, fled here, and carried out his doomed work.

Artax-Ris, intelligent giant rudishva skeleton: SZ L; AL NE; AC 2; MV 90’; HD 8+8; HP 68; #AT 1 or 2; Dmg 3-18 (weapon) or 2-8/2-8 (bone throwing); MR 50%. Special attacks: bone throwing; sonic blast. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from sharp or edged weapons; half damage from fire; immune to sleep, charm, cold, poison, and paralysis.

### 3-40: Thoth, the Knower of Secrets

* Covered passage (southwest): led to 3-4, filled with rubble, bricked up, and plastered over in antiquity.  Detect as secret door.
* A narrow, 3.5'-wide stone bridge spans the chasm with a slight arch.
	* If fighting on the bridge, roll DEX vs 4 to balance and avoid falling into the chasm.
* The chamber is 30’ tall and unlit, with sconces on the north and east walls.
	* A massive, 15’-tall image carved from solid basalt shows squatting, baboon-headed Thoth (as Aani, who sits on the soul-weighing scales against the feather of Maat).
	* The images on the walls are hermetic, dealing with strange, gnostic principles and magical knowledge.
		* Human forms are largely absent, but moons of all phases, baboons, ibises, pentagrams, circles, and numbers in talismanic sequences are ubiquitous. 
	* The floor is dusty, but clear of trash.
	* Firelight may be visible from 3-4, if the grimalkin still occupy that room.
	* The northwest corner holds a tangle of spider webs.
		* Noise and light in this room may attract the spiders from 3-37.
	* In the northeast corner huddles the crushed skeleton of an adventurer.
		* Dagger, rotted purse (26 pp), rotted backpack w/ spellbook (Cleophalus’s look-away spell (new), comprehend languages, floating disk, jump, read magic, shield).
* There are three normal doors, one north and two east.
	* They are magically held (hold portal 18th-level), openable via the statue of Thoth.
	* They open normally from the opposite side.

Statue of Thoth the Gnostic
* Thoth squats with knees drawn up to chest.  His arms are bent so paws/hands rest on his knees.  Eyes are painted in a life-like manner.
* This is the third of the great statues of Thoth on Level 3 which (along with 3-2 and 3-15), serves reveal the secret tunnel to 3-23.
	* The arms rotate separately from down ("knee", on lap), to forward ("raised", before him), to up ("eyes", covering eyes with back of hand, like See No Evil).
		* The arms both reset to down after 1 hour.

Left Arm Right Arm Effect
* Knee Knee None (default position)
* Knee Raised Opens concealed door to 3-40a
* Knee Eyes Opens door to 3-41
* Raised Knee Helps open secret passage at 3-2c
* Raised Raised Opens concealed door to 3-40b
* Raised Eyes Opens door leading to 3-42
* Eyes Knee Casts continual darkness centered on the statue
* Eyes Raised Opens concealed door to 3-40c
* Eyes Eyes Opens door to hallway, just north of 3-40c

##### 3-40a, 3-40b, 3-40c: Cells of the Guardians

* Each bare cell contains a re-spawning guardian designed to protect the secrets of the tombs of Thoth.
	* Each has a concealed door panel which slides into the ceiling when the proper combination of Thoth’s arms are ‘dialed’ at area 3-40.
	* The image on each door differs
		* 3-40a features a crescent moon shining down on an ibis
		* 3-40B depicts a baboon clubbing a crocodile
		* 3-40C depicts a single blue eye
	* When opened a guardian of Thoth is summoned to that cell and released.
		* If defeated, another can be summoned (in the same fashion) after 1 hour. If a guardian is inactive for 1 hour, it is banished.

3 guardians of Thoth (new): SZ M; AL LN; AC 5; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 22, 20, 18; #AT 3; Dmg 1-4/1-4/1-6. Special attacks: shriek 3/day. Special defenses: darkness 3/day.
* shriek: 50' radius, mortals save vs transform or disoriented d4 rounds (can't attack or cast, but can flee)
* magical darkness doesn't block darkvision?  doesn't say anything about it in spell

def 15, atk +4
