### 3-41: Ancient Tombs

* Three sarcophagi occupy this ornately decorated burial chamber. 
	* The inhabitants were important priests of Thoth, honored with a burial next to the cult image in 3-40.
	* The frescos are largely intact but faded by time. Priests genuflect at the feet of a seated baboon, whose the left arm points forward (a hint to the puzzle at 3-2).
* Opening any sarcophagus lids triggers the sand trap.
	* A hidden catch on the floor near the left-most sarcophagus can disable it.
	* Sand pours from three 5’-diameter holes in the ceiling (marked with Xs) and completely fills the chamber in 6 rounds.
		* Round 1: normal movement
		* Round 2-5: roll 4d6+(rounds-2) under Dex to successfully move.
	* Access to 3-41A via the ceiling holes requires the sand-trap be triggered, and 1-4 hours of sand removal has reopened enough of the room.
* Sarcophagi: each contains an inanimate mummy. Inside each mummy is a piece of elaborate jade jewelry (500-3,000 gp) and a black pearl (325 gp).

##### 3-41a: Tomb of Menas the Logothete, with access to 8-34

* The tomb of Menas lies above chamber 3-41.
	* It is accessible through the 5’-diameter holes in the ceiling of 3-41 once the sand has been drained and 1d4 hours spent clearing it enough to reach the holes.
* Menas’s tomb is 10’ tall and richly decorated with frescoes showing Thoth in all his forms – ibis, baboon, sky-chariot driver, etc, particularly vibrant due to the sand's protection.
	* The largest fresco is centered on the south wall above Menas’s sarcophagus; an enormous ibis streaming rays of energy. Above the fresco are words from the Litany of Light (Mithric) “The Gift of Thoth to the Faithful” (see 2-3 and the Litany of Light in books)).
* Four 2'-tall oval daises daises protrude from the west, north and east walls.
	* Attached to the walls above them are large sheets of slate (2' wide x 6' tall).
* Dominating the tomb is the massive granite sarcophagus of Menas (8’ long, 4’ wide, 4’ tall), also on a 2’-tall oval dais (magically held shut, 18th level).
	* Inscribed on the front (short) end is an image of a Thothian priest in robes and cylindrical headdress, along with the name ‘Menas the Logothete’.
	* Attached to the lid is another sheet of slate.
* A basin attached to the south wall still holds sand (from the trap)
	* At the bottom are several pieces of chalk.
* Door (north): magically held (18th level), unsealing along with the sarcophagus.
	* If approached from 8-34 before the sand is drained, opening the doors causes an avalanche of sand (see 8-34).
	* Leads to an undecorated corridor and a very long stair to the Nether Reaches (8-34).

Opening the Sarcophagus
* One must print the letters of one of two words on the slates in the chamber (one letter per slate), either "LIGHT" or "MAGIC", upon which the sarcophagus lid slides open.
	* One can start and end the word on any combination of slates.
	* These are the gifts provided by Thoth to humans.
* Within, beside the desiccated (and inert) mummy of Menas are his grave goods.
	* 2,345 ancient silver pennies, 459 ancient gold solidi.
	* The legendary thieves’ mask (new).
	* Three books: a libram of silver magic (Thoth's Gift of Silver Magic), a tome of leadership and understanding (Ra's Guidance to Kings), and Bruning of Westholm’s cursed grammar (new, unlabeled).
	* Ten solid gold shabti figurines in unusual stylized dance poses (350 gp each).
	* A scroll with 7 illusionist spells: phantasmal force, wall of fog; brain full of small spiders (see new spells), invisibility, magic mouth; invisibility 10’ radius, spectral force.
	* Two silver ankh-keys (see Arden Vul items).

### 3-42: More Ancient Tombs

* Three sarcophagi occupy this ornately decorated burial chamber. 
	* The inhabitants were important priests of Thoth, honored with a burial next to the cult image in 3-40.
	* The frescos are largely intact but faded by time. Priests genuflect at the feet of a seated baboon, whose the left arm points forward (a hint to the puzzle at 3-2).
* Opening any sarcophagus lids triggers its dart trap.
	* A hidden catch on the west wall across from each sarcophagus disables its trap (1-in-8 to spot the first, then 1-in-4 for the others).
	* Opening a sacrophagus triggers a volley of 6 darts from it's X mark (+5 atk, probably with surprise), each dealing 1d2 damage and save vs Doom against black lotus powder poison (paralysis for 3d4 Turns, or 1d4 rounds on success).
* Sarcophagi: each contains an inanimate mummy. Inside each mummy is a piece of elaborate jade jewelry (50-500 gp) and a garnet (125 gp).

### 3-43: Still More Ancient Tombs

* Three sarcophagi occupy this ornately decorated burial chamber. 
	* The inhabitants were priests of Thoth, honored with a burial next to the cult image in 3-40.
	* The frescos are largely intact but faded by time. Priests genuflect at the feet of an impassive human with a cylindrical headdress whose left arm points forward (a hint to the puzzle at 3-2).
	* The floor is dotted with 3/4”-diameter holes, readily visible.
	* Two adventurer skeletons huddle, multiply pierced, before the western sarcophagus.
		* 2 rusted suits of chain mail, shield +1, two maces, a scroll (magic mouth), purse with 26 ancient silver pennies and a cursed penny (new).
* Opening any sarcophagus lids triggers the spear trap.
	* A hidden catch on the east wall near the right-most sarcophagus can disable it.
	* Iron spears stab up through the floor holes. Anyone in the chamber is struck by 1d3+1 spears (+5 atk, possible surprise) dealing 1d4 damage.  (Spear hits x 5)% chance that their poison is still potent (save vs Doom or die).
* Sarcophagi: each contains an inanimate mummy. Inside each mummy is a piece of elaborate jade jewelry (50-500 gp) and a garnet (125 gp).

### 3-44: Magic Fountain

* In the center of the room is a 5’-diameter and 3’-tall basin, with a crouching marble baboon at its center, pouring clear liquid from his mouth.
	* This circular hall is brightly lit with a continual light spell.
	* The water was protective magic, but has grown more chaotic over the centuries.
		* Each hour, its effect shifts.

D20 Duration Magical Effect
1-3 1 hour Protection from evil
4-5 1 hour Detect magic
6-7 1 hour Protection from evil, 10’ radius
8-9 2 hours Shrink to 50% height
10-11 2 hours Darkvision, per spell
12-13 n.a. Cure 2-16 HP
14-15 Permanent A wasting curse (-1 CON per week until removed)
16-17 1 hour True seeing
18 1 hour Magic resistance (33%)
19 1-4 months Grow donkey ears

### 3-45: Hall of Mysteries

* A balustraded balcony overlooks the Hall of Mysteries.  The hall lies 15’ below and is accessible via a set of stone stairs.
* Along the eastern and western sides of the chamber are giant 15’-tall statues of the old deities standing in classic pose - left foot advancing, hands by their sides, and with traditional symbolic headdresses.
	* East: lion-headed Sekhmet, Set (in Set-Animal form), and jackal-headed Anubis
	* West: Osiris, Horus and Isis.
* On the north wall is a larger (25’-tall) statue of Thoth in his ibis-headed form.
	* One of its 2’-diameter eyes is empty.

* 2 rounds after someone descends the stairs, one of three mysteries will take place (d3).
	* 1 Thoth, the Silver Light
	* 2 Thoth, the Wise Arbiter
	* 3 Thoth, the Source of Magic

Thoth as the Silver Light:
* The statues of Set and Horus advance into the center of the chamber, where Set jabs a spear into Horus’s eye.
* A 2’-diameter, 2”-thick silver disk (representing the moon) rolls out of Horus’s head and clatters to the ground.
* The ritual is completed if the PCs advance, pick up the silver disk, and insert it into the empty eye socket in the statue of Thoth.
	* If accomplished, Thoth emits brilliant silver light curing all diseases and healing all wounds of those within the chamber.
* If not recovered within 1 Turn, the Set Statue crushes the disk under foot, causing an , earsplitting clap of thunder and 2d6 damage to all in the room.
* The eye is restored in 2 days and the mystery can be replayed.
 
Thoth, the Wise Arbiter:
* Osiris and Sekhmet advance and begin to strike each other with their massive stone fists. 
	* Chips of stone fly for several rounds, then Thoth commands (Mithric): “Halt!”
	* The statues stop in mid assault, and Osiris drops his flail to the floor.
	* Thoth intones “One with wisdom must choose!”
		* If someone picks up the flails, the lion-head of Sekhmet comes to life and attacks them (Archontean animated construct).  Their companions are magically held for the length of the combat.
			* If they die, Thoth again shouts “Halt!” and they are revived, but lose 5 HP permanently.  If they prevail, Thoth grants them +3 HP permanently.
	* After Thoth’s judgment, the statues return to their positions.
		* A victor may keep the flail (flail +1) and a new one will appear in Osiris’s hand. If defeated, the flail returns to Osiris’s hand.
	* A person can only receive the blessing once, but the fallen can try again repeatedly.

Thoth, the Source of Magic:
* Set and Isis advance into the room. Isis opens a cavity in her abdomen, and places a small (8”-tall) ebony statuette of Osiris on the floor.  Set shatters Osiris with his axe into 15 pieces. A wall of force seals the chamber.
* Set then coughs forth 3 giant snakes which attack all in the room. Thoth shouts, in Mithric: “Isis must restore him, but only I can revive him!” 
* The statue must be reassembled and re-inserted inside Isis.
	* 2 rounds per piece (30 rounds total). Each assistant reduces the total by 5 rounds (e.g. 3 people take 20 rounds).
	* Every 10 rounds, another giant snake emerges.
	* Once reinstalled inside Isis, a slip of parchment floats from Thoth’s mouth (Mithric) “With knowledge I prevail.”  Reciting it aloud causes Set to retreat, any remaining snakes to crumble to dust, and the wall of force to disappear.
	* The statuette of Osiris turns to solid gold (5,000 gp, 100 lb).
		* Each repetition of the mystery produces a statue one substance more common (silver, 5000 sp, copper 5000 cp, bronze 100 gp, wood 50 gp).

Archontean animated construct - stone Sekhmet lion (see new monsters): SZ L; AL N; AC 2; MV 60’; HD 3-8; HP varies; #AT 3; Dmg 1-6/1-6/1-10; MR 25%. Special defenses: immune to elemental magic, poison, and mind-affecting spells; +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from slashing or piercing weapons. Special: Thoth fixes the lion’s HD at 2 less than its opponent, with a minimum of 3 HD and a maximum of 8 HD.

Many giant poisonous snakes: SZ L; AL N; AC 5; MV 150’; HD 4+2; HP 31, 27, 20; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: poison.

def 15, atk 17, 40' move
X / 20
X / 31
X / 27

## Level 3: 46 - 60

### 3-46: Larel One-Eye

* Relics of the legendary hero Larel One-Eye (see Tales of Larel One-Eye in Arden Vul books) rest in this chamber.
	* Larel is a figure of legend and one of the Worthies of the ancient Archontean empire, whose exploits have been spun into a series of moralizing folk-tales emphasizing the value of wit and good cheer over force. These tales are still told in some form in the Archontean Empire today.
	* Larel is most commonly depicted as a short, pudgy man with ginger hair in a pudding-bowl style, green eyes, and a red eye-patch.
	* His iconic items are his sack, from which he drew myriad useful items, his thin dagger "Larel's Pin", and his humble grey cloak, patched with a variety of colorful patches.
* The chamber is decorated on the north wall with an enormous fresco of Larel wearing a green cap and patched cloak, carrying a sack over his shoulder, with his dagger at his side. 
* The other walls feature scenes from his famous tales:
	* Larel producing a chicken from his sack to distract wolves.
	* Larel using his cloak as a quilt to conceal himself from an angry husband.
	* Larel cleverly spiking four apples on his dagger while distracting the innkeeper with a card trick.
	* Larel absconding from the castle of the wizard Tilgo with the latter’s spell book in his sack.
* Relics of Larel are draped across various racks in the center of the chamber.
	* A cloak rack contains three cloaks: a fine blue wool one (25 gp), a simple black linen cloak, and a ratty patched cloak of many colors (Larel’s cloak, new).
	* A small rack of various weapons, including six fine-but-wicked-looking daggers, 3some curvy, some with gold handles, others bejeweled (110 gp total).
	* A writing desk with a gold apple (35 gp), a plain silver ‘letter opener’ (actually Larel’s Pin, new), and three fairly explicit love notes in Mithric from Larel to three aristocratic women of Archontos (20 gp each to collectors).
	* An unlocked oak chest contains a variety of fine clothing (20 gp), 3 leather belt pouches, a purple silk purse with a gold-thread drawstring (25 gp), and a green stocking cap.
		* Stuffed into the cap is a brown sack (Larel’s sack, new).
	* In the center of the chamber is a stone pedestal, on which is a capped pewter urn filled with ashes - allegedly those of Larel.
* All the "relics" detect as magical.  Larel's true relics don't (except to a 9th level caster or better).
	* If the PCs come away with the true relics, they will undoubtedly draw attention from thieves and others who might wish to possess the relics of Larel.

Larel's Ashen Urn
* If the cap is removed (e.g. to see what’s inside), Larel's invisible spirit manifests.
	* It attempts to possess the one with the greatest combined WIS and CHA (save vs Spells w/ -3). If unsuccessful, it makes one more attempt on the next highest combination of WIS and CHA.
	* If successful, Larel causes the subject to act mischievously, particularly by poking fun at, or humbling, the mighty.
		* If the ashes are desecrated, the spirit maliciously works to cause major bad luck and misfortune.  Otherwise, it causes only minor mischief.
		* Over time Larel’s spirit will cause the possessed to exhibit wanderlust, regular lust, and increasing disregard for all authority.
		* It may be difficult to detect the possession, and only exorcism by a high priest (at a cost of 9,000 gp) will rid the possessed of the spirit.  If exorcised, Larel’s spirit returns to the urn, wherever it happens to be. 

### 3-47: Spiral Stair up to 2-46

* This granite stairway climbs 125’ to 2-46.
	* Numerous cobwebs and an abandoned backpack halfway down the staircase.
		* 10 iron spikes, 3 torches, 2 flasks of oil, an everfull purse (resets to 15 sp, 15 gp every night).

### 3-48: Jaken the Proud

* The tomb of Jaken the Proud, a famous spearman and companion of the heroes Arden and Vul.
	* A series of water-stained frescoes shows scenes from Jaken’s legendary adventures: skewering a giant bipedal salamander, casting a spear at a flying globe of yellow light, riding a beast (unclear due to water damage), holding up Arden’s cloak, drinking a hornful of beverage, etc.
		* Jaken is identifiable by his tall, plumed, conical helmet, his heavy boar-spear, and his scarlet banded mail.
	* Jaken’s tomb is an elaborate marble block.
		* Carved with struggling warriors on all four sides and an image of a supine Jaken is carved on the lid, carrying his helmet and spear.
		* The lid is well balanced, and slides off easily.
		* Inside are:
			* The alleged relics of Jaken the Proud, including his conical helmet, heavy spear and red armor (all extremely shiny and polished, 75 gp)
				* No wear and tear, looks newer than the bones.  Actually a set of ancient copies, made by the priests of Thoth for show in promoting the cult of the great hero.
				* The equipment looks impressive, detects as magic, but is just ornamental and has a 10% cumulative chance of breaking per use.
			* A small (30”x8”x12”) ivory coffer (45 gp) containing an incomplete set of very old, tarnished, and charred set of bones (Jaken's).
				* Detect as magical.  If carried before you, grant Protection from Evil 10’ radius. 
				* May be used to contact Jaken’s spirit: he is bluff and martial, but not stupid.  He speaks only Mithric and knows nothing of the Halls, but is well-versed in ancient history, mythology, and tactics.

### 3-49: Pit of Fire

* A large, 20’-diameter pool (1'-"deep") of fire sits in the center of this 20’-tall room.
	* The walls are covered with flaking plaster painted orange, an effect which magnifies the effect of the fire.
	* The pit is rimmed with a 1’-tall lip of marble.  The fire leaps and crackles to a height of 8’ above it.
		* The top of the lip is inscribed with obscure mystical symbols.
			* Read Mage / Sage: “The fire of Truth cleanses the mind and transports the body of those faithful who proclaim that Thoth Reigns Triumphant!”
	* A large golden key is easily visible in the center of the pit.
	* The fire pit is inhabited by a fire elemental, who can be glimpsed by those who spend several rounds gazing at the fire.
	* Entering the fire deals 3d6 damage and the elemental may freely attack all present.
* If one speaks “Thoth Reigns Triumphant” (any language), they can safely enter the flame.
	* Doing so, the elemental will allow them to take the key and speaks telepathically: “Thoth values your love. Do you wish to be cleansed or to be transported?”
		* Thinking or saying “cleansed”: granted a gift (cure of all damage and removal of all curses and afflictions), permanent +1 Int, or seven tattoo icons appear, each can be triggered for a day of 20% magic resistance).
			* Cleansing can only be gained once, ever.
		* Thinking or saying “transported”: they and those who follow after them are transported immediately to the legendary City of Brass on the plane of fire.
			* May be used repeatedly.
* Secret Door (south): difficult to spot.; opens with the fire pool key; opens inwards.

1 fire elemental: SZ L; AL N; AC 2; MV 120’; HD 12; HP 79; #AT 1; Dmg 3-24. Special attacks: combustion. Special defenses: +2 weapons or better to hit.

### 3-50: Priscian Antechamber 

* The chamber is barrel-vaulted and 15’ tall. Two 3’-tall ledges run across the north and south walls, atop of which stand granite statutes of kilted spearmen.
	* The floor of the passage between the ledges boasts three impressive mosaics, each featuring a blue knot (Sortian knot).
	* The statues are Archontean animated constructs (spearmen; new), which animate whenever a being traverses the passage.
		* Intruders have 1 round to show a Sortian eye (new) of any type or be attacked.
* Occupying the east wall is an 8’-tall carving of a distinguished, late middle-aged male human face with crew cut, trim beard, piercing eyes, wrinkles, a few blemishes, and empty eye sockets.
	* The generic image of the Philosopher, similar to a Sortian face (new), but mundane, not magical.
* Secret Door (north): easy (1 in 4) to locate from this side. It opens by a hidden catch and pushing the door into 3-49.  Not locked from this side.

6 enhanced Archontean animated constructs - spearmen (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 2; MV 60’; HD 8; HP 61, 58, 55, 53, 50, 49; #AT 1; Dmg 5-10; MR 25%. Special defenses: immune to elemental magic, poison, and mind-affecting spells; +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from slashing or piercing weapons. These constructs are slightly more powerful than the run-of-the-mill variety.

##### 3-50a: Stairs Up to AV-19

* This narrow staircase rises 350’ through several landings to the basement of a ruined palace in the city of Arden Vul (AV-19).

##### 3-50b: Stairs Down to 6-49a

* This 5’-wide staircase descends 850’ through multiple landings and switchbacks to 6-49a.
	* The stairs show signs of recent traffic (booted feet). 

### 3-51: Cavern and Monolith

* * An aura of evil hangs over the cavern like a damp mist; it is easily detectable by magic and will be manifested by a sense of prickling skin and of looming, unseen menace.
* This large cave contains a 10’-square monolith which rises 150’ to Level 2 (2-48).
	* Carved of the native granite of the cavern, but with some strange textural features.
	* Touched with bare flesh, the stone feels greasy and appears to leave a filmy residue on the skin that touches it.  This effect is psychosomatic, but lingers for hours.
	* The monolith appears to be polished, lacking the usual grain of natural stone.
	* Strange cursive runes are incised in the monolith in apparently random patterns, filled with a red substance that appears liquid, but is in fact solid.
		* If a rune is touched by anyone who not Chaotic Evil, they take 1d6 damage and the rune brands itself on a visible portion of their body (face, neck, arm, hand).
			* Each brand drains 1 Con / month and cause a -3 to CHA or reaction rolls.
			* Each requires a Remove Curse to remove it.
	* The top of the monolith is a flattened triangle, described at 2-48.
* The cave floor is littered with a scattering of bones, mostly human, but some humanoid and monstrous.
	* Sorting through the bones may turn up something useful:

D12 Object
1-3 a piece of non-magical armor
4-5 a non-magical metal weapon
6-9 a random piece of adventuring gear
10 a gemstone of 5 gp value
11 a scroll case, containing:
	1-2: empty
	3-4: 1 random MU spell
	5-6: map
12 an intact potion of healing

### 3-52: Great Seat of Contemplation

* This 25’-high chamber is extremely old, created by the Rudishva early in their tenure in the middle halls, centuries before the priests of Thoth rediscovered the area.
	* The floor is composed of cracked and buckled 10’-square flagstones (+1x diff terrain, -1 atk)  The walls are undecorated grey granite.
		* Careful investigation notes the flagstones around the chair look newer.  The priests shifted the chair from looking west to the chasm to looking across at their Lesser Chair (3-53).
	* The centerpiece is a giant stone chair (4' seat, 5' wide and deep, 6' back). 
		* The back is draped loosely with an extremely worn piece of leather.
			* The back is incised with a 2' rudishva glyph for guardianship.
		* The seat and arms of the chair are worn by use, and slightly greasy to the touch. 
			* The seat is incised with a 2' rudishva glyph for sight.
		* The glyphs are activated by the touch of living flesh.  Anyone sitting in the seat activates the glyph of sight.  The glyph of guardianship is activated only if the leather drape is removed.
	* Set in the floor behind the chair is an 8’x15’ stela.
		* Inscribed is an imposing biped with small horns on its temples (a rudishva) dressed in a flowing robe, its hands resting on the hilt of a great sword.  At its feet is a sinuous reptile (Kaliyani? Heqeti?).
		* Strange runes line the image (Glyphik) “Grev-Kilj the Far-Seer, Tamer of the Winged Ones, Lord of Air and Earth, Student of Subterranean Life Forms, Slayer of the Hopping-Ones.”

Glyph of Sight: 
* Grants the viewer a viewpoint able to fly through the chasm, perceiving a VR display within their mind (Grev-Kilj and the priests of Thoth used it extensively).
	* Takes time to adapt.  50% chance the user vomits within 3 rounds.
	* Dangerously attractive to human minds.  After 1 Turn of use, save vs Spells to voluntarily leave the seat.  May try again after 6 hours.  Those ensnared feel a great compulsion to return to the seat and use it again.
* A few old rudishva regions of the chasm are cloaked from the sight of the chair, appearing as clouds of roiling darkness.: the Floating Gardens (6-4 and 7-4), area 6-99, and area 9-71. Note that the chair provides perfect vision, as if the chasm was well lit.
* Vision is clear, like 60' darkvision but well lit.  Does not reveal secret doors or hidden passageways.
* A complete scan of the chasm will take many days to accomplish.

Glyph of Guardianship: 
* Activates the rudishva point defense systems defending the rudishva bastion (9-88) for 3 hours before shutting off (probably kills the mimic there?)
* The remains of Grev-Kilj burst forth from beneath the stela and attack those who dare to use his chair.

Grev-Kilj, intelligent giant rudishva skeleton (see new monsters): SZ L; AL NE; AC 2; MV 90’; HD 8+8; HP 68; #AT 1 or 2; Dmg 3-18 (weapon) or 2-8/2-8 (bone throwing); MR 50%. Special attacks: bone throwing; sonic blast. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from sharp or edged weapons; half damage from fire; immune to sleep, charm, cold, poison, and paralysis. 

##### 3-52a: Forgotten Hall, with connections to AV-12 and 5-64

* This hall is only 7’ tall, and contains three sarcophagi.
	* Each sarcophagus bears a crude image of a rudishva carved into its lid and the words (Mithric) “Old One. Do Not Open.”
	* Each is bound with rusted metal bands, preventing it from being opened.
	* Inside each is a giant rudishva skeleton.
		* If they hear noise (any party that isn't trying to be very quiet) they become agitated.  Those outside hear sounds of scraping, clawing, and hammering from inside.
		* Each round, for each sarcophagus, there is a 1-in-10 chance the hammering breaks the rusted bands.  On a 2-4, the bends visibly bend and creak.
* The natural tunnel east climbs 350’ before ending at a crack in the wall of the cellar of the north tower at AV-12. 
* Secret Door (north): opens by pushing a catch hidden beneath the eastern-most sarcophagus. It leads to a long, 5’-wide staircase that descends 250’ to 5-64.

3 semi-intelligent giant rudishva skeletons: SZ L; AL NE; AC 2; MV 90’; HD 8+8; HP 61, 55, 52; #AT 1 or 2; Dmg 3-18 (weapon) or 2-8/2-8 (bone throwing); MR 50%. Special attacks: bone 
throwing; sonic blast. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from sharp or edged weapons; half damage from fire; immune to sleep, charm, cold, poison, and paralysis.

### 3-53: Lesser Seat of Contemplation

* A stone chair proportioned for human beings sits in the center of this chamber, facing out across the chasm towards 3-52.  Its seat bears the Rudishva glyph of sight.
	* It lies on the exact axis of the Great Seat of Contemplation in 3-52 and was built by the priests of Thoth to mimic the effects of the Great Seat without some of the risks. 
	* Touching the glyph grants projected sight, but it is erratic and hazardous (roll d10).
		* 1-4 Immobile vision of a single area (d6) of the chasm lasting 1 turn.
			* 1: Hall of Whispers (2-63)
			* 2: Seat of Contemplation (3-52)
			* 3: Thoth, Knower of Secrets (3-40)
			* 4: Sundered Span (5-35)
			* 5: The Sanctum (5-83)
			* 6: The Troll Lift (6-5)
		* 5 Blindness (permanent)
		* 6 See invisible and hidden, 1 day
		* 7 A horrible vision of a demon; it haunts the PC until curse is removed. 
		* 8-9 see stars for 1-6 days, causing all rolls involving sight to be at -1
		* 10 Hint of a tantalizing vision of a location in the Halls (GM’s choice) that fades to black after a second

### 3-54: Porch

* The narrow passageway from 3-55 leads to a shallow, undecorated porch looking out over the chasm.
	* A pair of iron sconces are attached to the southwestern wall.
	* Listeners will hear moving air and a random chasm sound (see 3-38).
	* Three 50' coils of hemp rope, a hammer, and 20 iron spikes lie on the floor.
		* The rope is quite old (3 in 6) to break when 75 lb supported for >= 4 rounds.
* Light and sound on the porch likely (75%) draws the spiders from 3-55 (arriving in 4 rounds), and an encounter with the spiders may (25%) provoke 2 rolls on the chasm random encounter table (see 3-38).

### 3-55: Stairs Down to 5-76

* This staircase leads down 250’ at a steep angle to 5-76.
	* The stairs are granite blocks, littered with dust and stone chips.
	* About 50’ down the stair is a thick web in which live 4 huge spiders.
		* The stairs under the web are littered with bones, mostly of beastmen. 
		* Among the corpses are 93 sp, 210 cp, and a fine broadsword worth 30 gp.

4 huge spiders: SZ M; AL N; AC 6; MV 180’; HD 2+2; HP 15, 13, 13, 11; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: surprise 1-5; poison (+1 to saves); can leap up to 30’.

def 14, atk 15
X / 15
X / 13
X / 13
X / 11

### 3-56: Secret Doors and Pit Trap

* The passageway is rough undecorated stone, only 6’ tall, and extremely dusty. 
	* Secret Door (west, from 3-65 and 3-53): the catch can be released by sliding a thin object along a 1/8-inch wide opening between the secret door and the floor, releasing it to pivot on a vertical pin.
	* Secret Door, trapped (east): easy to detect (1 in 4), opens by pushing.  If a hidden catch is not enaged, when the door opens, the pit does too.
		* Trap (pit trap): -5% to detect, 30’-deep pit. Lid closes after 1 Turn.
			* Bones of dead adventurers, 2 long swords, 1 mace, 3 short swords, 6 spears (one is a spear +1). A dozen suits of unusable metal and leather,  three usable shields (one is a shield +2). Scattered in various rotting purses and backpacks are 257 gp, 143 sp, 87 cp, two vials of holy water, and a potion of waterbreathing.

### 3-57: Antechamber

* The door from 3-64 is a typical wooden door, but stuck.
* The stone walls are painted a peeling yellow, with 3' high stone benches attached to all the walls.
	* The benches are hinged (not obvious unless examined, detect as secret door), covering storage spaces.  All are empty except the one next to the door.
		* Inside is a bolt of carefully folded yellow silk (100 gp), a bulls-eye lantern, a flask of oil, and an octavo-sized codex marked “Property of Eustachius the Cantor” (books).

##### 3-57a: Trapped Door

* The door is a normal, well-oiled, wooden door that opens out, to the north.
	* The beastman witch doctors cast Probus’s Thunderous Alert (new) across this opening.
		* Anyone crossing the entryway must save vs Spells or a dozen very loud brass horns sound for 10 minutes, alerting the beastmen at 3-160. 

### 3-58: Chapter House

* The Collegiate Chapter of the clergy of Thoth met here to discuss internal business under the leadership of the prior.
* The Chapter House is richly painted, with a sky blue ceiling on which was depicted the constellation of the ibis in gold stars.
* Thirty-nine cherry-wood stalls line the walls; each 5’ tall and 4’ wide, with a 3’-deep seat.
	* The stalls are intricately carved with floral, geometric, and animal patterns.
* On the east wall is a larger seat, 8’ tall, 6’ wide, and 5’ deep, with a wooden canopy; this is the prior’s seat.
	* Secret Door (east): hidden in the back of the prior’s seat, opened by pressing the eye of a carved ibis on the prior’s seat.  A panel on the back of the prior’s seat springs forward, revealing the passageway beyond.
* All of the seats, including the prior, are hinged, covering a storage cavity.
	* Six stalls contain items (2 Turns to search them all).
		* 1: a potion of hill giant strength
		* 2: a leather pouch with 250 ancient silver pennies
		* 3: a potion of poison
		* 4: a quarto volume of erotica entitled The Seventy-Four Ways of Opening the Lotus (books)
		* 5: an orange cylindrical ceremonial headdress made of silk and studded with colored glass (175 gp)
		* 6: a pair (yellow and green) of glass activation squares.
* The center of the chamber contains an oval band of unusual living mosaic 15’ tall by 8’ wide (new).
	* The mosaic's image can be controlled by standing in 3’-square, 6”-deep indentation in the middle of the oval and thinking of the appropriate location (must be known in order to visualize).
	* Currently showing 3-2.
* 25% chance the ghost of Prior Jacobus the Small is present (see 3-59).
	* Because of this, the beastmen avoid this chamber.

### 3-59: Prior’s Study

* This chamber housed the private quarters and study of the prior of Thoth, the second highest ranking officer in the temple (after the high priest).
* The study is decorated with 52 impressive frescoes of previous priors, all dressed in ceremonial robes and cylindrical hats, with empty spaces for 2 more future priors.
	* The last image is an extremely short (4’ 10”), heavy-featured, older man with silver hair and eyes (Jacobus the Small, last prior before the collapse of the temple).
* Furnishing include: 
	* A marble pedestal with a copper bowl (now filled with dust)
	* A cherry-wood desk with one drawer, and a stool.
		* Resting on the desk is a silver letter-opener (15 gp), a bronze ink well (10 sp), a fancy stylus (5 sp), and a gold and opal signet ring (100 gp).
		* On the desk is a sheaf of parchments, mostly mundane financial and personnel matters.
			* One sheet is the plans for the complex at 3-61 to 3-63, marked “Tomb of Jacobus, 52nd Claustral Prior of the Chapter of Thoth”.  They clearly indicate the secret door and the location of the sarcophagus in 3-63.
	* A small cabinet for scrolls.
		* Contains 50 scrolls bound with silk ribbons of mundane administrative and financial records.
			* Rolled up inside one scroll is a sketch map of some areas of Level 3, including areas 3-71, 3-77 to 3-80, and 3-86.
		* A single quire containing one of The Deeds of Phagtro the Westron (books).
	* A small armoire and a camp bed made of carved ebony.
		* The armoire contains two full sets of orange ceremonial robes for the cult of Thoth, complete with cylindrical hats.
			* In one hat is a small key strung with orange silk as a necklace (to the secret door in 3-60).
* The benign ghost of Prior Jacobus haunts the study.
	* If not encountered in 3-58 (25% chance), he will be here, sitting at his desk.
	* Jacobus greets any arrival with delight and relief, rising and gesticulating wildly at himself, his desk, and his surroundings.
		* He cannot audibly communicate with the living.
			* He will try to point to the blueprints on the desk, indicating the tomb.
		* He can move between areas 3-58, 3-59 and 3-60, but nowhere else.
		* Immune to physical attacks, but might be harmed by magic.
		* If angered, he can strangle as does a haunt.
		* His body was never placed in the grand tomb he was preparing (3-61 to 3-63).
		* He will haunt these rooms until his remains (3-61) are placed in the sarcophagus in 3-63.
			* In that event, his ghost appears, bows gratefully, indicates the secret compartment in the sarcophagus, and disappears for good. 

### 3-60: Supply Closet

* This former supply closet has been enthusiastically and systematically plundered, leaving just scraps of parchment and bits of linen and silk.
	* Secret Door (north): difficult to find seam and keyhole (d8) from within the room, obvious from the tunnel.  
	* 5'-tall x 3'-wide, locked (key in 3-59), swings inward toward 3-61. 

## Level 3: 61 - 75

### 3-61: Tombs of the Priors

* This chamber contains the tombs and gisants of all 51 of the priors of the chapter of priests of Thoth.
	* The imposing stone double-doors to the chasm swing open; their locks smashed, preventing them from being secured. 
	* 32 early priors were buried neatly in niches carved into the walls, each 3’ deep with a carved marble gisant of the prior (varying gender, race, size, etc).
		* Only the last 10 of the gisants conceal cavities for bones and grave goods.
			* 1d3+1 Turns of hard work with tools (noisy, attracting encounters, see 3-38) to remove the lid of each gisant.
			* Nine contain only bones and minor jewelry (1d10 x 10 gp). The tenth (the 33rd prior, Yakon), contains a wand of lightning (5 charges).
	* The other 19 priors were entombed in sarcophagi of varying composition and quality set haphazardly on the floor of the chamber.
		* They obscure and, in places, have damaged, some beautiful floor mosaics featuring pastoral scenes.
		* Some are stone, some marble, a few are oak caskets.  There is a gradual simplification in artistic style of the images carved on the tomb lids.
		* All have been opened, their lids lie in and between the sarcophagi, making the room a jumble of concealed spaces and narrow pathways through the clutter.
			* Difficult terrain, -1 atk.
			* Every 2 Turns of searching: 25% of finding coins worth 15 gp (50%) or a gem (50 gp) (50%) (maximum of 350 gp worth).
	* A pack of ghouls led by a wight (the 51st prior) has taken up residence in the hall.
		* They wait several rounds before springing their ambush (25% chance one moans with hungry anticipation, spoiling the surprise).
	* The funeral-shrouded skeleton (short of stature) of Prior Jacobus, the 52nd prior, lies on the floor in front of the secret door to 3-63.
		* The wight attacked Jacobus’s servants as they brought him to his resting place, and they dropped him unceremoniously here.
		* On Jacobus’s corpse: a gold and sapphire torc (950 gp), small iron rod to open the southeast secret door, a small duplicate key to the secret door in 3-60 on an orange silken cord.
	* Secret Door (southeast): narrow and short, leads to a short hallway to 3-60; difficult to spot (1-in-8), opens by sliding a rod into a 1/4”-diameter hole next to the door.
	* Secret Door (northeast): hidden in the back of a burial niche; a rectangle 24” high x 4’ long, opened by sliding the panel upward, revealing the passage to 3-63.

1 wight: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 120’; HD 4+3; HP 28; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4. Special attacks: energy drain. Special defenses: silver or magic needed to hit; immune to sleep, charm, hold, cold, poison, and paralysis.

def 15, atk +5
X / 28

6 ghouls: SZ M; AL CE; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 2; HP 15, 13, 12, 11, 11, 10; #AT 3; Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-6. Special attacks: paralysis. Special defenses: immune to sleep and charm.

def 14, atk +2
X / 11

### 3-62: First Prior

* The first prior of the chapter of Thoth, Kyrus Esgarete, was re-interred in this special extension to 3-61.
* The tomb features a large marble pedestal with a life-sized marble gisant of Kyrus.
	* Gisant and wall-art are defaced by the wight, who has made this tomb his nest.  The whole area stinks of decay and death.

### 3-63: Priors’ Hoard

* The secret panel in the burial niche at 3-61 leads to a short passageway, and from there to a small room crammed with treasures.
	* A marble lid sits beside an empty sarcophagus.
		* Incised with the image of a very short man in Thothian ceremonial robes, with the legend (Mithric), “Iacobus, Prior of Thoth”.
		* If the remains of Jacobus are brought from 3-61, placed in the sarcophagus, and the lid put into place, the ghost of Jacobus (3-59) appears, points to a secret panel on the sarcophagus, and fades into happy oblivion.
		* Secret compartment: 1-in-10 to spot, locked it is locked, contains: ring of free action, belt of hill giant strength.
	* The rest of the chamber is strewn with treasures accumulated by centuries of priors.
		* 6 bolts of expensive silk (500 gp, 10 lbs each); a 3'-tall solid gold statuette of a baboon (750 gp, 15 lb); a magic mace 'Finisher' (new); 16 10-lb bars of silver (25 gp each)
		* 2 disks (28” in diameter) of grooved, beaten gold with 1” holes in their centers (used to open the lesser obsidian gates (SL4-34))
		* The Book of Priors (books); cleric scrolls (command, chant, dispel magic, feline senses (new), knit bones (new))
		* 12 potions: extra healing x2, flying, human control, levitation, longevity, undead control (ghouls), water breathing, oil of slipperiness, philter of persuasiveness, molasses, and truthfulness (last two are new).
		* A trapped wooden chest (poison needle)
			* 6,876 ancient copper bits, 3,397 ancient silver pennies, and 1,349 ancient gold solidi.

### 3-64: Empty Chamber

* Empty and trash-strewn.
	* A bone scroll case is hidden in the trash in the southeast corner.
		* It contains a scroll (phantom armor).

### 3-65: Hall of Remembering

* The chamber has the usual thick dust and trash.
	* The walls are not badly damaged and show a midnight blue with hundreds of small flecks of silver - one per priest of Thoth.
	* On a low dais is a 4’-tall alabaster book stand, on which are some scraps of parchment.
		* Originally it held the Memorial Codex of Thoth (books), with names and dates of death in the priesthood.  It was taken by the beastmen, and is currently in Deino’s chamber (3-158).
	* Two stone doors and a secret door exit from this chamber.
		* The stone doors only open with difficulty (as if stuck).
		* Secret Doors (east): opens only to a Knock spell.
			* The passageway revealed culminates in a blank wall.  It is easy (1-in-4) to spot the secret door to 3-66; opens by sliding the door panel to the left.

##### 3-65a: False Door and Traps

* The ibis-covered wall frescoes of this corridor have been vigorously defaced.
	* Lying along it are some 20 corpses, surrounded by bits of broken adventuring gear.
		* Searching the corpses for 1d3 Turns: longsword +1, a scroll (protection from normal missiles, massmorph, hold monster, reincarnation, clenched fist, volley), gold ring (50 gp), ioun stone (incandescent blue), shield +2; 177 cp, 143 sp, 568 gp, and 97 pp.
	* The door at the north end of the corridor is a false door.
		* Upon opening the false door, the entry door swings shut and has no way to be opened from within the hall.
		* Trapped victims eventually die of thirst or hunger.  Only magic, actual stone mining tools, or someone else opening the outer door can save those trapped within.
			* A patrol of beastmen might investigate and parley surrender or ransom for rescue.

##### 3-65b: Another False Door and Trap

* The plastered walls of this corridor are painted sky-blue with numerous white ibises.
* The door at the north end is a trapped false door.
	* Opening the false door opens four pit traps (20' deep) along the corridor.  The pits’ lids snap closed after 2 rounds.
		* The pit closest to the false door contains a recent corpse (human thief).
			* Leather armor, a short sword, and a 5-lb gold ingot stamped with the imperial insignia (250 gp).
				* Or varumani insignia?

### 3-66: Tomb of the Founder

* This complex houses the tomb of Ptoh-Ristus, cleric of Thoth and one of the companions of Arden and Vul.

The Antechamber
* The 20’-tall antechamber, or eastern ell, is supported by six thick basalt columns.
* Thirty-two 5’x5’ slate flagstones cover its floor, with thin gaps between.
	* (Entry pressure plate) the 10 x 10 area of flagstones north of the secret door leading to 3-65 drop a massive (10 x 10 x10) granite block onto their space.
		* Save vs Doom at -2 or be instantly crushed.  The fallen stone blocks departure.
	* (Wall pressure plates) the eight northernmost and eight southernmost flagstones launch 1d3 darts from the priest eye-holes nearest the triggering space (atk 19 each).
		* Each dart deals 1d3 damage; 1-in-4 darts has still-potent poison (2d6 damage, save for half).
		* A thin blade can slide between flagstones and cut a trigger wire there.
* The walls are painted with images of Thothian priests in orange ceremonial robes and tall cylindrical orange hats, all striding towards the western part of the chamber.
	* The eyes of these priests are black and round; actually holes, rather than painted eyes, if scrutinized.
* Secret Door (antechamber, leading to 3-65): opens by sliding a panel to the right.

The Tomb of Ptoh-Ristus
* West of the antechamber is the tomb proper, with a 40’ ceiling, a floor of large, fitted, marble flagstones (5’ square), and walls painted a pleasing shade of blue.
	* In the center is a 15’x20’ dais supporting Ptoh-Ristus’s enormous, polished basalt sarcophagus (10’x15’). 
		* Bears the inscription (Mithric) “Ptoh-Ristus, Servant of the Lord Thoth, Knower of Secrets and Founder of these Halls”
		* Extremely heavy lid, STR vs 6 to open.
		* Inside is a mummy (inanimate) with a golden deathmask.
			* The death mask of Ptoh-Ristus is a potent magical item (new). 
		* Surrounding it are numerous miniature models representing mundane and magical objects of significance to the great high priest.
			* Made of wood, but enhanced with paint, glass gems, bits of lapis, and gilt (only 20 gp raw value for to lot, more to a collector).
			* Among them is a miniature chair, Theodorus’s chair of great ease (new). 
			* Scattered amongst are 25 ancient silver pennies, 30 ancient gold solidi, and 12 golden beryls worth 1,000 gp each.
	* To the north and south are two smaller 6’ x 4’ white marble ones.
		* A generic, stylized image of a priest is carved on each lid.
		* Each contains the mummy of one of Ptoh-Ristus’s lieutenants.
* The western wall features three colossal painted images.
	* In the center is an orange-robed priest of Thoth (Ptoh-Ristus) looking serenely forward and holding an ankh and codex.
	* To his right is a female warrior (Arden), armored in antique style, looking approvingly at Ptoh-Ristus as she leans on her spear.
	* To the left is a cloaked figure (Vul), pointing three fingers at Ptoh-Ristus.
* On the east wall, flanking the entry to the antechamber (perhaps initially hidden when entering via the antechamber), are 8’-tall stone statues of kilt-clad spearmen.
	* These Archontean animated constructs attack any who enter from the antechamber.
* Secret Door (north): the white sacrophagus must be moved to access the button on the wall that opens the door.

* If any sarcophagus is opened, the mummies of both white sarcophagi shatter their tomb lids from within and attack, as do the stone spearmen, if they haven't already.

2 Archontean animated constructs - spearmen (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 2; MV 60’; HD 6; HP 37, 35; #AT 1; Dmg 5-10; MR 25%. Special defenses: immune to elemental 
magic, poison, and mind-affecting spells; +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from slashing or piercing weapons.

def 18, atk 18
X / 37
X / 35

2 mummies: SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 60’; HD 6+3; HP 44, 41; #AT 1; Dmg 1-12. Special attacks: fear; rotting disease. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from magic weapons; immune to sleep, charm, hold, cold, poison, and paralysis.

##### 3-66a: Treasure Room

* This chamber is undecorated, but stuffed with riches.
	* 6 delicately carved alabaster vases (100 gp, 10 lb each).
	* A plain stone jar filled with fragrant oil (enough for 20 flasks).
	* A wooden chest: 3,333 ancient copper bits, 2,222 ancient silver pennies, and 1,111 ancient gold solidi.
	* A carved ebony box stuffed with incense (100 gp), a 10”-tall solid silver ibis (50 gp), a golden feather (95 gp), 2 platinum rings set with rubies (1,250 gp each).
	* A pair of 3' x 4' prayer rugs (rugs of instant access) (new).
		* Commands "Hither" and "Yon", river imagery
	* An illuminated parchment codex entitled The Founder and His Deeds, detailing the adventures of Ptoh-Ristus, Arden and Vul.
	* Cleric scrolls (hallow, warding chain of glyphs) (both new). 
* Secret Door (east, from 3-66a): easy to spot (1 in 4), open when pushed on its left side (from either side of the door).
	* Trapped with a poison needle (save or die; lose 1d4 Con for 1d4+1 months even on success).
	* Leads to a narrow natural tunnel exiting into the chasm (concealed and very difficult to spot from the chasm itself).
* Secret Door (south): not designed to be opened from this side.

### 3-67: Greater Hall of Columns

* The chamber boasts a 20’ ceiling and 21 stone columns gleaming with hints of yellow gold (shimmering gold paint).

	* Floating in the darkness amid the columns are 6 small chasm cephalopods.
	* Door (west): stuck

### 3-68: Lesser Hall of Columns

* Door (east): stuck

* This large, 15'-high chamber is dominated by 6 squat stone columns.
	* A 1’-deep layer of trash covers the floor, including broken furniture, masonry chunks, bits of statuary, and decrepit equipment.
		* Beastman often sift through the rubbish (50% chance 6 are present); 
	* Scratched onto the base of a pillar, below the layer of trash (Dwarvish): "I found him! Ptoh-Ristus rests some 130’ east and 80’ north. Be wary!" (refers to 3-66).

### 3-69: Vestibule, and Warning Sign

* This former administrative chamber is another mess of rubbish.
	* A waist-high barricade spans the width of the chamber, made of large bits of furniture, entire sarcophagi, and miscellaneous adventuring gear piled up.
		* On the barricade south of the X, a tripwire is pinned along the top of the heap.
			* Touching it sends a rack of spearheads on bent poles whipping around from behind the barricade, dealing 1d8 damage and ringing a number of small bells.
	* A rotting grimalkin head is impaled on a spear, stuck in a crack in the pavement just before the northern door, marked X.

### 3-70: Traps and Beastmen

* Originally a minor administrative office complex for the cult of Thoth. It has been occupied as a forward outpost by some beastmen from Sheep Company (see 3-141).
	* Nervous about their exposed position, they have devised several traps.
	* Parties bypassing 3-70 heading south will be spotted from the peephole in 3-70A.
	* If discovered, the beastmen will negotiate with non-aggressive parties. 
* Door (trapped): opening the door to 3-70 triggers a pair of crossbow traps (d8 damage each).  A tripwire 1' high catches anyone rushing through the doorway (DEX vs 5 or fall prone, d6 damage if running).

##### 3-70a: Beastman Outpost

* Inside are some bedrolls, a small brazier, and several sacks of provisions.
	* The beastmen use the peephole here to spy on those passing by. They shadow any party that passes southward, hoping to engage it from the rear.

4 beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 7, 6, 6, 5; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics.
* Possessions: ring mail and shield; spears; short swords; short bows, 3-18 sp.
* 2 pigs, goat, rat

1 beastman sergeant (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 4; MV 90’: HD 2+2; HP 15; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6 or 2-5. Special attacks: tactics.
* Possessions: ring mail and shield; spear; war hammer, 3-18 sp.
* sheep

##### 3-70b: Beastman Barracks

* The door to this chamber opens outward into the hallway.
	* It is barred from inside, opened when a visitor gives the password.
* A squad of beastmen camps here; bedrolls, a cooking fire, and provisions are scattered throughout.
	* A small keg of decent brandy (30 gp), 30 iron spikes, two 50 coils of rope, boards, nails, hammer.

6 beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 8, 7, 7, 6, 6, 5; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics.
* Possessions: ring mail and shield; spears; short swords; short bows, 3-18 sp.
* goat, 2 pigs, 3 sheep

##### 3-70c: Bait and Switch

* Opening into the hallway, this door is wide open.
	* Visible from the door is a pile of trash, apparently of more recent vintage (barrel fragments, bits of less-rotten wood, sacks, etc.).
	* To one side of the trash pile sits a wooden chest, bait for the hasty.
		* It is locked, but contains only sand.
	* The beastmen in 3-70a and 3-70b hope to lure the incautious into this chamber and lock them in.
		* Should a party enter the chamber, they rush out and slam the door, then hammer two wooden beams across the door and spike the door jamb.
		* They send for reinforcements from Tagma Command (3-150) and hope to negotiate with their captives from an impregnable position.

##### 3-70d: Barred Door

* The door to this chamber opens outward to the hallway and is barred from the outside by pieces of wood hammered across the door.
	* On the door itself is painted the word (Archontean) “Danger”.
	* Snarls, growls and wordless pleadings emerge from within, from the 2 ghouls the beastmen have trapped here.

2 ghouls: SZ M; AL CE; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 2; HP 15, 10; #AT 3; Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-6. Special attacks: paralysis. Special defenses: immune to sleep and charm.

### 3-71: Desecrated Temple of Thoth

* The narrow (5’-wide), undecorated passage from 3-15 opens suddenly into an enormous darkened hall whose walls rise out of the gloom 30’ to a coffer-vaulted ceiling.
	* The cult statue of Thoth commands immediate attention on its pedestal lying in the center of a low pool.
	* Rows of columns lead from the entrance towards that impressive statue, but just over half have been thrown down, leaving the floor covered in dust and stone fragments.
	* Empty iron sconces line the walls at 15’ intervals.
	* Clear tracks through the debris lead towards the door in the southwest corner of the room. 
* Desecration by Set (evil beings gain +1 to all d20 rolls, good ones take -1)
	* The walls are smeared with dirt and feces, and all the gilt has been pulled off.
	* Obscene images and vulgar phrases are scrawled across the walls of the temple.
		* (Archontean): “The Ibis has been Shorn”, “Fuck Thoth!”, “We have ‘known’ Thoth, but there is better flesh to be known in Archontos” and “Where is your power now, Bird-Brain?,” and so forth.
	* An enormous sketch of a crocodile devouring an ibis has been splashed with black paint on the western wall behind Thoth’s statue.
	* Several rotting corpses of goblins, humans, and beastmen have been piled in front of the statue and pool.
	* A fresher pair of human corpses have been stripped of all clothing and pinned to the north wall with iron nails. 
	* Those sensitive to such things feel the aching ‘wrongness’ of the desecration as a damp shroud falling over all who enter. 
* Statue of Thoth: Thoth stands 20' tall, carved of black marble with a white marble ibis head, in the classic semi-advancing pose, arms at his side. He wears a kilt and a headdress with a single feather in it. 
	* Unable to knock over the statue, the Set cultists defaced it.  Bits of dung and streaks of dried blood spatter it; the head of a beastman is impaled on the feather.
	* The eye sockets are gaping holes (the Set cultists pried out the sapphire eyes, which are currently in the Set temple, at 3-90). 
		* If restored, the desecration ends in a blast of white light, cleaning all wounds and granting enough XP to each hero to raise them to their current position in the next level.
* Pool of Faith: The statue is centered in a basin that is 3’ tall and 15’ in diameter.
	* Originally filled with cool clear water, it has been desecrated and now holds a malodorous opaque sludge, within which lurks a slime kraken.
		* If the kraken is defeated, the pool can be purified with a vial of holy water.  It loses its odor and color, and will return to crystal-clear within a week.
		* Drinking from it cures 1d6 HP per draught per day (water can't be removed and retain its effect).  The water level is constant, regardless of consumption.
	* A yellow glass activation square and a Thothian passkey rest in the Pool of Faith.
* The Set cult carved two spy holes 20' up the western wall (3-90b) looking over the empty fane of Thoth.
	* 33% chance Set’s spies notice movement in the temple of Thoth, or 66% if a group engages the slime kraken in extended combat.
	* Even if noticed, they likely just watch, but alert the minions of Set in 3-81 and 3-89 to be ready to repel intruders.
* Secret Doors
	* North and South walls: easy to spot (1 in 4), opened by a catch beside them.
	* Southwest corner: opens by pulling a nearby iron wall sconce.
		* Traffic through the door is regular, but most explorers assume that the tracks lead to the door to 3-77 instead of to the secret door.

1 slime kraken (see new monsters): SZ L; AL N; AC 4 (-3 submerged in basin); MV 120’ swimming; HD 7, HP 49; #AT 7 (6 pseudopods and a beak); Dmg 1-8(x6)/1-12. Special attacks: stunning slime (poison at +2 or stunned +1d3 rounds). Special defenses: slow regeneration (1d6 / Turn).
* 30' tentacle reach, pull stunned target 10' / round, 3d6 under Str to break free (+1d6 per round caught)
* sever tentacle for 1/4 max hp damage

def 16, atk 19
X / 49


### 3-72: Alcoves of the Guardians

* These semi-circular chambers hold only the grime, filth and graffiti found in 3-71.
	* Each alcove originally housed a guardian of Thoth.
	* If the temple is cleansed of its desecration, the magic binding the guardians is restored.
	* Should that occur, they will manifest and emerge to challenge those who approach the statue of Thoth without bearing his holy symbols (attacking if they do not desist).
		* They will manifest and bow to those who cleaned the temple.

2 guardians of Thoth (see new monsters): SZ M; AL LN; AC 5; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 20, 18; #AT 3; Dmg 1-4/1-4/1-6. Special attacks: shriek. Special defenses: darkness 3/day.

### 3-73: North Gallery

* A narrow gallery, 15' above the temple floor, accessed by a door and a ramp, overlooks the grand temple of Thoth.
	* The ramp is decorated with reliefs of servants of Thoth carrying various treasures, codices, and scrolls. These scenes are faded and worn, but not overtly desecrated. 

### 3-74: South Gallery

* A narrow gallery, 15' above the temple floor, accessed by a door and a ramp, overlooks the grand temple of Thoth.
	* The ramp is decorated with reliefs of servants of Thoth carrying various treasures, codices, and scrolls. These scenes are faded and worn, but not overtly desecrated. 
	* Abandoned by long-departed adventurers, on the floor of the gallery are a bulls-eye lantern, three flasks of oil, and a bag of 10 iron spikes.
	* Secret Door (southeast): shaped like a female worshiper bearing an urn; opens by pressing the figure’s left eye.

### 3-75: Antechamber

* The walls of this tiny chamber are painted with a dense silver paint in a textured way such as to resemble scales, creating an effect that makes the walls ripple in torchlight.
	* The door leading to 3-76 is locked, and the key is long gone.
	* A rope ladder, about 15’ in length, is coiled next to the door.

## Level 3: 76 - 90

### 3-76: Arcanum Cave

* This roughly spherical (30' diameter) cave resembles the inside of a geode, with fabulous orange crystal formations growing from every surface, pulsating with a dull orange light. 
	* The door opens into the wall 15’ above the ‘floor’ of the cave. 
	* A secondary cave extends to the southwest; the geode sphere only 10’ in diameter.
		* A hole is bored in its floor (leading to 3-78).
* This cave is a natural pocket of arcanum (new), with the usual compulsions and properties of such. 
	* Casters and inherently magical creatures save vs Spells or feel compelled to linger in the cave for 1d4+1 days, studying and basking in the arcanum's power.  After which they conquer the compulsion and may leave.
		* Each day of extended exposure, roll a random effect.
		* Each day, 1d3 2-lb fist-sized lumps can be carefully extracted.  After 3d4 lumps are removed, the main pocket becomes inert for centuries.

### 3-77: Cave-In

* Both doors to this chamber can be opened, but the room is buried in several tons of rock, earth, and other debris.

### 3-78: Store Room

* This storeroom contains a variety of equipment, all ancient.
	* 4 coils of rope, 3 large carboys of oil (40 flask worth each), a case of wine turned to vinegar, a dozen iron spikes, 4 shovels, 3 pick-axes, a hammer, three 10’ poles, a sheaf of parchment, several bottles of dried ink, 2 lanterns, 10 torches, and an Alexia’s useful pole (new) ‘decorated’ as a candle-holder.
	* If the touched, a magic mouth barks (Mithric) “Touch not the Possessions of Lord Thoth. You have been warned!”
* There is a 4’-wide hole in the eastern ceiling (easy to miss), leading up about 8’ to 3-76.

### 3-79: Ruined Council Chamber

* The sound of wheezy, labored breathing is audible if one listens from either entrance.
* The focal point of the chamber is a stone table 15’ long running north-south.
	* Rotted wooden stools lie on either side.
	* The door to 3-80 has the words (Archontean) “Do not open!” painted on it.
	* Strapped to the table is an undead Thothian priest in tattered orange robes.
		* It wheezes, dead but soul bound to the soul-stone in its mouth, a kind of semi-aware, willness zombie.
		* If the soul stone (new) is removed, he whispers raggedly (Mithric) “Go no further. They are waiting," after which his soul departs.
			* He warns of the zhouls in 3-80 and the wight in 3-86.

### 3-80: Those Who Wait

* The door to this room is stuck.
* Long strips of pale blue paint flake from the walls, and a half-dozen coffers line the walls.
	* Four priests of Thoth were trapped here a millennium ago and have risen as zhouls.
		* They relentlessly attack and follow those who release them.
	* The coffers mostly contain ruined vestments. One holds a few valuables.
		* Orange silk robe of Thoth (35 gp); two silver Sortian eyes (new); a parchment slip with (Mithric) “yellow-blue-green-white-black-red” (the ‘address’ for the Thothian teleport ring at 3-159).

4 zhoul (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 6; MV 120’; HD 4; HP 28, 25, 23, 18; #AT 1; Dmg 3-12; MR 10%. Special defenses: immune to charm, hold, sleep, and cold; turned as ghasts.

### 3-81: Secret Antechamber to Set

* This small room is filled with dusty and broken pieces of trash, with two especially big piles in the northwest and southwest corners.
	* Tracks from the secret door lead to the center of the room and stop. 
* The junk pile to the southwest is a heap of furniture (settee frames, bits of bookcases, side table tops, and numerous table legs), concealing an ordinary door (to 3-89).
	* The Setites have (subtly) nailed it together into a solid mass, resting on a door with wooden runners, allowing it to be dragged or pushed with relative ease.
	* Inside the mass of junk is a dart trap (inspection may spot it through the strategic gaps for the darts to exit.  Jostling / moving the mass without reaching into a crevice (accessible on either side) to set a catch causes it to launch darts.
		* 1d3 darts, atk 17, 1d4 damage
* Door (south): to 3-89, new, freshly oiled hinges, -10% to pick and Difficult; trapped.
	* A trap expels vapor collected from the Breath of Set (4-2a).  Triggered when the door is opened without flipping a switch in the crack at the bottom of the door.
		* All in a 15’ radius must save vs poison or be confused for 2-4 turns.
		* A bell is rung, 50% likely to bring the guardsmen from 3-89 to investigate.
		* The Set priests will reset it within 1-3 days.
* Secret Door (east): easy to spot from this side (1 in 4), opens with a simple catch.

### 3-82: Stuck Door to an Empty Chamber

* The southern door (to 3-71) is spiked shut (by the adventurer in 3-83). 
* The chamber itself has been badly despoiled, the walls stripped of their plaster, which lies in heaps on the floor. 

### 3-83: Lost Adventurer

* The walls of this trash-strewn chamber have been stripped, leaving only patches of plaster.  It smells foul, as if of excrement, sweat, and fear.
	* A lost adventurer lurks here, hoping to escape past the slime kraken (3-71) and the vigilant eyes of the priests of Set.  She is down to her last iron rations and is desperate for assistance.
		* Her party came through the pyramid, then through the secret door in 3-15.  They fought the slime kraken and a party of Set cultists attacked them.  They fled into the 82-85 rooms, where her companions were killed by 2 ghouls, but she finished off the last.  She fears to leave back into the temple, but knows the one-way door goes into the undead-filled catacombs, blocked by a portcullis (they went that way once before, and retreated and reclosed the gate).

Susarra, 2nd-level female Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL NG; AC 4; MV 90’; HD 2; HP 10 (max 18); #AT 1; Dmg 2-9 battle axe) or 1-4 (light crossbow). Abilities: STR 17; INT 12; WIS 12; 
DEX 10; CON 15; CHA 13.
* Possessions: chain mail and medium shield; battle axe; light crossbow with 20 bolts; two torches; two flasks of oil; 45 gp; and a ring of feather falling and a spellbook (taken from her fallen comrades in 3-85): the Bracteros effect (see new spells), change self, gaze reflection, phantasmal force, phantom armor, wall of fog; improved phantasmal force.

### 3-84: Ruined Hall

* This chamber has been thoroughly and enthusiastically looted.
	* In the center, the plaster from the walls lies in a heap, mixed with bits of wooden furniture, clothing, and so forth.
	* Soot blackens the walls, as someone once tried to light all the trash on fire.

### 3-85: Corpses and One-Way Door

* The bodies of two adventurers and two slain ghouls lie moldering here, former companions of Susarra (3-83), a thief and an illusionist. 
	* Thief: short sword, leather armor, silver signet ring (35 gp).
	* Illusionisst: (beneath) a snapped wand and a fine, broken lute (repaired by a master luthier for 150 gp, then worth 350 gp to a bard or collector).
* One-way Door: leads to the catacombs (3-22), closes in 1 Turn unless jammed open.

### 3-86: Wight

* The room is inaccessible and thus exceptionally well preserved.
	* The walls are still decorated with scenes of skiffs moving over dark waters, poled by humans and ibises.
	* Bits of equipment from slain adventurers litter the floor.
		* a sack (solid gold ibis (750 gp), 4 aquamarines (100 gp each), and 239 ancient silver pennies); a fine short sword +1, a potion of human control, a scroll of protection from petrification, and a pair of Thorstein’s oculae (new).
	* The door leading to 3-88 is spiked shut on the side of 3-88. 
	* A wight lurks in this chamber, along with three zombies.

1 wight: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 120’; HD 4+3; HP 27; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4. Special attacks: energy drain. Special defenses: silver or magic needed to hit; immune to sleep, charm, hold, cold, poison, and paralysis.

3 zombies: SZ M; AL N; AC 8; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 13, 11, 10; #AT 1; Dmg 1-8. Special: always strike last.

### 3-87: Stairs Down to SL6-7

* This staircase leads down 550’ to the Drowned Canyon (SL6-7). 

### 3-88: Hidden Room

* A nondescript chamber with flaking pale blue frescoes studded with silvery moons.
	* The bones of a dead mule rest here, complete with a pannier with 2 coils of rope, a lantern, and 6 flasks of oil.
	* The door to 3-86 is spiked shut from this side.
* Secret Door on the south wall of the hallway to the north (to 3-88): difficult to spot (1 in 8) , opens via a keyhole concealed as an ibis’s eye (no key, must be picked?)

### 3-89: Set Guardpost

* The Setites use this old priests’ dormitory and as an advance guardpost for their temple.
	* A 4'-tall wooden barricade with a 2'-wide gate spans the top of the stairs.
		* Anchored to the walls with iron bolts.
	* A troop of guardsmen is posted under the command of Hurub, a deacon of Set.
		* They are alert, and use missiles and oil to impede advance up the stairs.
		* If hard pressed, they will summon aid from 3-93.
	* The walls have been stripped of their former Thothian imagery, replaced with crude images painted on the bare rock of Set surrounded by crocodiles, hippos, and pigs.
	* The chamber contains four wooden bunk beds, a wooden chest, a bucket of water, another bucket for night soil, and a rack of spears.
		* Chest: 150 sp, 4 flasks of oil, a golden statuette of a crocodile (50 gp), 2 aquamarines (100 gp each), and 2 silver holy symbols of Set (in Set animal form, 10 gp each).
	* A linen screen with the sign of Alpha Sept (4-40), a huge black boar, leans on the west wall.
		* It conceals the door to 3-98.
	* The hallway to 3-91 has been roughly cut through the rock in decade past.

6 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 16, 15, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

def 15, atk +2

Following the party's attack:
* The guard has been doubled
