##### 3-89a: Closet

* Hurub the Set deacon sleeps in this chamber.
	* There is a fine bed with sheets, a desk and chair.
	* A locked, iron-bound chest rests against the wall.
		* 159 gp, 2 solid silver goblets (25 gp each), a bronze key (to 3-35), and two potions of extra healing.

### 3-90: Main Temple of Set

* A temple to Set has existed here in one form or another since the founding of Arden Vul.
	* This serves as the primary site for rituals and ceremonies of Set in the upper levels and even for some from outside the dungeon.
* The central axis of the fane runs from the huge bronze double-doors at 3-110 to the altar and cult statue at 3-90A.
	* The ceiling slopes from 20' high at the walls to 50' in the center.  Two rows of eight large stone pillars support the roof.  The floor is clad in blood-red tiles.
	* Beside the bronze doors and on the walls behind the altar are monumental (35’) frescos of sha-headed Set.
	* 20' high heavy black drapes line the north and south walls and the eastern end.
		* They conceal a series of shrines (3-91 to 3-96) and the passage to the spy chamber at 3-90B.
	* Torches on the western and eastern walls light the temple, aided by a pair of sconces set into each pillar.
		* The torches are treated with red lotus blossoms (flora), lending the room a smoky, languidly-sweet aroma.
		* A faint but noticeable breeze gently whirls the smoke west, towards 3-110.
		* A box of 30 doses of dried red lotus blossoms (flora) near the bronze doors.
	* Two 35’-long pools flank the central axis; 15’ feet deep, with lily pads drifting.
		* 4 crocodiles lounge in the pools.
		* 40 aquamarines (100 gp each) are strewn throughout the pools.
		* In the southern pool, at the bottom, is a skeleton.
			* It wears a torc etched “to Nyema” (350 gp).  If returned to Yrtol in EX-4 the torc will melt and put his ghost to rest.
		* In the northern pool, in a leather pouch, are 2 enormous eye-shaped sapphires (10,000 gp each) from the statue of Thoth (3-71).
			* Touching the eyes directly (pouch protects) shocks for 1d4 dmg / round. Thoth will be pleased if they restored to the statue.
	* At the eastern end is a dais, three steps rising 8', topped with a red stone altar, behind which is an enormous statue of Set (3-90a).

Defenses
* 12 guardsmen wait 3-93 and 3-96.
* If not already defeated, the forces at 3-89 and the cultists in 3-90b might be summoned.
* In dire need, a guardsman might release the boars (3-95) and open the grate (3-94) leading to Apophis the lizard (3-112).
* Others will be present, depending on what ceremonies are under way.

Ceremonies (d12)
* If adventurers manage to enter the temple without having alerted the cult of Set to their presence, one of several ceremonies might be taking place:
* 1-6 No ritual
	* No formal ritual, but 2-8 Set cultists and 1-3 Acolytes will be present
* 7-8 Invocation of the Dark (minor)
	* A general ritual to praise Set, culminating in summoning a roiling cloud of magical darkness that sweeps through the temple and out the bronze doors.
	* Involves a Set deacon, 2 Set acolytes and 3-12 Set cultists.
* 9-10 Ritual of the Lesser Beast (minor)
	* The summoning of a large, sacred creature (1-4: crocodile; 5-6: snake; 7-8: armadillo, 9-10: snake; 11-12: wild boar).
	* Involves a Set deacon, a Set acolyte, and 4-16 Set cultists.
* 11 Sacrificial Ritual (major)
	* Gifting a human sacrifice to Set. Victims are taken from dungeons of Set (3-105) or supplied by the Guild of Service (4-11, 4-12 and 4-13) and prepared at 3-97. During the ritual the victim will be screaming in fear and dripping blood from numerous shallow cuts inflicted before the ceremony began.
	* Involves the high priestess, the third priest, a Set deacon, 3 Set acolytes, and 3-12 Set cultists.
* 12 Ritual of the Set Animal (major)
	* A rare ritual to summon a Set animal, performed under only the direst circumstances. Involves the sacrifice of two humans and one acolyte.
	* Involves the high priestess, the second priest, the third priest, 4 Set deacons, 4 Set acolytes, and 1-4 Set cultists.

4 crocodiles: SZ L; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’, 120’ swimming; HD 3; HP 24, 22, 16, 15; #AT 2; Dmg 2-8/1-12. Special attacks: surprise on 1-3.
* A gold ring (75 gp) is in the gullet of the largest crocodile.

1-4 Set acolytes (see new monsters), as 3rd-level Archontean clerics of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 21, 20, 19, 18; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow). 
* Possessions: Set armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (see new magic items); and a silver holy symbol of Set (10 gp). Spells prayed for: command, cure light wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good; hold person, silence 15’ radius.

1-4 Set deacons (see new monsters), as 6th-level Archontean clerics of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 90’; HD 6; HP 44, 42, 39, 36; #AT 1; Dmg 3-8 (mace +1).
* Possessions: Set armor +1 (see Arden Vul items); deacon’s was stick (see new magic items); footman’s mace +1; an amulet of protection against normal missiles (see new magic items); a potion of extra healing; a potion of glibness; a scroll of curse; a gold holy symbol of Set (150 gp); and the key to the chest in 3-89A.
* Spells prayed for: command, cure light wounds (x2), cause fear, protection from good; chant, hold person, know alignment, resist fire, silence 15’ radius; animate dead, dispel magic, cause blindness; cause serious wounds.

The high priestess is Stephania (4-51)
The second priest is Marius Junienos (4-56)
The third priest is Lacedaion of Archontos (4-57)

Up to 16 Set cultists: SZ M; AL LE; AC 9; MV 90’; HD 1; HP 7(x3), 6(x3), 5(x3), 4(x4), 3(x3); #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger) or 2-7 (flail) or 1-6 (staff). Special attacks: fanaticism. Possessions: padded armor; daggers; flails or staves.

1 Set animal (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LE; AC 5; MV 150’; HD 2; HP 13; #AT 2; Dmg 1-4/1-6; MR 25%. Special attacks: venom; jump; confusion; dispel magic 1/day.


Ritual of the Lesser Beast (minor)
* The summoning of a large, sacred creature (1-4: crocodile; 5-6: snake; 7-8: armadillo, 9-10: snake; 11-12: wild boar).
* Involves a Set deacon, a Set acolyte, and 4-16 Set cultists.

##### 3-90a: Altar and Statue

* Carved from a single block of red marble, the main altar pulses with an evil red light.
	* Atop the pulsing slab (6’ long, 3’ wide, 4’ high) is a human-shaped indentation, runnels to drain blood, and copper shackles.
	* On it rest a jagged stone knife with a crocodile-hide hilt (100 gp), a green jade cup for catching blood (100 gp), and two black candles (emit oily black cloud if lit) (10 gp each).
	* The altar radiates evil palpably.
* Behind the altar is a 25’-tall granite statue of Set, in Set animal form (long flat ears, forked tail, long curved snout).
	* He grasps a was stick in his left hand and an ankh in his right.
	* The head is made of ivory, gold, and lapis, with lemon-sized rubies for eyes (5000 gp each).
		* Attempting to remove the eyes brings down a curse (lose 1 CON / month until one shrivels to nothingness).  The curse also afflicts subsequent buyers.
		* The rest of the head may be ripped apart for 1,000 gp.

* Ritual of the Sandstorm Gate
	* On equinoxes and solstices, if a victim is sacrificed before the statue, formally in Set's honor, their blood opens a portal to an ancient, hidden temple of Set on Mithruin.  It appears as a short passageway through darkness, with walls of swirling sand.
	* The discovery of that temple a century ago allowed the cult to enter Arden Vul and begin establishing their hold.  They use it to resupply, communicate, and set members to and from.  Given its importance, only the dedicated faithful know of or use it, or even of that temple (it's not part of the normal operations of the cult).

##### 3-90b: Spy Chamber

* The priests of Set dug this extension of their temple so they could keep an eye on the ruin of their old enemy’s temple.
* The rough stone chamber contains two short wooden benches and peepholes which peer out into 3-71 from 20' up the wall.

2 Set cultists (see new monsters): SZ M; AL LE; AC 9; MV 90’; HD 1; HP 5, 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger) or 2-7 (flail) or 1-6 (staff). Special attacks: fanaticism. Possessions: padded armor; daggers; flails or staves.

## Level 3: 91 - 105

### 3-91: Shrine of Set-Sobek

* Standing at the east end of the room is a stone table on which sits a large statue of a crocodile, with mouth open for the attack.
	* This is Set in his crocodile form (taking over the role of Sobek).
	* Placing any extremity in its mouth causes it to snap down for 2d6 damage and a 50% chance of severing that extremity. 
		* if severed, the crocodile leaks out two large tears, which harden into aquamarines worth 100 gp each.  Six gems can be created this way per month.
* The room is decorated with riverine scenes, showing crocodiles terrorizing boaters, fishermen, and other wildlife.

### 3-92: Shrine of Set the Warrior

* Against the south wall is a shrine devoted to Set the Warrior.
	* On a low pedestal stands a 6’ statue of the god with the head of a Set animal.
	* Arranged around it are bowls with lotus flowers floating in them, and two iron candelabra with lit candles.
	* The other walls show images of Set as a warrior dispatching all manner of enemies, including ibises, falcons, snakes, turtles, and even crocodiles.
* Secret Door (south): if a button on Set's sandal is pressed, the shrine slide away from the wall, revealing a passage behind it.
* If a major ceremony is taking place in the main temple, the shrine is empty.
	* Otherwise 50% chance for 1-2 Set acolytes to be present.

Set acolytes (as 3rd-level Archontean clerics of Set): SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 20, 19; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Possessions: Set armor (new item); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (new); and a silver holy symbol of Set (10 gp).
* Spells prayed for: command, cure light wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good; hold person, silence 15’ radius.

### 3-93: Guardpost

* A section of 4 Set guardsmen lounge behind the curtain, dicing and talking lowly.
	* The walls are painted brightly with desert scenes.
	* They have a barrel of water, a table, and some chairs.

4 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

### 3-94: Shrine of Set-Apep

* At the east end of the room is a stone table atop which writhes a 10' coiled green serpent.
	* It coils, writhes, and hisses in a mechanistic way, animated by magic (can be dispelled)
	* It is made of jade inlaid with carnelian, lapis, and other stones in a beautiful and mesmerizingly realistic fashion (1000 gp but heavy and bulky).
	* If touched without being disabled, it strikes with poisoned fangs (+8 atk, save vs Doom or die).
* Grill: A 4' square iron grill is set in the north wall, providing access to 3-112, and to the giant lizard which roams between 3-94 and 3-111.
	* If the grate was opened by the guards (see 3-90), there is a 25% chance that Apophis the giant lizard (see 3-112) has come to investigate.

Apophis has been animated as a zombie, and is always here, lurking.

### 3-95: Shrine of Set the Knower of Secrets

* Against the north wall is a shrine to Set as diviner of secrets.
	* On a table are several large silver basins glistening with silver liquid (mercury, 2 flasks, 10 gp each), 2 golden candlesticks (50 gp each), and 2 mummified objects, a hand and a small crocodile’s head.
		* The hand is a hand of glory (new).
	* A pathetic and anemic (but still living) ibis hangs in a cage to the right of the table.
* 2 wild boars are chained to the east and west walls.

2 wild boars :SZ M; AL N; AC 7; MV 150’; HD 3+3; HP 24, 20; #AT 1; Dmg 3-12. Special attacks: fights for 2-5 rounds after 0 HP reached, or until -7 HP is reached.

1 Set deacon (see new monsters), as 6th-level Archontean clerics of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 90’; HD 6; HP 39; #AT 1; Dmg 3-8 (mace +1).
* Possessions: Set armor +1 (see Arden Vul items); deacon’s was stick (see new magic items); footman’s mace +1; an amulet of protection against normal missiles (see new magic items); a potion of extra healing; a potion of glibness; a scroll of curse; a gold holy symbol of Set (150 gp); and the key to the chest in 3-89A.
* Spells prayed for: command, cure light wounds (x2), cause fear, protection from good; chant, hold person, know alignment, resist fire, silence 15’ radius; animate dead, dispel magic, cause blindness; cause serious wounds.

### 3-96: Guardpost

A section of 4 Set guardsmen lounge behind the curtain, dicing and talking lowly.
	* The walls are painted in a starry night scene.
	* They have a barrel of water, a table, a side of roast pork, and some chairs.

4 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

### 3-97: Preparation Room

* Sacrificial victims intended for the altar in 3-93 are prepared for their fate here.
	* Centuries of sacrificial preparations here have produced a permanent fear effect (as the spell).  If not holding a was stick, save vs spells or frightened for 4d4 rounds.
	* Shackles line the north wall.
	* A stone table sits in the center of the room, with more shackles and restraints.
	* Implements of torture are neatly arranged on a wooden table by the south wall. 
	* More torture implements rest in the hallway to 3-109.

### 3-98: Stair of Screams

* A dark and ominous stair running two steep flights (down about 50’).
	* It is dimly lit by black ever-burning enchanted candles.
		* If any non-evil person descends the stairs, the candles give off thick black smoke, and blood-curdling screams fill the air.
		* The priests are used to the screams of the tortured, so no one will respond from the temple proper.  50% chance, the guards from 3-99 come to see what new sport is arriving.
			* If combat breaks out on the stairs, 25% chance that Lenuel the Jailer (3-104) joins the fray after 2-5 rounds.
	* Secret Door: halfway down the stairs, on the landing between the two flights, easy to find (1 in 4).  Opens to a key held by Lenuel (3-104).

### 3-99: Guard Chamber

* Kathroc and Hidlat, the two torturers of Set, reside in this brightly-lit, homey chamber, along with their four guardsmen.
	* Two bunkbeds line the south wall, while two beds occupy the north wall.
	* Each torturer has an iron-bound chest at the foot of his bed.
		* Kathroc’s chest: 345 sp, 312 gp, 3 aquamarines (100 gp each).
		* Hidlat’s chest: 756 sp, 213 gp, two 125 gp gems, and his spell book.
			* Spell Book: enlarge, identify, magic missile, push, read magic, shield, sleep, shocking grasp; fool’s gold, mirror image, ray of enfeeblement, scare, strength, wizard lock; flame arrow, tiny hut.
	* A pair of charcoal-fueled tripods, a table with six chairs, a water barrel and box full of foodstuffs.
	* A weapons rack hangs on the east wall, over a table with a large selection of implements (knives, spoons, whips, thongs, etc.).
	* Several impressive specimens of taxidermy line the north and south walls.
		* Heads of a varumani, a lion, a heqeti, and a goblin.
		* A continual light on the lion head lights the room (can cover with a  blanket).
		* The goblin head is enchanted to sing jolly folk and drinking songs when a bit of alcohol is placed in its mouth (100 gp).
* 50% chance that the torturers are busy in one of the torture chambers and have taken 2 guardsmen with them.
* If screams come from the Stair of Screams (3-98), 50% chance that 2 guardsmen poke their heads out to see what is going on.

4 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows, 20 bolts.

Kathroc, 4th-level male Thorcin fighter: SZ M; AL LE; AC 6; MV 60’; HD 4; HP 33; #AT 1; Dmg 3-8 (footman’s flail +1), or 4-7 (Red Welt). Abilities: STR 15, INT 13, WIS 12, DEX 10, 
CON 16, CHA 10.
* Possessions: scale mail; footman’s flail +1; and a bullwhip Red Welt (new)
* Kathroc’s face is round and scarred with welts, some fresh and red and others old and white. He grins almost all the time.

Hidlat, 4th-level male Wiskin magic user: SZ M; AL NE; AC 5; MV 120’; HD 4; HP 14; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (staff +1). Abilities: STR 9, INT 16, WIS 15, DEX 14, CON 13, CHA 10.
* Possessions: staff +1; bracers of defense (AC 5); wand of shielding (17 charges, new).
* Spells: enlarge, magic missile, shocking grasp; mirror image, ray of enfeeblement.
* Hidlat is tall, thin, and dour, with greasy black hair and bad skin.

### 3-100: Disposal

* This small room contains a 5’-diameter hole which drops down 10’ to a (unmapped) 20’-diameter natural cavern.
	* In the lower cavern is a trapped and hungry otyugh, to which the Set jailors toss the bodies of prisoners who die under torture or who are deemed otherwise useless.
	* Among the bones on the floor of the pit are 2 diamonds (850 gp and 1,350 gp) whose owners had swallowed them before capture.

1 otyugh: SZ M; AL N; AC 3; MV 60’; HD 7; HP 44; #AT 3; Dmg 1-8/1-8/2-5. Special attacks: disease. Special defenses: limited telepathy (30’); never surprised.

### 3-101, 3-102, and 3-103: Torture Chambers

* Three torture chambers once served the ancient cult of Set, now only one is operated by the two available torturers.
	* 50% chance a torture session is in progress (with a victim (from 3-105).
	* They usually (80%) use 3-103, but occasionally they vary their routine.
* The three 25’-tall rooms are almost completely identical.
	* Brightly lit with torches and painted a midnight blue.
	* In the center is a large (4’-wide x 4’-tall x 8’-long) stone table with head and limb restraints.
	* One or more braziers with coals, a set of buckets of various diameters filled with water, and a table with more torture implements.
	* Room 3-103 has a smiling jackal head painted on the north wall; the eyes are spyholes leading to 3-106a. 

2 torturers (see 3-99)

2 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; 
MV 60’; HD 2; HP 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

### 3-104: Jailer’s Room

* The jailer Lenuel has taken over this former torture chamber for his dwelling.
	* Midnight blue paint, with stone table (with silk pillows and sheets) and accoutrements.
		* A small locked, trapped iron box under the table (poison needle).
			* Lenuel holds the key.
			* Inside are 155 pp, 127 sp, 4 aquamarines worth 100 gp each, a potion of extra healing, and the spell book of Geleg, a prisoner in 3-105.
				* Spells: charm person, comprehend languages, detect magic, enlarge, friends, Frigg’s flatulence (see new spells), identify, light, read magic, shield, sleep, floating disk; ESP, levitate, mirror image, strength, web, wizard lock; clairaudience, clairvoyance, dispel magic, hold person, monster summoning I.
	* Eadgithu, a human woman is chained to the wall as his personal plaything. 
	* Lenuel is present in his chamber 50% of the time; otherwise he is found at 3-105.

Lenuel the jailer, 5th-level Archontean fighter (50% chance): SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 90’; HD 5; HP 39; #AT 1; Dmg 3-8 (short sword +1). Possessions: short sword +1; chain mail; and boots of the north. Lenuel has STR 17. He also carries a key ring with 10 keys on it, including keys to each of the cells at 3-105, the key to his iron box (see below), and a key to the secret door at 3-98.

Eadgithu, 2nd-level female Thorcin ranger: SZ M; AL CG; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 14 (max 19); #AT 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: STR 17, INT 15, WIS 16, DEX 16, CON 13, CHA 10. 
She gratefully joins any party that helps her escape Arden Vul. She might be willing to permanently join a good-aligned party.

### 3-105: Prisons of Set

* The notorious prison of Set holds interesting prisoners for interrogation, torture, and possible sacrifice in the temple proper.
	* Lesser captives are sold as slaves (4-3) once Set-Sobek (3-91) has no more gems to offer for severed limbs.
* The prison comprises seven 10’x10’ cells enclosed by iron bars, each with its own lock. 
	* The ceiling slopes from 25’ high on the northeast and southeast walls to 12’ high on the western wall.
	* The whole room is well lit by several continual light spells.
	* Against the southeast wall are a table and some chairs.
		* Four guardsmen sit, dice, and taunt the prisoners.
		* There is a 50% chance that Lenuel the jailer is also present (see 3-104).
	* The northeast wall features two obvious observation slits 20’ up the wall (to 3-106).
		* If Set deacons are present in 3-106 (15% chance), various shouts of encouragement and direction can be heard from the observation slits.
		* Deacons will fire spells through the slits if combat breaks out.

4 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 17, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

Lenuel the jailer (50%): for stats see 3-104

Inhabitants of the Cells
* All prisoners are clad only in undergarments; their equipment has been dispersed elsewhere.

* A
	* Lillian, canon of the temple of Mitra in Newmarket (see World of Archontos appendix), as a 4th-level female Archontean cleric: SZ M; AL CG; AC 9; MV 120’; HD 4; HP 8 (max 22); #AT 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: STR 11, INT 15, WIS 17, DEX 15, CON 10, CHA 15.
	* Gagged and unable to pray for spells. She was taken by beastmen outside Arden Vul and sold to the Cult of Set. She has been tortured and is in bad physical shape, although her spirits are still strong. If released, she requests assistance in returning to Newmarket, where a reward of 5,000 gp is waiting.
* B
	* Gribble, a goblin captain (as gnoll): SZ S; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 2; HP; 12; #AT 1; Dmg 2-8, but weaponless at the moment.
	* A brother of King Weskenim (SL4-22), Gribble was taken in ambush on Level 5. He has not been tortured much, as the Set cultists are hoping to trade him back to the goblins for territory and/or information.
* C
	* Empty
* D
	* A fishman (see new monsters), bought from the lizardmen: SZ M; AL CE; AC 5; MV 60’, 150’ swimming; HD 3+1; HP 19; #AT 2 or 1; Dmg 1-3/1-3 or 2-7 (bone club, spear or javelin); MR 10%. Special attacks: paralyzing mucus. Special defenses: immune to cold and poison.
	* The fishman attacks if released.
	* Unbeknownst to jailer, guards, and fishman, this cell contains an ancient escape tunnel hidden under a flagstone (leads down to 4-157).
* E
	* Geleg, 5th-level male Archontean magic user: SZ M; AL NG; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 5; HP 17; #AT: 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: STR 9, INT 18, WIS 15, DEX 10, CON 15, CHA 13.
	* Geleg is an adventurer captured in the Halls. A plump and cheerful fellow, with a fondness for sweets. He has not been tortured ... yet. His spell book is in 3-104. He eagerly joins any good-aligned party.
* F
	* Azgallatu, 4th-level male Archontean cleric of Mitra: SZ M; AL CG; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 4; HP 8 (max 28); #AT 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: STR 16, INT 10, WIS 17, DEX 12, CON 16, CHA 7.
	* Azgallatu is manacled and gagged. A fierce warrior-cleric with a strange blue-tinged scar along the right side of his face. He was imprisoned for insulting a ranking member of the Guild of Service in the Forum of Set (4-2); three of his fellows escaped and are holed up in area 3-214.
* G
	* Grist the Hammer, a 4th-level male dwarven fighter searching for evidence of dwarven activity in Arden Vul: SZ M; AL LN; AC 10; MV 90’; HD 4; HP 5 (max 35); #AT 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: STR 18/55, INT 11, WIS 12, DEX 9, CON 16, CHA 10.
	* Grist is in bad shape. He is suspicious of other races and reluctant to share information. He cautiously joins those who can help him escape Arden Vul. He might accompany such a group for a longer period if his rescuers can prove their power and wealth, or if they have evidence of dwarven activity.

## Level 3: 106 - 120

### 3-106: Observation Chamber

* The small chamber contains three leather-bound easy chairs, some side tables stocked with goblets and wine bottles, and a bench that abuts the southwest wall.
	* A pair of spy holes set in the southwest wall allow observation of activity in 3-105.
		* High level Set priests like to come here and observe the misery of the prisoners, occasionally shouting commands to the guards below, mostly asking them to prod or otherwise discomfit the prisoners.

2-4 Set deacons (see new monsters), as 6th-level Archontean clerics of Set (15% chance): SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 90’; HD 6; HP 42, 39, 36, 33; #AT 1; Dmg 3-8 (mace +1). Possessions: Set armor +1 (see Arden Vul items); deacon’s was stick (see new magic items); footman’s mace +1; an amulet of protection against normal missiles (see new magic items); a potion of

### 3-106a: Observation Window

* This side passage leads to a pair of spy-holes overlooking the torture chamber (3-103).
	* At the end of the passage is a bench and a parchment codex with notes written in it.
		* DM's option: mundane information, grisly torture details, or clues.

### 3-107: Robing Room

* The Set priesthood uses this room for robing and preparing for rituals in the main temple.
	* Brightly lit with continual light.
	* Large frescoes depict Set crushing enemies (ibises, baboons, bipedal amphibians) and receiving tribute from abject specimens of many races.
	* Two racks by the south wall hold ceremonial robes and headdresses.
	* 4 comfortable leather-bound chairs and several tables with metal cups and flagons of wine sit by the east wall.
		* One of the cups is silver (25 gp).
	* Secret Door (south): This door is easy to locate (1 in 4) but may only be opened by fitting a rod-shaped object (staff, spear-butt, etc.) into a small hole in the ceiling. The door leads to the spy tunnels around the prisons of set.

* 50% chance a Set deacon and 2 acolytes are present here, preparing for rituals.

1 Set deacon (see new monsters), as 6th-level Archontean clerics of Set (50% chance): SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 90’; HD 6; HP 42; #AT 1; Dmg 3-8 (mace +1).
* Possessions: Set armor +1 (see Arden Vul items); deacon’s was stick (see new magic items); footman’s mace +1; an amulet of protection against normal missiles (see new magic items); a potion of extra healing; a potion of glibness; a scroll of curse; a gold holy symbol of Set (150 gp); and the key to the chest in 3-89A.
* Spells prayed for: command, cure light wounds (x2), cause fear, protection from good; chant, hold person, know alignment, resist fire, silence 15’ radius; animate dead, dispel magic, cause blindness; cause serious wounds.

2 junior Set acolytes (see new monsters), as 2rd-level Archontean clerics of Set (50%): SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 13, 12; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Possessions: Set armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (see new magic items); and a silver holy symbol of Set (10 gp). Spells prayed for: command, cure light wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good.

### 3-108: Alcove

* This alcove contains a wooden bench and 2 wooden pegs fixed to the wall.
	* On each peg hangs an enchanted Set animal mask (long curved snout, square ears; new), which the priests use to observe torture sessions and the prisoners in (3-105).

### 3-109: Waiting Room

Cultists wait here before being permitted to enter the temple of Set. 

* The walls are plastered, and depict scenes of Set animals preening, receiving worshippers, and being adored.
* A black curtain runs across the back of the room.
	* It obscures the door to the torture chamber (3-97).  Occasionally the priests need to ‘borrow’ a cultist for ceremonial purposes, and this door allows that to happen.
* Wooden benches fill the room, and a barrel of lukewarm water stands by a table along the south wall.
* A variety of cultist (3d10) are always present here, chattering eagerly, under the supervision of a pair of Set acolytes.

2 junior Set acolytes (see new monsters): as 2nd-level Archontean clerics of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 14, 13; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Possessions: Set armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (see new magic items); and a silver holy symbol of Set (10 gp). Spells prayed for: command, cure light wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good.
* Each acolyte has 28 sp and 17 gp.

Set cultists (see new monsters): SZ M; AL LE; AC 9; MV 90’; HD 1; HP 7(x5), 6(x6), 5(x7), 4(x8), 3(x4); #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger) or 2-7 (flail) or 1-6 (staff). Special attacks: fanaticism. 
Possessions: padded armor; daggers; flails or staves.
* Each cultist has 56 sp and 21 gp.

### 3-110: Bronze Doors and Set’s Path

* The 20’-wide stairway-cum-corridor is known as Set’s Path, and leads deeper to 4-1 after 100’ of slow descent.
* The massive bronze doors at the eastern end leading to the Temple of Set (3-90) are normally kept unlocked, unless a major ritual is underway.
	* The keys are kept by the high priestess (4-51).

### 3-111: Cavern Crossroads

* This large, 50' high, c-shaped cavern has a flattened, sandy floor.
	* The atmosphere is cool and wet, and stalactites hang from the ceiling.
	* It serves as a nexus point for several tunnels leading to various areas of the Halls.
		* Clear paths through the dust lead to 3-110, 3-112, 3-114, and 3-115.
	* A section of Set guardsmen led by an acolyte is posted here to watch the passageways, usually lurking on the ledge of the tunnel leading to 3-110.
	* Apophis the lizard (3-112) likes to hunt in this cavern for bats, cave crickets, and other delicacies (50% chance she is encountered here).

6 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 16, 16, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

1 Set acolyte (see new monsters), as a 3rd-level Archontean cleric of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 19; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Possessions: Set 
armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (see new magic items); and a silver holy symbol of Set (10 gp). Spells prayed for: command, cure light 
wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good; hold person, silence 15’ radius.

### 3-112: Lair of Apophis

* Apophis, the giant lizard and revered aspect of Set, makes her lair in this natural cave.
	* Steps have been carved in the tunnel to allow easier access to 3-111.
	* The lizard has created a nest of bones, dirt, straw, and other goodies.
		* Hidden deep in the nest is a ring of truth.
* She is encountered here (1-in-3) or 3-111 (2-in-6).
	* If the grate at 3-94 is open, she goes there to 3-94 to investigate, drink, and/or assault any intruders (1-in-4), is here (1-in-4) or 3-111 (2-in-4).

Apophis, the exceptionally large giant lizard (50% chance): SZ L; AL N; AC 5; MV 150’; HD 5+1; HP 35; #AT 1; Dmg 3-13. Special attacks: double damage on a natural 20.
* She is trained to obey those who wield was sticks.

### 3-113: Ledge and Cave with Hole to 3-22

* A ledge 20’ up the northeast wall of 3-111 leads to a cave filled with stalactites and stalagmites.
* About twenty of the rock formations have been snapped off, and the remains of a campfire and discarded ration-packages litter the floor (garbage left by the Set cultists).
* There is a a 3’-diameter hole in the floor at the far east of the cave, dropping to 3-22.
	* A rope ladder is attached to a large stalagmite next to the hole, hanging down.  The bottom part has been dissolved by the gelatinous cube.
	* Carved crudely onto the stalagmite (Archontean) “Stilicho was here.”
	* The cultists sometimes use this as a garbage disposal, but aren't diligent.

Setites have laid multiple heavy stone slabs over the hole down to the catacombs.

### 3-114: Winding Tunnel with Hole to 5-99

* A steeply descending tunnel with several sections of steps carved into it leading to a small cave with a 5’-wide hole covered by a heavy wooden cover.
	* The hole slopes very gently northwest and leads down 250’ to 5-99.

### 3-115: Tunnel Leading Down to 4-88

* This tunnel snakes down about 100’ until it eventually reaches 4-88.

### 3-116: Hidden Tomb

* 40’ up the southwest wall of the cavern (3-111) is a ledge concealed by a glamor to look as if it were part of the cavern wall.  The cult of Set is ignorant of this tomb.
* The corridor leading to the burial crypt is of roughly finished stone.
	* Faintly decorated with geometric images, mixed with primitive sketches of warriors and salamander-like amphibians (heqeti).
* The walls and ceiling of the crypt itself are also rough-carved.
	* In the center, under a carpet of dust, is a 10’-long stone sarcophagus.  Atop it sits a thick tallow candle mounted on a heqeti skull.
		* The lid is intact and bears the faint polychromed image of a man with a ram-horn helmet holding a massive two-handed sword.
		* If the lid is disturbed, Tuolicha the mummy rises to repel the desecrators.
		* Inside: a two-handed sword +1, +3 vs heqeti; 450 ancient gold solidi; 3 potions (healing, invisibility, levitation); a silver circlet set with jade (750 gp), the key to the secret door, and a treasure map showing a route from 3-1 to the tomb of Sethu (5-57 to 5-60).
	* Secret Door (southeast): easy to locate (1 in 4 chance); a key in the mummy’s sarchophagus fits a small hole in the rock, unlocking the door.

Tuolicha, a mummy: SZ M; AL LE; AC 2; MV 60’; HD 6+3; HP 41; #AT 1; Dmg 1-12. Special attacks: fear; rotting disease. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from magic weapons; immune to sleep, charm, hold, cold, poison, paralysis. 
* Possessions: torc of protection (new).

### 3-117: Dripping Chamber, with Well to 5-104

* The corridor from 3-116 is narrow, low, cramped (5’x5’x5’), and completely undecorated.
	* It ends at a square stone door with a simple wooden latch.
* The chamber is sheathed in white marble squares (5’ square) on all walls, floor and ceiling.
	* Each square of marble has a symbol incised in its center and filled with gold inlay.
		* Symbol: an open, toothless mouth, from which extends a thick tongue.
		* All the tiles are slick with dripping moisture; the moisture beads on each incised tongue, dripping off or down, eventually collecting in the basin.
	* The floor is slightly convex, dipping towards a 10’-diameter basin in the middle of the floor.
		* The chamber is quite slippery (+1x difficult terrain, 3d6 under Dex or fall is moving quickly.
		* Anyone slipping may slide down to the basin, affected by multiple doses of sweat of Rimmaq-Isfet (new) for 5-20 damage. 
		* The liquid is clear and slightly more viscous than water.
			* It is an extrusion of Rimmaq-Isfet known to sages as the sweat of Rimmaq-Isfet (new).
			* There are 10 flasks worth, and it replenishes 1 flask per day. 
	* Brightly lit by no visible light source.
	* At the east end is a 5’-diameter well extending 200’ down to 5-104.
		* Small handholds have been chiseled into the stone well.

### 3-118: Oracle of Thoth

* Passing through the central mouth in 2-70 leads PCs to a long and steep stairway that descends in a series of twists for some 150’.
	* The stairwell is narrow (5’ wide), roughly carved, and unadorned.
	* It ends at a small landing (10’x10’x10’), with light visible through a 4’x4’ hole in the ceiling.
	* The hole leads to the legendary Oracle of Thoth.

* The Oracle chamber lies beneath a shallow dome 25’ high in its center; brightly lit by a continual light spell.
	* The walls curve inward immediately, making the ceiling quite low along the edge.
	* The ceiling is painted with a bright yellow paint that glitters and sparkles in the light.

* A 10’x10’ dais lies in the center of the chamber.
	* Once shrouded by hanging curtains.  They have long since rotted, leaving sagging iron curtain rods in a square around it.
	* On the dais is a large and unusual statue of an ibis, wings cocked to enclose a marble seat just in front of the ibis’s body.
		* The seat is arranged such that any sitting in it are enfolded by the ibis’s wings, their head shadowed by the ibis’s beak.
		* The ibis statue is impressive: marble, lapis, and jet cleverly worked together to produce an effect of verisimilitude.
			* The head is pure white marble, carved to resemble a real bird - save with empty and vacant holes for eyes.
			* Though the statue is clearly stone, the marble may be seen to gently rise and fall, as if the bird were actually breathing.
		* The plinth on which the statue sits is inscribed (Thothian tongue): “Sit, Ask, and Receive. Lord Thoth Knows All.”
		* Currently a human figure is writhing in the chair, surrounded by the wings of the ibis.
			* This is Anaximander, an Archontean sage. 

Anaximander
* Arriving here 250 years ago with Adrienic’s expedition (see 5-18), Anaximander sought to trick the Oracle into providing more than its customary delphic pronouncements. He has been condemned ever since to trade riddles with an Aspect of Thoth, while his life was preserved (barely) by the magical breath of Thoth.
* Anaximander’s body is wasted and thin, and his beard and hair are now long, stringy and white. He mutters nonsense words under his breath as he thrashes about.
* Only if he is physically pulled from the Oracle will he leave its embrace.  He then faces life as an extremely old, frail, and insane person, whose ravings may well be taken as oracular themselves. He will not be able to convey much of interest to adventurers, and if pressed will merely babble in Archontean “My hubris was my downfall. Hubris! Pride! Alas. The voice .... I could not withstand His voice ....” He speaks thereafter in crude doggerel and only responds to questions with riddles or with what may actually be the answers to unknown riddles.

Consulting the Oracle
* Once Anaximander is gone, anyone may consult the Oracle by sitting in the chair.  A postulant is immediately enveloped by a warm secure layer of air, and *feels* a low voice state “Speak Thy Query” in his/her mind.
	* Speaking or thinking a question results in several seconds of psychic turmoil culminating in the postulant losing conscious control of his or her brain.
	* Bystanders hear a deep, alien voice boom forth from the lips of the postulant as the oracle is declaimed. The postulant must succeed at a roll of 4d6 under INT to recall what Thoth said through him or her.
* What is said by the Oracle is delphic, that is, obscure and in need of interpretation; in no way does it provide a straight factual answer.
	* The Oracle can and will predict future events as well as specific, current questions of fact; the degree of opacity of its answer is inversely related to both the specificity of a question or the temporal distance of a prediction.  More specific factual questions and more distant predictions will elicit more opaque responses.
		* For instance, if a postulant asks/thinks, “Will I die in the Halls of Arden Vul”, the Oracle might reply in fairly specific ways, such as “Thy fate is linked to the month of the Crab and the acquisition of the iron circlet of Ghanor; Thou shall not fear under such signs” [a very specific response].
		* If a postulant were to ask, “Where is the iron circlet of Ghanor?”, the response might be “Resisting the Breath of the Feeble will lay bare the Path” [a reference to 3-127A].
		* And if a postulant were to ask, “Will I become a king?” the response would be true, but vague, along the lines of “Thou shall reign over time and mortals in the capacity that Thou desires.”

Effects of an Oracular Pronouncement:
* In addition to the Oracle’s pronouncement, Thoth’s voice stuns listeners for 1-4 rounds (save vs petrification to resist) and reduces the WIS of the postulant by 2-6 for 1-4 days due to the psychic shock of acting as the conduit for Thoth’s dicta.
	* If the postulant is a priest of Thoth, the wisdom loss is halved (1-3).
	* If the postulant is evil, a greater guardian of Thoth (see new monsters) teleports in to dispatch the blasphemer (in addition to the standard WIS loss).
	* There is a base 10% chance that any postulant immediately becomes a devotee of Thoth; this chance increases by 2% for each subsequent consultation. Such converts will be fanatical, and conversion may have class and/or alignment implications.
* Due to the psychic stress of channeling Thoth, characters may only consult the Oracle once per month.

Anaximander, male Archontean sage: SZ M; AL LN; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 8d4; HP 3 (max 14); #AT 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: STR 13, INT 18, WIS 16, DEX 8, CON 5, CHA 8.
* Without his books and research materials, he has only access to the following clerical spells: detect evil, detect magic; augury; locate object; divination, tongues; true seeing; stone tell.
* Anaximander was a famous sage in his day, but is now more than 300 years old and insane. Were it possible to cure him, his major field of study is physical universe (specialties: architecture & engineering, chemistry, geology & mineralogy), while his minor fields of study are humankind and supernatural and unusual.

1 greater guardian of Thoth (see new monsters): SZ L; AL LN; AC 0; MV 120’; HD 8; HP 53; #AT 4 or 1; Dmg 1-8/1-8/1-8/1-8 or 1-12; MR 20%. Special attacks: fear, stun. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; teleport without error 2/day.

### 3-119: Fountain of Knowledge

* A domed chamber, damp and mildewed, with long strands of rotting plaster hanging from the ceiling/walls.
	* In the center is a 10’-wide basin with a fountain gushing prodigious amounts clear, cold water.
		* The water is mundane, but temporarily transformed by the basin into a elixir.
		* Originally meant to boost Wis (to counter the effects of the Oracle), but now turned chaotic.  Only works once per month per person.
	* The water has spilled over the basin and collected in a low pool in the southeast corner of the room.
	* Over centuries the water has eroded a segment of wall, producing a small stream that disappears into a wall of fractured rock.

D20 Effect
1-5
+1d4 WIS for 1-4 days (original function)

6-8
+1d3 points to a random attribute for 1-4 days

9-11
-1d3 points to a random attribute for 1-4 days

12-14
Strong delusion for 1-4 days (e.g. believes a companion to be a devil; sees a shadow trailing a member of the party, etc.)

15-17
Heal 4-40 HP and cure disease

18-19
Poison. Take 1-8 damage per round for 3-6  rounds; save for half damage. If fail first save, 
must make second save at end of the  3-6 rounds. If fail second save, die. If  succeed, take an additional 2-8.

20
Re-roll twice, ignoring future results of 20

### 3-120: Entrance Hall and Doors

* This 20’-wide hallway ends in a pair of massive stone double doors at its eastern end.
	* The hallway's plaster is gone, revealing arrow slits on the north wall.
	* The scorched and cracked doors are stuck open inward, leaving a 3’-wide gap.
	* One door is carved with an ibis, the other a feather.

## Level 3: 121 - 137

### 3-121: Guard Post

* The beastmen mount a watch in this guard post, ready to blow a pair of enormous horns mounted through the east wall (bells pointing out into the Great Hall 3-123).
	* The horns echo like alpenhorns with a dull, reverberating boom that resonates into the Great Hall (3-123).

2 beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 6, 5; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spears; short swords; 
short bows.
* 3-18 sp per beastman.
* 2x rats

### 3-122: Secret Door and Passageway

* Secret Door (west wall of 3-123, leading to 3-127): difficult to notice (1-in-8) and opens by pressing in the bell of one of the horns protruding from the nearby wall (see 3-123).
	* Beyond, steep steps descend to a 5’-wide by 6’-tall passageway of rough-hewn rock leading to 3-127.
	* Those passing through the secret door without uttering a prayer to Thoth are subject to a Dispel Magic (see 3-127).

### 3-123: Great Hall

* The Great Hall is an imposing place, with a ceiling that stretches some 100’ above the floor. 
	* Major meetings of the whole cult of Thoth were held here; now it is a no-man’s land between the beastmen (areas 3-138 to 3-162) and grimalkin to the north.
	* The Hall is dark, although brackets for a score of torches still exist on the walls. 
	* The first 25’ of wall was originally plastered and decorated with images of Thoth.
		* Still remaining is a monumental side view of Thoth, left arm horizontal to the ground and pointing, right arm against his thigh (a clue to the puzzle in 3-2).
	* Eight 40’-tall freestanding columns once lined the Hall, now thrown down, with only 5’-tall broken stumps remaining.
	* There is remarkably little dust here, a sign that much traffic flows through this hall.
	* Scorch marks are easily noticeable on the floor and walls, and a large number of broken arrows litter the ground.
	* The upper reaches of the hall extend into Sub-Level 3 (see SL3-3).
		* With enough light, 75' above are seen an arcade circumscribing the hall, a stone bridge passing west to east, and at the south end, the looming statue of Thoth, the Overseer of Truth (see SL3-3).
	* Just south of the entry from 3-121 is a painting of a bearded man with empty eyes.
		* Approached within 10’ by a Medium or bigger creature, a magic mouth speaks (Archontean) “The Path of Lord Priscus is the path to enlightenment and fulfillment. The eyes will tell you the way.”
			* Refers to the Priscians (base in 9-58 to 9-64) and Sortian eyes.
			* Mouth fades after it speaks 8 more times.
	* The bells of the two horns stick through the wall from 3-121.
		* Turning the rim of one horn opens the secret door at 3-122.
	* A flight of 6 baboon-form gargoyles nest in niches 40’ up the walls of the Hall.
		* Slow to rouse.  Those who spend >3 Turns here will be attacked.
		* Each has a small stash of loot in its niche:
			* #1: a pair of +1 throwing daggers
			* #2: 2 carved ivory teeth of Pol (see the stone head at SL6-8)
			* #3: a pearl (195 gp), a green glass activation square
			* #4 a silver pitcher (25 gp), 2 aquamarines (100 gp).
	* Secret Door (west, leading to 3-121): easy to spot (1 in 4), opens by pushing a stone panel inward.

* If beastmen have sounded the horns in 3-121, the hall resounds to large kettledrums beating a military rhythm (see 3-123A).

Teleport Destination
* The Great Hall is arrival point for several one-way teleporters: UP-11, 2-10 and 4-167.
* Those arriving appear at the far north of the Great Hall, between the fallen pillars.

6 simian-form gargoyles: SZ M; AL CE; AC 5; MV 90’, 150’ flying (Class C); HD 4+4; HP 32, 29, 28, 22; #AT 4; Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-6/1-4. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit.

##### 3-123a: Beastman Barricades 

* Each of these 3 locations has a similar 7'-tall masonry barricade running across the original hallway.
	* Platforms 4’ up the eastern sides of these walls allow missile fire at enemies approaching from the Great Hall.
	* Each wall has a 4’x4’ wooden door set into it, kept closed and locked at all times.
	* The northernmost barricade can be supported by arrow fire from slits in the wall leading to 3-138.
* Each barricade is manned by a bandon of 6 beastman troopers and a sergeant. 
	* They don't immediately engage those entering the Great Hall.
	* If warned by the horns at 3-121, they beat their kettle drums in a slow, rhythmic tempo.
	* If confronted by clearly superior forces, or rapid 33% casualties, the sergeant sends a runner for additional forces from the relevant barracks (3-138, 3-140, or 3-141), as well as from their varumani allies in 3-162 (25% chance the varumani ignore the summons). Beastman reinforcements arrive in 1d3+3 rounds, and one of the varumani arrives in 1 turn.

6 beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 8, 7, 7, 6, 6, 5; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spears; short 
swords; short bows.
* 3-18 sp per beastman

### 3-124: Fearful Chamber

* A permanent glyph of warding (fear) (12th-level) has been inscribed in a 20’-diameter circle in the center of this chamber (invisible).
	* Crossing the glyph: save vs Spells at -1 or flee in terror in a random direction
		* d4: 1: north, 2: east, 3: south, 4: west. 
* A fear elemental (new) has been drawn to the glyph
	* It's presence is preventing the escape of the goblins (3-130) and guardsmen (3-125).
	* It waits for the glyph to do its work, then attacks those who resisted , then tracking down the terrified.
	* It cannot enter the Great Hall, but pursues through open doorways in the area from 3-124 to 3-137. 
		* Currently the door to 3-125 is spiked shut from the north side
		* The doors to 3-129 and 3-133 are ajar.

1 fear elemental (see new monsters): SZ L; AC 0; MV 90’; HD 6; HP 39; #AT 1 per target; Dmg special; MR 50%. Special attacks: cause fear; immobilize with fear; drain CON. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; immune to cold and fire.

### 3-125: Set Patrol Beset

* An exploration party of Set guardsmen, led by Hamil the acolyte, ran into trouble in the Great Hall, fled west, and (like the goblins in 3-130), was trapped by the fear elemental.
* This is an undecorated former administrative chamber.
	* A fire burns in a hastily improvised fire pit.
	* The Setites are attempting to recuperate, and the entire party is jumpy, choosing to fight first and ask questions later.
		* If pressed, they release their zombified former comrades from 3-126.
	* They have piled a fair amount of rubble against the door to 3-128.
	* Rubble in the northwest corner contains the remains of a dead priest of Thoth.
		* He still wears a silver amulet of Thoth (25 gp).

4 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

### 3-126: Zombies

* Hamil raised 2 Set guardsmen as zombies and told them to wait in this closet.

2 zombies: SZ M; AL N; AC 8; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 12, 10; #AT 1; Dmg 1-8. Special: always strike last.

### 3-127: Hidden Tombs

* * The narrow, low tunnel from 3-122 is littered with five charred, rotted bodies.
	* No usable equipment, except an ebony ring of protection +1 (hard to spot).
	* The tunnel ends in a plain wooden door, swollen with moisture and stuck.
* This is the tomb of Neferet, one of the last high priestesses of Thoth.
	* It is also the location of the legendary Iron Circlet of Ghanor (new). 
 * The main area is a 10’-tall chamber with frescos of pleasant pastoral scenes of men and women fishing, hawking, and hunting.
	 * The west wall (to 3-127A) is illusory, and appears comparable to the rest.
	 * Wide archways lead north and south to separate chambers (3-127B and 3-127C).
	 * The false tomb of Neferet dominates the center of the main chamber.
		 * On a 2’ dais rests a large basalt sarcophagus (6’ long, 3’ high, 2’-4’ wide).
		 * The long sides are carved (Mithric) “Neferet, Beloved of Thoth, Seeker of Truth, Preserver of Secrets”. 
		 * The lid's image is of a placid-looking female in classic pose, wearing a circlet.
			 * Requires a feat of strength (like a stuck door) to remove the lid.
			 * Opening it wakes the undead in the adjoining rooms.  They attack, with Neferet herself (in 3-127A) casting spells through the illusory wall.
		 * The false tomb contains only sand, with a layer of dust of sneezing and choking covering it.
			 * Disturbing the sand unleashes the dust.  3 doses if skimmed very carefully.

##### 3-127a: Illusory Wall and True Tomb

* Behind the illusory wall from 3-127 lies the true tomb of Neferet. 
	* It is only 8’ tall, and is painted a darker blue on which appear a variety of mystical symbols (moons, stars, hermetic symbols, knots, etc.).
	* In the center of the room is a simple granite sarcophagus.
		* If intruders have opened the sarcophagus in 3-127, Neferet rises as a greater mummy to smite the desecrators, still dressed in the tattered orange ceremonial robes of the priesthood of Thoth, with a prominent ankh and ibis on a chain around her neck. She wears the Iron Circlet of Ghanor (new).  The smell of spice emanates strongly from her body.
	* The rest of the chamber is crowded with grave goods.
		* Delicate gilt chairs, a gilt settee, several ankhs on the end of 10’ poles (5000 gp intact, but fragile, 250 gp for just the gilt).
		* A 10’-diameter net made of gold mesh (Immobilizing Mesh, new)
		* A variety of alabaster and jet canopic jars (250 gp total).
			* There is a diamond (2500 gp) in one canopic jar, in another a pearl of the sirines, and 4 beads of force in another.
		* 5 cleric scrolls (dispel magic, bestow curse, neutralize poison, detect magic, speak with dead)
	* A few bits of crumpled parchment have been tossed into the corners.
		* One reads (Mithric) “To Neferet, glorious Priestess, from Hellas, humble librarian, greetings. I am working to accommodate your request to transport the contents of the special library to your new residence. Alas, the flight of so many of our acolytes, the evils of the present age, and my own decrepitude has delayed their transfer. I will seek to fulfill your wishes in good order.”
			* GM Note: this is the final draft of the note found in 2-71; Hellas never intended to move the library.

Tactics
* Once awakened, Neferet allows her minions from 3-127B and 3-127C to confront the desecrators while she fires spells through the illusory wall. The source of these spells may be unclear.  The strong smell of her spice may be a clue to her presence.
Sample tactics
* Neferet opens combat by casting silence 15’ radius into 3-127, then protection from good and hold person. Given conditions in 3-127, she might then cast insect plague or blindness. She uses cause and cure wounds spells as needed. She waits until the illusory wall is discovered to cast darkness, and until her minions are defeated to use flame strike. Only then, and possibly only after casting resist fire on herself, will she emerge to engage in hand-to-hand combat.

Neferet, greater mummy (new): SZ M; AL LE; AC 0; MV 90’; HD 10+3; HP 71; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12; MR 50%. Special attacks: aura of despair (saves at -3); mummy rot; command other undead. Special defenses: magic weapons to hit (+1 does 1 HP damage; +2 does half damage; +3 does full damage); immune to cold; takes half damage from non-magical fire; turned as a ghost.
* Possessions: amulet of protection from normal missiles; pearl necklace of invisibility (7/8 pearls); Iron Circlet of Ghanor (new for all three).
	* She is unable to use the iron circlet of Ghanor (a side effect of mummification)
* Spells as a 10th-level cleric with WIS 18
	* command(x2), protection from good, darkness, curse (reverse of bless); cause light wounds; hold person(x2), silence 15’ radius(x2), resist fire, chant; dispel magic, bestow curse (reverse of remove curse), blindness, animate dead; protection from good 10’ radius, cure serious wounds(x2), cause serious wounds; flame strike, insect plague.
* She cannot be turned while in area 3-127.

def 20, atk 23

### 3-128: Battle Scene (Embalming Chamber)

* A set of wooden shelves runs along the west wall, old and rotten, but intact.
