### 3-129: Audience Hall

* A semi-circular audience hall for the high priests of Thoth.
	* A raised platform rises at the western end.  A large, high-backed chair sits in the middle; its wooden back and ivory arms carved in elaborate geometric forms (100 gp, bulky).
	* The audience hall was turned into a tomb, and 3 stone sarcophagi lie in a neat row in front of the platform. 
		* Sarcophagus 1: truly ancient, worn, chipped and lidless (2000 gp to a collector). 
			* Moved and reused several times, now empty save for dust and a dried-up wineskin.
			* Bas-reliefs on its side show a dragon ridden by a man in elaborate armor. The dragon is scorching humans, eating lizards, and buffeting bipedal salamanders.
			* An inscription on a short side (Mithric) ‘The Imperator and his Consort defeat all enemies.’
		* Sarcophagus 2: no decorations, and no lid, roughly shaped and inelegant.
			* Hiding inside is a confused and very hungry giant centipede (trapped by the fear elemental in 3-124). It strikes at the first person to come near.
		* Sarcophagus 3: red basalt, with an intact brass lid affixed by heavy iron bolts (a sarcophagus of entombment, new).
			* Each side features a painted black eye.
			* The brass lid has an imprint of a humanoid with open screaming mouth and clutched hands.
			* Inside is a very hungry wight, Heraclos.
				* A clay tablet within the sarcophagus is broken into 3 pieces.  Reassembled; it reads: “Heraclos was found guilty and sentenced to eternal punishment without release.”
				* Heraclos still wears a platinum ring (250 gp) and a gold torc inset with lapis (300 gp).
	* Secret Door (west): easy to find (1 in 4); opens by sliding the door upward.

1 giant centipede: SZ S; AL N; AC 9; MV 150’; HD 1 or 2 HP; HP 2; #AT 1; Dmg n.a. Special attacks: poison (+4 to save).

1 wight: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 120’; HD 4+3; HP 33, 29, 27; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4. Special attacks: energy drain. Special defenses: silver or magic needed to hit; immune to sleep, charm, hold, cold, poison, and paralysis.

def 15, atk 
X / 33

### 3-130: Lost Goblins

* The chamber is nondescript, and its original function is hard to discern.
	* The west door opens to a hallway, blocked by to collapsed walls and ceiling. 
* An adventurous band of goblins made a foray from their main halls below.
	* Originally 20, they were overmatched by beastmen and Setites and now trapped.
	* Only a sub-chief, a witch doctor, and ten warriors still remain, taking refuge here.
		* Food is running low and they are nervous. Happy to negotiate if not immediately attacked, especially if offered protection from the Set guardsmen and/or assistance in returning home. 
		* Putatively sent forth for general exploration, they are secretly tasked by King Weskenim (SL4-22) with finding the lost scepter of the goblins (see area 8-69).
		* Rescuing and helping them to return to SL4 ensures a favorable hearing from King Weskenim.
	* GM Note (goblins’ route): 5-41 to 5-1, up the stairs to 3-12, south to 3-69 and into 3-123, then west into 3-124, where the fear elemental and the Set patrol (3-125) drove them to 3-130.

10 goblins: SZ S; AL LE; AC 6; MV 60’; HD 1-1; HP 7, 7, 6, 5(x3), 4, 4, 3, 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6.
* 3-18 sp per goblin.

Harab, goblin sub-chief (as a hobgoblin): SZ S; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 1+1; HP 8; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (military pick). Possessions: military pick.

Larakim, the 5th/4th-level goblin witch doctor: SZ S; AC 6; MV 60’; HD as a 3 HD monster; HP 21; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6 (spear). Spells: (lined out = already cast): ~~cure light wounds~~, ~~resist fear~~, protection from evil; augury, ~~chant~~, resist fire; dispel magic; ~~dancing lights~~, shield, ventriloquism; ~~invisibility~~, scare.

### 3-131: Simonet the Sun-Scarred Knight

* This was the high priest’s residence in antiquity, and bears traces of its former glory. 
	* An azure ceiling flecked with golden stars, still largely intact.
	* Enormous fresco of Thoth covering the east wall.
	* A settee, a four-poster bed, two tables, and a desk and chair are badly deteriorated.
		* Reclining on the settee in his gothic armor (new tech) is Sir Simonet of the the Sun-Scarred Knights.
			* He was exploring west of the Great Hall, attacked by the fear elemental, then the goblins and the Set cultists.  He retreated to this chamber to recover his strength and meditate about his next move.
			* Subsequent visits to this room find it empty of inhabitants, or (25%) occupied by goblins or beastmen hoping that Simonet abandoned some object of value.
A stone chest rests against the south wall and is still intact. 
	* It is trapped with explosive runes (5% per level for mage to detect, 1% per level for thief/bard), when read 10' radius 6d4+6, save for half (no save for reader).
		* If set off, roll saves for each item in the chest.
	* Ibis-skin pouch (350 ancient silver pennies); a platinum and jade necklace (275 gp); two heavy silver goblets (25 gp each); 3 leather scroll cases w/ scrolls (1: invisibility to undead, hold person, locate object; 2: cure serious wounds, neutralize poison, insect plague; 3: cloudburst, raise dead, resurrection.

Playing Simonet
* Will parlay with non-aggressive visitors.  Defends himself with his sun lance.
* He will doff his helm when parlaying, allowing PCs a glimpse of his face.
	* About 6’ tall, slim and wiry.  Coal-black hair, a thin nose, and pupils bleached of all color.  Laugh lines crinkle around his eyes, and he smiles easily, displaying prominent incisors.
	* Cheeks marked with old black scars in the form of a circle with rays radiating from it. 
	* He wears his circlet (silver w/ large emerald) on his brow and body armor at all times.
	* Fairly affable, though unmoved by claims to friendship or alignment obligations.  Enjoys a good joke, and likes to make puns, albeit sometimes very obscure puns. 
* Simonet is an inveterate collector of lore.
	* Particularly interested in the modern cult of Priscus Pulcher (he has glimpsed and parlayed with Priscians).
	* Would trade lore in return for information.
	* Might take an interest in some specific aspect of the PCs’ story and/or plans, reappearing at moments both opportune and inopportune.
* Unmoved by claims for assistance based on moral or ethical grounds.
* Uninterested in mundane wealth.
* No love or hatred for any of the factions of the Upper Halls.
* Will remain here for another day.

Sir Simonet, Sun-Scarred knight (see new monsters), 10th-level male Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LN; AC -2; MV 120’; HD 9+3; HP 66 (max 91); #AT 3/2; Dmg 7-13 (broadsword +2). 
Abilities: STR 18/70, INT 13, WIS 16, DEX 12, CON 8 (max16), CHA 12.
* Possessions: key to SL10A-16, gothic armor and sun lance (new tech); solar ring, circlet of command, and backpack of capacity (new for all three); 16 ancient octagonal platinum coins; broad sword +2; cloak of wise negotiating (new).
* He is down 8 Con from the fear elemental.
	* gothic armor (AC -2, 1/3rd from fire, cold, and electricity, regen 2/round (not limbs), sealed atmo)
	* sun lance (lesser power cell X / 24 charges, 2d6 (1 charge), 4d6 (2 charges), 6d6 (3 charges), 6d6 25' radius blast (4 charges))
	* solar ring (at will: sunlight 50' radius, feather fall, jump, air bubble around head for underwater for up to 1 day)
	* circlet of command (at will detect alignment, detect lies; 3/day command, 2/day charm person or monster)
	* backpack of capacity (10x carrying capacity)
	* cloak of wise negotiating (tongues, broken reading, raise hood to become invisible)

### 3-132: Antechamber

* Former antechamber to the high priest’s residence, now in shambles.
	* Wooden furniture smashed into sticks and thrown to the sides of the chamber.
	* Painted plaster has been ripped from the walls and piled in a mound.
	* A path amid the litter leads from the secret door to 3-133 to the door of 3-130.
	* Two goblin corpses lie mangled against the south wall; their bodies are badly burned and scorched. 
	* Secret Door (north): once expertly concealed by plaster, now easy to find (1 in 4).  The wall pulls outward into the room.

### 3-133: Fountain

* A burbling fountain stands by the east wall of this humid room.
	* Cool water flows from a 4’-tall bronze spigot carved to look like an upright cod.  The basin around the fish is shaped like a giant clam shell and is filled with the water.
	* There is no plumbing; the cod is a Decanter of Endless Water (no stopper is present) and the pool is a Basin of Evaporation (new).
* Secret Door (south): difficult to detect (1 in 8).  The wall pulls outward into the room.

### 3-134: Closet

* The door to this closet hangs broken on its hinges.
* The closet is empty save for some graffiti (Goblin Mithric) “We are trapped! Grugor went for help but did not return. I am hungry.”

### 3-135: Grand Stair up to SL3-9

* A barricade with a baboon skull on it lies across the entrance to the Great Hall.
	* The skull is a danger warning to beastmen, the stairs lead to baboon territory.
	* The corridor to this chamber is choked with cobwebs.
* An impressive circular stairway made of stone blocks rises 100’ to SL3-9.

### 3-136: Looted Chamber

* This former priest’s chamber has been looted enthusiastically. 
	* Various vulgar expressions in multiple languages are scrawled across the walls, stripped of plaster. 
	* Furnishings are gone, and a mound of organic matter rests against the south wall.
	* Three sheep beastman corpses lie in the center of the room, scorched severely. They rise as zombies 2 rounds after the room is entered.

3 beastman zombies: SZ M; AL N; AC 8; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 13, 9; #AT 1; Dmg 1-8. Special: always strike last.

### 3-137: No Man’s Land

* The beastmen have made this room into an initial point of defense for their complex.
	* The northern door opens, but the passage beyond has collapsed and is full of rubble.
	* The eastern door is barred (other side) and well maintained.
		* It has a small viewport that can be operated from the east side.
	* A continual light spell has been cast in the center of the ceiling.
	* The floor is littered with rubble, rising to a height of several feet in the corners.
		* Faint paths lead from the three doors to the center of the room.
	* In the center is a waist-high cylindrical stone plinth rises in the middle of the room, a small gold statuette atop it.
		* The beastmen pour reagents into the hollow interior of the plinth that produce a colorless narcotic gas.  The statuette stops the hole.  If it is removed, the slightly pressurized gas puffs out, filling the room in 2 rounds.  Those who breath it too long fall asleep for 1d6 Turns.
			* The mixture will be refreshed by beastment alchemists in about 2 days.
		* If at least half of a group falls asleep, the beastmen at 3-137b rush out, hoping to capture and imprison the intruders for interrogation.
	* Noise Traps: stepping near points marked N triggers a magic mouth which begins loudly singing beastman marching songs in bastardized Archontean
		* e.g., “Good Old Count Janisto/He took two hundred men/he marched them all around the halls/and he marched them home again,” and similar stuff.
		* Lasts for 1 turn, and alerts the beastmen in 3-137b.
	* Punji Traps: At the 2 points marked X, the beastmen have constructed 2' deep pits concealed by grey canvas scattered with rock dust and gavel.  Within are punji stakes smeared with excrement.
		* 1d2 damage, save vs Doom or foot injury slows for 12 - 24 hours (depending on footwear).  10% chance of blood infection (50% mild, 50% acute).

##### 3-137a: Dead Goblins

* Outside the door to 3-137 lie the bodies of three goblins slain by the beastmen.
	* The goblins are stripped of all belongings, and butchered for choice ‘meats’.

##### 3-137b: Beastman Watch

* Two beastmen from 3-142 are posted as watchmen behind this door.
	* They have a solid bar across the east side of the door (bend bars to break).
	* The beastmen watch 3-137 through a viewport.
	* If intruders are spotted, one beastman runs to 3-142 to summon an additional 6 beastmen and a sergeant.
		* They only open the door to 3-137 if half of a party has been incapacitated, or they possess overwhelming force.

2 beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 6, 5; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spears; short swords; 
short bows.
* 3-18 sp per beastman.
* rat, pig

## Level 3: 138 - 162 (Precincts of the Beastmen)

* In ancient times this was the heart of administrative and priestly activity for the cult of Thoth. It is now the home of a group of humanoids known known in the halls as ‘beastmen’, who call themselves either the Children of Deino or, more formally, the 4th Kentarchia of the 3rd Cohort of the Imperial Tagmata.
* All beastmen appear as hybrids of human and beast, whether the beast be dog, pig, goat, sheep, or rat. They are the product of centuries of breeding experiments overseen by Deino, a quasi-immortal sorceress (see 3-158). 

Background
* Some 250 years ago, the emperor sent a new archon, Adrienic (see 5-18), to Arden Vul with orders to re-establish imperial control over the complex. Adrienic brought with him the elite 3rd Cohort of the Imperial Tagma and the 2nd legion of scutarii (heavy infantry).
* When the imperial expedition foundered in the lower levels, the men of the 3rd Cohort sought to escape the Halls. One kentarchia (unit of 100) under the leadership of Gennadius found its way to this region, where they fell under the sway of Deino. Deino entranced most of the soldiers, although Gennadius and his faithful whippet (named Rex) managed to escape (see 6-50 for Rex, and 8-41 for Gennadius). She kept the most handsome and useful soldiers alive through sorcery and potions, and transformed the others into beasts. She ‘grew’ her flock by interbreeding the soldiers and their descendants with animals until the current self-sustaining mix of debased beast-men was reached. 
* Despite their bestial form (and aggressive natures), the Children of Deino are surprisingly well organized and disciplined. This is due to the old legionary training of the forefathers of the group, whose expertise and tactical sense has been passed down over the generations.
* The beastmen maintain a semblance of the old military structure of their forebears, although some titles have been garbled: the Children consider themselves a single tagma divided into konturbia (‘companies’ of 20-30 members), which are subdivided into banda (patrols of 10 each).
* They are also well led, starting with Deino the witch, but also including Count Skleros (3-151) and his tough staff sergeants. Beastman military hierarchy is based on merit, even though individual Konturbia are named after a single sub-species of beastman. That means that each konturbs is actually comprised of a mixture of basic types. 
* The Children are highly organized, and react in a disciplined manner to any threat or assault. They have erected impressive barriers (3-123A) at the most obvious entry points to their domain, and post vigilant guards at each of these locations. Should intruders assault one of the entry points, the leaders will be swiftly informed, and appropriate measures will be taken to repel invaders. If possible, the beastmen attempt flanking maneuvers in force; that is, reinforcements in the form of at least one company will be sent to meet the intruders as they advance, while another company will be sent to come upon the intruder’s flank.
	* Skleros (3-151) will certainly summon the witch doctors (3-144), the varumani (3-162) if necessary (although they only respond 75% of the time), and, after some hesitation, Deino herself (3-158).
	* If intruders seem too strong, Skleros orders a fighting retreat down one of the entrance paths so as to allow the rest of the Tagma to escape out one of the other entrances/exits.
* Once assaulted, the Children will double their vigilance: no banda (patrols) will be absent from their barracks, and entrance points will be strengthened with the presence of a witch doctor and another patrol; given sufficient time, the beastmen will also rig magical and mechanical traps in the great hall (3-123). 

### 3-138: Beastman Barracks: Porcine Konturbs (Pig Company)

* The beastman troopers of Pig Company live in this chamber.
	* Pig Company ranks second in seniority, and its members are proud and haughty.
	* The konturbs is 21 beastmen, organized into three banda (patrols) of 6 troopers and one sergeant per bandon.
		* One bandon is all pig-men, the other two are mixed. The sergeants are all pig-men.
		* One bandon is always on guard at 3-123A; one bandon is always here; and the third patrol is either here (33%), or elsewhere in the complex (3-161, 3-147, 3-156, or 3-158).
*  Their chamber is spartan and very neat, with well-ordered bed-mounds surrounding a trestle table at which troopers can play dice, etc.
	* The far wall boasts the tattered Pig Company banner: a mailed fist with small fragments of equipment, bone, and a few slips of parchment (battle mementos) hanging from it.
		* Theft of the banner provokes immediate and vengeful retribution.
	* Below the banner is a 10’x10’ ‘rooting ground’ of mud and soil, ripe for wrestling and rooting.
	* * The company has a communal stone chest next to the wall.
		* Dried rations, 2 potions of healing, a few extra helmets, etc.
	* A stone water barrel sits next to the chest. 
	* A weapons rack on the other side of the door holds spears, shields, and swords.
* An arrow slit allows support of allies at 3-123a.
	* Two troopers are always posted near the slit with bows at the ready.
* The company has collected a dozen busts and bits of statuary to decorate its barracks.
	* One is a portrait bust of Priscus Pulcher (so marked on its base) and malfunctioning Sortian face.
		* A handsome young man, with close-cropped hair, a trim beard, and smiling eyes.  Empty sockets in the place of eyes.
			* Sortian eyes placed in the sockets cause fizzing and sputtering.
* Pig Company’s prize possession is the mummified head of Comentiolus, one of the original imperial soldiers and, according to Pig Company lore, the ‘First Pig’.
	* Comentiolus’s head is often touched for luck, and is thus fairly shiny with wear.
	* Given the right spell, PCs might learn something from Comentiolus’s restless shade.

6 or 12 beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 9, 8, 7(x3), 6(x4), 5(x3); #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spears; short swords; short bows.

1 or 2 beastman sergeants (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 4; MV 90’: HD 2+2; HP 16, 15; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6 or 2-5. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spear; war hammer.

Each of the beastmen has 2-12 sp, while each sergeant has 3-18 sp and 1-8 gp.

### 3-139: Supply Closet

* A small room with supplies.
	* Brooms, hammers and chisels, a wide selection of pieces of lumber pillaged from the halls, and odds and ends (goblin equipment and weapons, coils of rope, etc.).
	* 20% chance any bit of non-comestible, non-warlike equipment can be found here.

### 3-140: Beastman Barracks: Canine Konturbs (Dog Company)

* The beastman troopers of Dog Company live in this chamber.
	* Dog Company is the most senior of the beastman units; its troopers smarter and quicker than the others, with the most battle experience.
	* The company is a thorough mix of dog-, pig-, sheep-, goat- and rat-men, all of whom are veterans.
	* They expect, and receive, deference (as well as envy!) from the other companies.
	* A total of 16 beastmen (4 dog-men, 4 pig-men, 3 goat-men, 3 rat-men, 2 sheep-men) are stationed here, organized into two six-beastman banda (patrols).
		* 2 patrol sergeants (one dog-man, one goat-man) and 2 staff sergeants (one pig-man, one rat-man) also live here.
	* One bandon is always on guard at 3-123A. The other patrol is present in the barracks 50% of the time; the rest of the time it will be found in either 3-156, 3-158, 3-161 or one of the harems (3-145 to 3-148).
		* The Staff Sergeants will be present here 50% of the time. 
* The chamber is spartan and neat, with well-ordered bed-mounds surrounding a trestle table at which troopers can play dice, etc.
	* On the east wall is displayed the tattered blue Dog Company banner featuring a mailed fist; hanging from it are very small fragments of equipment, bone, and a few slips of parchment (battle mementos).
		* Theft of the banner provokes immediate and vengeful retribution. 
	* The company has a communal stone chest by the north wall
		* dried rations, 6 potions of healing, a few extra helmets, etc.
	* A stone water barrel sits next to the chest.
	* A weapons rack next to the door holds spears, shields, and swords. 
* A looted golden idol of Anubis is mounted on a ledge on the south wall (90 lbs, 5000 gp).
	* Human body with a canine head whose mouth is open, displaying sharp teeth.
	* Believing it to be an image of Rex (6-50), the whippet companion to the original imperial kentarchia, the company considers it to be its special mascot. 

0 or 6 beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 8, 7, 7, 6, 6, 5; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spears; short swords; short bows.

0 or 1 beastman sergeant (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 4; MV 90’: HD 2+2; HP 15; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6 or 2-5. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spear; war 
hammer.

0-2 beastmen staff sergeants (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 4; MV 90’; HD 3+3; HP 23, 20; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7. Special attacks: tactics; +1 to damage from STR. Possessions: ring mail 
and shield; spear; short sword.

Each of the beastmen has 3-18 sp.

### 3-141: Beastman Barracks: Ovine Konturbs (Sheep Company)

* The beastman troopers of Sheep Company live in this chamber. 
	* Sheep Company is the most junior company, with the youngest and least tested troopers.
		* Although well trained like all of the Children of Deino, the Ovine troopers tend to be simultaneously more nervous and more aggressive than their senior colleagues (weaker morale, but more likely to attack).
	* A total of 21 beastmen are stationed here: three six-beastman patrols with 3 patrol sergeants.
		* 8 sheep-men, 6 goat-men, 3 dog-men, 3 pig-men, 1 rat-man. The three sergeants are all goat-men. 
	* One bandon is always on guard at 3-123A. Another bandon is always present in the barracks. The third patrol will be found either in the barracks (25%), in the mess hall (25%), with its harem in 3-145 (25%) or training in 3-156 (25%).  
*  The chamber is small and cramped, with rickety wooden bunkbeds arranged in rows across the floor (although the sergeants get single beds).
	* The troop possesses no table.
	* Their banner is significantly newer and less tattered than those of the other companies (the last banner was lost a decade ago in a disastrous expedition to the lower levels). It boasts no battle mementos.
		* Even still, theft of the Sheep Company banner provokes immediate and vengeful retribution.
	* The company has a communal stone chest next to the door
		* dried rations, a contraband jug of wine, a few extra helmets, etc.
	* A stone water barrel sits next to the chest.
	* A weapons rack next to the door holds spears, shields, and swords.
	* Lacking better spoils, the company has decorated its chamber walls with surprisingly high quality painted images of giant beastmen spearing a variety of enemies, including goblins, humans, and, improbably, varumani.

6 or 12 beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 9, 8, 7(x3), 6(x4), 5(x3); #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spears; short swords; short bows.

1 or 2 beastman sergeants (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 4; MV 90’: HD 2+2; HP 16, 15; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6 or 2-5. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spear; war hammer.

Each of the beastmen has 3-18 sp.

### 3-142: Beastman Barracks: Caprine Konturbs (Goat Company) 

* The beastman troopers of Goat Company live in this chamber.
	* Goat Company ranks third in seniority. Its troopers are a mixed bag, a fair proportion of misfits passed over for promotion, and an equal number of ambitious youngsters hoping to prove their worth and earn promotion to Dog Company.
	* Although an effective unit by most standards, it is the most fractious of the konturbia that make up the Tagma. Given its status, its troopers are equally likely to bully Sheep Company troopers and to cringe in the presence of the veterans of Dog and Pig companies.
	* A total of 28 beastmen are stationed here: four six-beastmen patrols with four patrol sergeants.
		* 8 sheep-men, 7 rat-men, 5 pig-men, 5 dog-men, and 3 goat-men; of the sergeants, 1 is a sheep-man, 2 are pig-men, and one is a dog-man. 
	* Two troopers are always on guard at 3-137B, while a full bandon is always elsewhere in the complex (3-146, 3-156, 3-158 or 3-161). The remaining troopers are always present in barracks.
* The chamber is cramped and crowded with rickety wooden bunkbeds.
	* Although clean, it smells of too many beastmen living in close quarters.
	* Given the cramped conditions, it is common (25%) to find troopers relaxing in the hallway outside their barracks. 
	* The west wall boasts the tattered Sheep Company banner featuring the usual mailed fist; hanging from it are only three battle mementos.
		* Loss of the banner will inspire company morale and will provoke immediate and vengeful retribution.
	* The company has a communal stone chest next to the door
		* dried rations, 2 potions of healing, a few extra helmets, etc.
	* A stone water barrel sits next to the chest.
	* A weapons rack next to the door holds spears, shields, and swords. 
	* The company has recently won some trophies:
		* three stuffed (but smelly) mantari hang from the ceiling
		* a poorly-preserved halfling corpse has been impaled on a spear in the center of the room, allowing the troopers to push it into amusing poses.

16 or 22 beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 9(x3), 8(x4), 7(x4), 6(x7), 5(x4); #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spears; short swords; short bows.

2 or 3 beastman sergeants (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 4; MV 90’: HD 2+2; HP 16, 15, 14; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6 or 2-5. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spear; war hammer.

Each of the beastmen has 3-18 sp. 

### 3-143: Inspection Point and Map

* The arrow slits in the east and south walls are obvious when traversing this passage.
	* Light seeps through the slits from the Fire Support Center (3-144), and the witch doctors within can fire spells and missiles through them.
* Tagma Command (3-150) has assembled tactical maps on pieces of hide (goblin, human)  stretched along the north and west walls.
	* Present a fairly complete picture of the easily accessible areas of Levels 3 and 4. 
		* Most hidden areas, accessed only by secret doors, are not indicated.
	* Numerous notes have been scrawled on the map in the beastman tongue.
* A large tapestry stolen from the cult of Set hangs on the west wall of the passage, concealing the door to 3-144.
	* Geometric forms, with a depiction of a was stick in its center (100 lbs, 450 gp).

### 3-144: Beastman Fire Support Center (Witch Doctors)

* The Tagma’s 3 witch doctors and their 1 apprentice inhabit this strategic choke-point.
	* Concealed Door: emerges behind behind the tapestry in 3-143.
	* Secret Door (to 3-145): a 3’x3’ panel pushed in and slid aside.
*  The chamber is sumptuously decorated, with many furs and cushions (350 gp all told).
	* The chamber is usually (75%) brightly lit with a continual light rock (concealable).
	* Each witch doctor has a bed and wooden chest.
		* Chest #1: 10 ancient octagonal platinum coins, 3 mage scrolls (sleep, magic mouth, blink), various clothing.
		* Chest #2: 50 small garnets (70 gp each), 3 mage scrolls (mirror image, explosive runes, fear), mundane clothing and gear.
		* Chest #3: a sapphire Sortian eye (new), a solid silver statuette of a varumani (400 gp), a fragment of a volume entitled "Deeds of Ptarmis" (provides a clue as to the location of Ptarmis’s tomb in 3-174).
	* Their apprentice sleeps under the table.
	* A stone water barrel rests against the east wall.
	* They share a small table with three chairs.
		* The witch doctors are close friends, and love to pass the time insulting each other as they gamble here.
		* 548 sp are scattered on the table as gambling chips.

Thirk, 7th/4th-level beastman witch doctor (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 7; MV 90’; HD as 5+ HD monster; HP 31; #AT 1; Dmg: 1-4. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail; dagger; 8 throwing daggers. Memorized spells: cure light wounds, detect magic, resist fear; augury, chant, snake charm; cause blindness, dispel magic; divination; identify, push, 
shield; levitate, scare.
* Thirk is a dog-man (+1 to surprise and initiative, +1 to all attack rolls, +10% morale).

Ujax, 5th/4th-level beastman witch doctor (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 7; MV 90’; HD as 4+ HD monster; HP 25; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail; 
staff. Memorized spells: cure light wounds, detect evil, light; augury, detect charm, speak with animals; remove curse; affect normal fires, shield, ventriloquism; Probus’s thunderous alert (see new spells), detect invisibility.

Drood, 4th/3rd-level beastman witch doctor (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 7; MV 90’; HD as 3+ HD monster; HP 27; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail; club. Memorized spells: cure light wounds, cause fear, remove fear; chant, speak with animals; dancing lights, shield; levitate.

Jixon, 2nd/2nd-level beastman apprentice witch doctor (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 7; MV 90’; HD as 2+ HD monster; HP 10; #AT: 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail; staff. Memorized spells: cure light wounds, protection from evil; dancing lights, shield.
* Jixon is a goat-man (33% berserk chance resulting in +2 attack and damage for 3 rounds, but -2 AC).

### 3-145: Beastman Birth Cauldrons

* An arrow slit lets noise and light into this chamber from 3-144.
	* The slit allows the witch doctors to fire spells and missiles at invaders.
* Big iron cauldrons line the walls.
	* Deino and the witch doctors brew up new beastmen from the remains of prior ones in these cauldrons.
* A blood-stained worktable stands against one wall, cleavers hanging above it.
	* Beastman corpses are dismembered to be spread among cauldrons.

### 3-146: Beastman Youth Dormitory

* This open area is home to 15 - 20 beastman youths (recently decanted from the cauldrons).
	* The chamber is clean, with sleeping areas, small tables, and a variety of mundane items stored in a set of wicker baskets affixed to the south wall (needles, thread, wool, skins, hammers, etc.).
	* When they are not running errands for the Tagma’s banda, they will be engaged in sweeping/cleaning, repairing equipment, or other support tasks.
	* If combat breaks out in 3-141, they make a fighting retreat to 3-158 or 3-159.

10 female beastmen, as troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 10; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 7, 7, 6(x4), 5, 5, 4, 4; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: clubs.

5-10 beastman young (see new monsters): noncombatants (AC 10, HP 2).

### 3-147: Beastman Concubines

* Identical to 3-146.

15 female beastmen, as troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 10; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 7, 7, 6(x7), 5(x4), 4, 4; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: clubs.

6-12 beastman young (see new monsters): noncombatants (AC 10, HP 2).

### 3-148: Detention Center

* This large room doubles as a detention center and a torture/interrogation site
	* Divided in two by animal-skin curtains.
		* The torturer does his work to the west.
		* The eastern half features eight sets of manacles set into the north and east walls, a small round table, and two chairs.

Currently the beastmen have only a few creatures in detention:

Ysabel Ligareon, 4th-level female Archontean cleric of Mitra: SZ M; AL LG; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 4; HP 18 (max 26); #AT 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: STR 15; INT 15; WIS 17; DEX 10; CON 9; CHA 11.
* A representative of one of the powerful noble Five Families (see World of Archontos appendix), Ysabel’s normally firm belief in her own invincibility is beginning to waver.

Rolf, 2nd-level male Wiskin ranger: SZ M; AL CG; AC 10; MV 
120’; HD 2; HP 11 (max 20); #AT 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: 
STR 16; INT 15; WIS 15; DEX 10; CON 15; CHA 12.
* A member of an adventuring party that entered the upper Halls, Rolf got separated from his crew and was swiftly overwhelmed. He has been tortured and is in bad shape. If desired, the GM could link him to any good-aligned party from the NPC appendix.

Thomas, a Set acolyte (see new monsters), as a 3rd-level Archontean cleric of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 5 (max 17); #AT 1; Dmg by weapon.

### 3-149: Count Georgik

* Georgik’s chamber is well appointed, with a comfortable set of looted cushions and furs.
* A trapped stone chest (poison needle trap; -5% to detect)
	* 456 sp, 278 gp, a mummified goblin hand, a winged statuette of a silver lizard (new).
* A wooden desk piled high with notes
	* Notes about missions, enemies, and history
* An armor rack with an elaborate suit of black chain mail chased in silver (150 gp)
* A weapons rack with a standard spear and sword.
* Mounted next to the south door, his rod of comital office.
	* Actually a wand of dispel fear (10 charges)

Georgik is found in his chamber (20%), Deino’s Hall (30% - see 3-158), or Tagma Command (50% - see 3-150).

Georgik, beastman count (see new monsters) (20%): SZ S; AL LN; AC 5 (due to leg); MV 60’ (due to leg); HD 5+5; HP 40; #AT 1; Dmg 3-8. Special attacks: tactics, +2 to damage from 
STR.
* Possessions: chain mail; spear; short sword
	* potions of explosive acid and Greek fire (see new magic items)
	* keys to his trapped stone chest and to the doors at 3-154, 3-156A, 3-163A, and 3-163B.
* This savvy, old, one-legged pig-man is the master strategist of the tribe.
	* Having fought enemies for several decades, he has a clear memory of the layout of the Halls, and of the strategies to be employed in traversing, defending, and assaulting them.
	* The map at 3-143 is his idea.
	* Despite his infirmity, Georgik hops around nimbly with his crutch.
	* As he has aged, Georgik has become a workaholic. He is also the patron of young Trisko the Natty of the LRCP, who returns Georgik’s favor with fierce loyalty.
	* Georgik’s voice frequently clashes with that of the younger Nikeos in council meetings.

### 3-150: Tagma Command

* The planning center for the Tagma.
	* 4 tables, a slew of parchment, and 4 camp beds.
		* Parchment sheets: significant information (specific and relatively up-to-date) about 1d4 major areas of the Halls, such as the goblin warrens (SL4), the troll thegn’s court (7-1 and 7-72 to 7-77), the arena (6-56 to 6-95), or the great cavern (3-163 and 3-172).
	* The four senior beastman staff sergeants live here and help plan strategy with the counts and Skleros.
	* At any given moment, at least 3 of the 4 staff sergeants will be present; it is also possible for some of the counts to be present. 

3 or 4 beastmen staff sergeants: SZ S; AL LN; AC 4; MV 90’; HD 3+3; HP 23, 20; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7. Special attacks: tactics; +1 to damage from STR.
* Possessions: ring mail and shield; spear; short sword
	* one has a spear +1.
	* 3-30 gp each

Counts Nikeos (40%) and/or Georgik (50%). For stats see 3-152 and 3-149.

Count Skleros (45%): for stats see 3-151.

### 3-151: Count Skleros, the Beastman Commander

* Skleros’s chamber is not significantly more luxurious than those of the counts.
	* He has a fine set of furs for sleeping.
	* An unused desk.
		* A cache of 150 ancient silver pennies in a leather pouch nailed to the back of the desk.
	* A stone water barrel, and a pair of Thothian tapestries showing bird scenes (100 gp, 40 lb each).

* He is present in his chamber (25%), Tagma Command (45% - see 3-150) or Deino’s Hall (30% - see 3-158).

Skleros, beastman count (see new monsters) (25%): SZ S; AL LN; AC 2; MV 90’; HD 5+5; HP 40; #AT 1; Dmg 5-10. Special attacks: tactics, +2 to damage from STR.
* Possessions: chain mail +1; spear +2
	* cloak of the dwarves (new)
	* ring of the stalker (new)
	* keys to the doors at 3-154, 3-156A, 3-163A, and 3-163B.
	* a pouch with 3 sables (100 gp each)
* Skleros is a middle-aged, slightly paunchy dog-man.
	* He has risen to command of the Tagma through a combination of a genial personality, canny politicking, military skill, and luck.
	* Although he may appear as slightly dim, he is in fact a shrewd judge of personality, and is adept at manipulating beastmen and others to attain his goals. He is exceptionally good at ‘managing’ Deino.  He gives Nikeos much public voice, while privately listening to the more cautious Georgik. In short, he is a very successful commander.

### 3-152: Count Nikeos

* His chamber is decorated in a sort of spartan-chic style.
	* Elegant furs, but not too many
	* A simple desk, but of valuable ebony (500 gp); no distracting documents
	* Two elaborate weapon/armor racks with a silver-chased chain mail shirt (300 gp), a silver-hilted sword +1, and an ebony hafted spear (50 gp).
	* A wooden chest.
		* 1,156 sp, potion of heroism, potion of invisibility

* The count is in his chambers (30%), Tagma Command (40%, see 3-150), or in Deino’s Hall (30%, see 3-138). 

Nikeos, beastman count (see new monsters) (30%): SZ S; AL LN; AC 2; MV 90’; HD 5+5; HP 40; #AT 1; Dmg 4-9. Special attacks: tactics, +2 to damage from STR.
* Possessions: chain mail; short sword +1
	* An amulet of spell absorption (11 spell levels) (new).
* An exceptionally canny goat-man, Nikeos is the youngest beastman to make count in many generations
	* Nikeos is in his early 30s, still young and virile.
	* He did so on the strength of his aggression and ambition.
	* Unlike his counterpart, Georgik, Nikeos is an imperialist, constantly urging Skleros to expand the territory of the Tagma and confront their enemies.
	* Given this philosophy, Nikeos is well loved by the younger companies.

1 beastman assistant (50% chance if Nikeos is present): SZ S; AL LN; AC 10; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 6; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics.
* Possessions: weapons; keys to the doors at 3-154, 3-156A, 3-163A, and 3-163B.

### 3-153: Armory

* This room serves as the forge and armory of the Tagma.
	* The room is smoky and hot, lit with a dull glow from the forge.
	* Against the western wall is a forge apparatus, worked by a sheep-man smith aided by three rat-man assistants.
	* Along the south wall are various casks for cooling hot steel, bins with raw metal, and the tools of a smithy.
		* The smith has a two 5-lb bars of gold (250 gp each) hidden among the pig iron and steel scraps.
	* The beds of the smith and his assistants lie against the eastern wall.
		* Hidden in the smith's bed is a pouch with 3 pp, 35 sp and a crystal ring (75 gp).
	* The center of the room holds a range of weapon and armor racks
		* 5-10 beastman-sized suits of chain mail, a dozen spears, a dozen beastman short swords, and various helmets, greaves and other equipment. 
* The beastmen have bored a chimney up into the rock.
	* It debouches in a cave some 30’ above this level. Despite the ‘chimney’, the area is still quite smoky.

1 beastman smith, as a sergeant (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 4; MV 90’: HD 2+2; HP 15; #AT 1; Dmg 4-7. Special attacks: tactics; +2 to damage due to STR. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spear; war hammer.

3 beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 6, 6, 5; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spears; short swords.
* The assistants carry 3-18 sp in a pouch.

### 3-154: Beastman Barracks: the Pedary Konturbs, a.k.a. the Long Range Cavern Patrol

* This unassuming chamber is home to one of the elite units of the Tagma, the Long Range Cavern Patrol (LRCP).
	* The LRCP consists of four seven-beastman banda (patrols), each of which comprises 6 troopers and a sergeant. 
	*  Only the most intelligent, self-reliant, and hardy beastmen are selected for service.
		* By temperament the LRCP attracts rat-men, but overall recruitment is by merit.
		* Members rightly see themselves as an elite and have little if anything to do with the regular konturbia; in turn, the Companies (even Dog Company) treat members of the LRCP with elaborate deference. 
	* 8 rat-men, 2 pig-men, 5 dog-men, 3 sheep-men, and 8 goat-men.  The sergeants are 3 rat-men and a goat-man.  They are led by Count Trisko the Natty.
	*  The sole function of the LRCP is the active exploration of the Halls and the acquisition of material and information usable by Tagma Command and Deino
		* Only one patrol is likely to be in residence here at any given time.
		* Above all else, the LRCP is tasked with procuring wood, iron/steel, fresh fruit and vegetables, and the specimens of cloud cap mushrooms that Deino (3-158) requires (see new flora). 
		* These missions take them, naturally, into the Great Cavern (3-163 and 3-172), where cloud caps can be found, but also into the ruins of the city of Arden Vul and sometimes into the valley below.
		* It is the LRCP that makes use of the ‘beastman entrance’ to the Halls, located at 3-189. 
* This chamber features nine bunk beds ranged against the north and south walls, four single beds along the west wall, a long trestle table, and a smaller table.
	* Next to the door is a communal chest, a stone water barrel, and an equipment stand.
		* Chest: 4 potions of healing, a potion of gaseous form, a potion of animal control, a potion of clairaudience, a potion of clairvoyance, and a potion of plant control. 20 iron rations, 6 water flasks, 6 flints, 6 belt knives, 20 torches, etc.
	* Trisko’s desk
		* A pouch of 20 aquamarines (100 gp each), an iron box with 275 sp, a silk bag with a small diamond (1,150 gp), a ring of protection +1, 10 doses of cloud cap mushrooms, and a quire of parchment with detailed notes on the features of 3-12 interesting locations on Levels 3 and 4 (GM’s choice). 
	* The insignia of the LRCP (a fist holding a torch) is painted on the east wall.
	* The door leading to the passage to 3-163a is locked and barred, with a viewing slit.
		* The LRCP has its own elaborate set of passwords that change on a daily basis. 
 
6 or 12 beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 8, 8, 7(x4), 6(x4), 5, 5; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; 
spears; short swords; short bows.

1 or 2 beastman sergeants (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 4; MV 90’: HD 2+2; HP 16, 15; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6 or 2-5. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spear; war hammer.

Each trooper of the LRCP has 2-12 gp and 1-6 pp.

Trisko the Natty, rat-man count (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 2; MV 90’; HD 5+5; HP 40; #AT 1; Dmg 5-10. Special attacks: tactics, +2 to damage from STR.
* Possessions: chain mail; short sword +2
* torc of domination (new)
* gilded helm of infravision (new)
* keys to the doors in 3-154, 3-156A, 3-163A, and 3-163B.

Count Trisko the Natty, a rat-man, commands the LRCP. 
* A canny explorer and diplomat, with the most experience of any of the beastmen leaders with conditions outside the Halls. Trisko has met and negotiated with Craastonistorex, and is legendary among his peers for a dangerous mission to the valley floor where he and one of his banda intimidated a tribe of local kobolds into delivering important prisoners into Trisko’s hands (see map BV-The Thicket).
* Trisko is the most willing to trade information and even maps with any peaceful visitors his patrols encounter.
* Trisko is especially anxious for the return of his missing bandon, that led by sergeant Histar (currently dwelling in 3-221 as slaves of the greenhag of area 3-204). 

### 3-155: Storage and Supplies

* Theoretically a storage room for the entire Tagma, it is considered the territory of the LRCP; the other beastmen tend to avoid it.
	* It is crammed with wooden and stone boxes and loose bits of gear and pillage.
		* 25% of the boxes hold foodstuffs (dried mushrooms, cured monkeys, meat jerky of dubious origin, etc.).
		* 2 forgotten casks of fine wine, stolen from the cult of Set (50 lb, 250 gp each).
		* Other boxes hold dungeoneering equipment: ropes, pitons, hooks, pulleys and grapples, poles, hammers, bits of stone and wood, etc.
	* Fruits of some of the LRCP expeditions:
		* A marble bust of a forgotten priest of Thoth (75 gp)
		* A 3’-diameter lapis and silver symbol of Set (50 gp)
		* A box: 35 ancient octagonal platinum coins
		* 35 samples of dried red veil mushrooms (flora)
		* 20 samples of aqua vitae mushrooms (flora)
		* A forgotten leather pouch: 1 silver, 1 gold and 1 sapphire Sortian eyes (new)  and a pale green ioun stone.

### 3-156: Sparring and Training Hall

* A 20’-wide, 20’-tall arched corridor, supported by a single row of 4’-diameter columns.
	* Sconces line the walls.
	* The beastmen have repurposed it to serve as a training and sparring hall.
		* The chief trainer (a dog-man staff sergeant) and his three assistants staff it.
			* Their sleeping pallets are in the southwest corner.
			* Normally 1 to 3 banda (patrols) from the various companies are present, sparring or practicing unit tactics.
			* If the complex is under assault, only the trainer and his assistants are here.
		* Bins of old shields and dulled weapons line the south wall.

Adros (dogman), 1 beastman trainer, as a staff-sergeant (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 4; MV 90’; HD 3+3; HP 20; #AT 1; Dmg 4-9 (mace +1). Special attacks: tactics; +1 to damage from STR.

##### 3-156a: Passage and Door to the Cavern

* A narrow (5’) passage, one of the primary routes of access to the Great Cavern.

### 3-157: Treasury

* Deino’s treasury: three large oak chests and various other items.
	* Chest #1: 18,259 sp. 
	* Chest #2: 5,673 gp and 14,512 cp.
	* Chest #3: a bolt of fine damask silk (450 gp), a silver head of a handsome ‘human’ (actually an infernal effigy (new)), a gauntlet of fire absorption (new), potions (healing 2x, flying, stone giant strength).
	* Near the chests are display stands:
		* Human-sized suit of black leather armor +2
		* A two-handed sword +2.
	* Scattered around the room are the following
		* A terra cotta tomb seal chased with lapis and silver (100 gp)
			* Taken from the tombs at 3-129, featuring the second secret name of Thoth (Giver of Life).
		* A pair of fireplace pokers with solid-gold handles (50 gp each)
		* An ivory and gold triptych studded with precious stones (575 gp)
			* Features the 8th, 9th and 10th of the Labors of Arden
			* A platinum, ceremonial, Mycenean-style helmet (350 gp)
			* A porcelain urn with a beautiful depiction of Larel One-Eye and the farmer’s wife (100 gp)
			* 3 clerical scrolls (protection from evil 10’ radius; silence 15’ radius; detect magic).

### 3-158: Deino’s Hall

* Soft yellow light, low pastoral sounds, the pleasing tones of a sung ballad, and enticing odors of roasting meat waft from the open door.
* An imposing, 25’-tall hall; the lair of Deino, witch, enchantress, and ‘mother’ to the beastmen of the “Able Ones” (the 3rd cohort of the Imperial Tagmata).
	* The upper register of the walls still has the frescos of a Thothian audience hall: images of ibises, baboons, magical symbols, and cylindrically-hatted priests.
	* Smokeless torches burn in sconces along the walls (see new magic items).
	* The floor is covered with large, overlapping carpets of vibrant colors and dynamic patterns. 
	* A 20’-wide by 15’-deep dais occupies the north wall, on which lies Deino’s king-sized bed.
	* West Wall
		* A series of five bronze tripods of heating (new) bubble merrily.
		* Closed door leading to Skleros’s chamber
	* East Wall
		* Wooden armoire, painted a cheerful blue color.
	* North, south, and east walls
		* Stiff, standing mummified remains of 25 human soldiers (zombies).
			* Dressed in archaic armor and festooned with colorful silk ribbons (remnants of the original 3rd Cohort of the Imperial Tagmata).
	* A 10’ trestle table with benches occupies the center of the chamber
		* Set with pewter plates and settings and silver goblets. Bowls of fruit, plates of marinated meat, and bowls of pickled mushrooms temptingly fill the table.
	* A number of goats, pigs, sheep, dogs, and rats wander about tamely.
	* 2-5 naked (very attractive) members of random species lounge idly.
* Secret Door (south): trapped with a poison needle trap (-5% to disarm). To open, fold up a corner of the carpet and press a small stud, unlocking a panel in the wall.
	* The panel slides both ways, and is trapped (-5% to detect).
	* Sliding it to the left releases a poison needle; sliding to the right avoids the trap. 

* Armoire
	* 10 sets of filmy silk garments, perfect for snuggling with Deino.
	* Worn adventuring gear (clothing, belts, sacks - no armor or weapons) that used to belong to her current playthings.
	* Memorial Codex of the Cult of Thoth (stolen from 3-65)
	* In the back of the armoire is a large, silver box.
		* Box is locked and trapped with a poison needle (save vs poison or die; 2d6 even on success).
		* three scrolls (1: pyrotechnics, tongues, polymorph self; 2: fumble, conjure elemental, passwall; 3: airy water, globe of invulnerability, power word stun)
		* a set of six colored glass activation squares for use in 3-159
		* 19 doses of Rastite lotus powder (flora)
		* A vial of hot red liquid. (Deino's phylactery)
			* It contains Deino’s life essence; if emptied / smashed, she will be unable to regenerate.

* Tripods: The basin of each bronze tripod of heating (new) contains a different substance:
	* Tripod 1: Meat stew.
		* A more savory form of the beastmen’s cavern stew, Deino feeds this tasty fare to her playthings and any visiting beastmen.
	* Tripod 2: Syrupy golden mead, brewed from a variety of mushrooms and vital fluids garnered in the Halls
		* One special ingredient, Rastite lotus powder (flora).
		* When enchanted by Deino, this produces a delicious mead, with strong soporific qualities (-2 saves in humans for an hour for each glass imbibed)
		* It also acts to mask most powers of vampires, a property Thegan White-Mane used to subdue Isocorax (see 6-20).
	* Tripod 3: Transformation wine.
		* This purplish liquor gives off a faint odor of granite, blackberries, and wild game.
		* Its secret ingredient is cloud cap mushrooms (flora).
		* Anyone drinking a mug of this will be transformed into an animal: 1=pig, 2=dog, 3=goat, 4=rat, 5=sheep, 6=unholy combination of all three.
			* The transformation is permanent, but can be removed by dispel magic.
	* Tripod 4: ‘Mother’s milk’.
		* This thick, viscous, yogurt-like substance smells of pine nuts.
		* It tastes delicious, but is in fact deadly poison and will kill all those who don’t save at -1.
		* Deino uses this to end the lives of playthings and animals of which she has tired, and to grant a painless end to elderly beastmen.
	* Tripod 5: Elixir of life.
		* A thin, watery, whitish liquid that smells and tastes of mint and, strangely, of pepper.
		* Deino extracts this from corpses and combines it with special ingredients to form the basis of both transformation wine and her own phylactery.
			* When cloud caps are added, it becomes transformation wine.
			* When Deino adds her own blood, it turns red and is used for her phylactery.


5 naked humans (2 Archontean, 2 Wiskin, 1 Thorcin): SZ M; AL N; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 1-6 HP; HP 5, 5, 3, 3, 2; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger).

25 zombies: SZ M; AL N; AC 8; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 14(x3), 13 (x3), 12(x4), 11(x4), 10(x3), 9(x3), 8(x3); #AT 1; Dmg 1-8. Special: always strike last.

(30% each) The beastman counts Georgik, Nikeos, or Skleros. For stats, see 3-149, 3-151 and 3-152.

(55%) Varumani advisors: see 3-162.


Deino, semi-immortal female enchantress: SZ M; AL LE; AC 2; MV 120’; HD 6; HP 38; #AT 2; Dmg 4-7/4-7 (Deino’s dagger); MR: 33%. Special attacks: charm song (-1 to saves). Special defenses: regenerate 4 HP/rd; immune to charm, hold, polymorph.
* Possessions
	* Deino’s ring (new): gold band set with huge opal
		* Protection from normal missiles, Immune to hold
		* 2/day haste
		* Tied to her lifeforce; if she dies, it loses its power after 60 - 90 days.
	* A pearl necklace of invisibility (new)
		* 1d10+10 pearls, eat once and turn invisible
	* Deino’s dagger +3 (new): beautiful copper-hilted, wavy-bladed
		* 2/day inject paralytic venom (save vs poison or paralyzed 1d4 Turns)
	* Belt of large pearls (1,500 gp)
* Spell-like effects
	* at will: audible glamer, change self, detect illusion, detect invisibility, detect magic, and hypnotism ().
	* 3/day (as 7th-level illusionist): blur (), dispel illusion, hypnotic pattern (), invisibility (), magic mouth, phantasmal force (), improved phantasmal force (), non-detection (), and suggestion ().
	* Can cast magic-user or illusionist spells from scrolls.


Deino the Witch
* An ancient, quasi-immortal enchantress whose mastery of seduction and charms would be legendary were it more widely known.
	* She was a priestess of Isis in centuries gone, and learned to keep herself alive through secret and complex alchemy.
* She appears as an attractive nut-brown woman with raven hair and coal-black eyes.
	* She dresses in a loose tunic of pale yellow, secured with a belt of large pearls, from which hangs a slim knife.  She wears a large opal ring. 

Deino determines whether visitors should be charmed, attacked, or invited to negotiate.
* Deino loves to seduce and charm attractive members of any gender and humanoid species.
	* Once under her thumb, she cavorts with them until she tires of them, after which she turns them into animals (using her potions and ring). 
* Deino warmly greets any group composed of at least one attractive member (CHA 14+), inviting them (and their friends) to join her feast.
	* She apologizes for her beastmen (if they have attacked the party), attributing any combat to their jealousy and protective nature.
	* Genuinely interested in tales of her guests’ adventures, she begs for news of adventure, clapping and ‘ooh’-ing approvingly during any story telling.
	* As the festivities continue, Deino plies the guests with her (drugged) food and drink and eventually offers to tell her own story, at which point she finally attempts to charm guests with her song; she sings delightfully, in a slightly haunting manner that compels attention (-1 to saves).
	* Attractive individuals (CHA 14 or more) who are charmed are kept as playthings for 2d6 months; others are transformed into animals.
* Should guests prove hostile, or should a group include no desirable males, she summons all her forces (zombies, animals, and charmed men) to defend her.

Deino is interested in...
* Acquiring large quantities of cloud cap mushrooms (available in the Great Cavern, i.e., 3-163 and 3-172)
* Locating the remains of Gennadius and Rex (Gennadius’s remains are found at 8-41 and Rex’s can be found at 6-50).
* Information about the cult of Set.
* Information about pa'ut, homunculi, ancient Isis and Thoth lore.

Deino leaves most tactical and daily decisions to her counts. Only larger matters of strategy and policy are brought to her attention.

The beastmen are fully aware of Deino’s nature, and of the cruel fate reserved for most guests.  Still, she is their ‘mother’, and they will defend her fiercely.
* If the party has befriended senior beastmen, they may offer a warning, either direct (“Avoid Deino’s hall completely!”) or indirect (“Careful what you drink in Deino’s hall …”).
* Strangers or enemies receive no such warning.
* Those who attack Deino instantly become mortal enemies to the Tagma.

Deino has a close relationship with Thegan White-Mane (6-20), host of the Inn of the Lost.
* She relies on him to procure rare ingredients for her brews (especially Rastite lotus powder).
* In return, she supplies him with her syrupy golden mead, allowing him to continue to subdue Isocorax (see 6-20).
* Interrupting this trade would seriously weaken (if not endanger) both parties, and so both take pains to support and promote the interests of the other. 

### 3-159: Commons

* This chamber retains its (magical) coat of bright yellow paint studded with pale-blue and white ibises.
	* Tagma Command designated this chamber for off-duty relaxation, but the beastmen consider the paint job ugly and few use it. Even the furniture designated for this chamber has been ‘re-assigned.’
	* (Futile) paint removal in this chamber is a classic punishment detail.  The paint regenerates soon after.
* In the northwest corner lies a Thothian teleportation ring (address: YE-BL-GR-WH-BK-RE).
	* The beastmen are ignorant of its nature.
	* Deino knows and possesses a full set of the squares (in her armoire) and knows the addresses to AV-29, 1-19, 2-42, and 3-33.  She has not used the ring in decades.

### 3-160: Beastman Barracks: Veterans’ Hall

* Elder beastmen unable to serve in patrols linger here.
	* More ferocious ones seek glorious death in the Arena, more capable ones are promoted to leadership.  These are the rest.
	* Allegedly they guardian the north door (3-57A).  Mostly they sit around swapping lies and drinking cold water.
	* If the trap at 3-57 sounds, they summon a patrol from one of the other companies (arriving within 1 turn).
* There are eight sleeping pallets here, and a weapons rack with some ancient spears and chipped swords.
* The north door is heavily barred and has a small barred viewport at beastman eye-level.

8 venerable beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 6, 6, 5(x3), 4(x3); #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; 
spears; short swords; short bows. Special: they are -2 to hit and -2 to damage due to decrepitude.
* Each venerable beastman has 3-18 sp.
* pig, 2x goat, 3x dog, 2x rat

### 3-161: Beastman Mess Hall

* The mess hall buzzes with activity in normal times as patrols cycle through for meals.
	* A serving table stands against the east wall.
	* A table stacked with plates and mugs stands in the southeast corner
	* Two very long trestle tables with benches occupy the center of the hall. 

14-28 beastmen (in times of peace) (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 9, 9, 8(x6), 7(x8), 6(x8), 5(x4); #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring 
mail and shield; spears; short swords; short bows.

(25%) Varumani advisors : for stats, see 3-162.

##### 3-161a: Kitchens

* The kitchen features a large open fireplace, ceramic ovens, and a maze of preparation tables.
	* A huge cauldron simmers over the firepit, filled with "cavern stew" (a noxious mix of mushrooms, monkey meat, other meat (when available), lichen, moss, etc.
		* The cook prefers to use wood for the fire, but must frequently rely on the dried stems of giant mushrooms.
		* A crude ‘chimney’ vents to an upper cave and into the Great Cavern near 163b.
	* The head cook and her six assistants toil here 18 hours a day in noisy, hot conditions.
		* Many pots, pans, ladles, spoons, and knives are present and in heavy use.
		* Stone water barrels hold hot, warm, and cold water for washing (no soap used!).
		* The kitchen staff loves to sing martial marches as they work.

1 beastman cook, as a trooper: (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 7; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 5; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail; cleaver.
* The cook wears a silver chain necklace (25 gp).
* rat

6 beastmen assistants, as troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 7; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 8, 7, 7, 6, 6, 5; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail; cleavers.
* 2x dog, 2x pig, sheep, rat

### 3-162: Varumani Advisors

* Two emissaries from the troll thegn (7-30) have been sent to advise (and observe) the Children of Deino.
	* If no alert has been sounded, the varumani are here (20%), the mess hall at 3-161 (25%), or Deino’s Hall (3-158; 55%).
		* The emissaries are lazy and not particularly interested in protecting the beastmen (25% chance they ignore any call for aid).
		* If they suspect the beastmen are going to be defeated, they retreat to 3-159 and use the teleportation ring to teleport to 6-64 (the only address they know).
* Their chamber holds two huge piles of fur, a water barrel, a table (with some fist-sized dice, a sausage, two tankards, a small barrel of beer), and a locked wooden chest.
	* Chest: 576 sp, 626 gp, 2 troll thegn’s passports (Arden items), a silver rod (to  open the doors at 5-6E), a full set of 6 glass activation squares, a pair of solid gold goblets (stolen from the beastmen, 125 gp each).
* They have been assigned two young beastmen as runners and messengers, and they take great delight in joking about eating their young aides.

Clug and Verv, 2 lesser varumani (see new monsters): SZ L; AL LE; AC 4; MV 90’; HD 8; HP 58, 57; #AT 3 or 1; Dmg 3-6/3-6/4-10 or 7-22 (mattock, 3-18+4). Special defenses: 33% resistant to mind-affecting magic; immune to cold and poison; save as 8th-level fighters or 8th-level magic users, whichever is better; regenerate 3 HP/rd; infravision. Possessions: mattocks.

2 beastman youths: noncombatants (AC 10, HP 2).

## Level 3: 163 - 180

### 3-163: Great Cavern, Northern Portion

* This iconic location is renowned through the upper levels of Arden Vul.
* Luxuriant mushroom groves, a prolific (and nutritious!) troop of albino monkeys, numerous species of lizard and cave insect, and several noteworthy physical features, including a river, some falls, a lake, and a 50’ cliff.
	* The northern section (3-163) connects to the precincts of the beastmen (3-137 to 3-162), and to the river caves and other complexes.
	* The southern half (3-172) holds several ancient tombs and artifacts, and eventually leads to the exterior via a tunnel system.
	* The cavern floor along the river below the falls (3-164B) is 25’ above the level of the river.
* The ceiling averages 60-80’ in height.
* The temperature of the cavern is warm and humid.
* Among the colossal fungal growths are some species that emit dim orange phosphorescence.
	* The areas by the cliff (3-163C), lake, and the tops of the rock formations (3-174, 3-178, and 3-179), are pretty dark.
	* Anyone emerging from 3-154, 3-156, or 3-227 will see a low orange glow emerging from a stand of enormous mushrooms (10’ to 15’ tall). 
* There is a hum of insect activity, as well as the occasional moaning of breezes, plops of liquid from mushroom caps, and an occasional thrashing sound (prey being snatched).
	* The sound of the falls (3-164B) is loud once one has descended the cliff.

Kerbog Khan (SL12-25) regularly sends his dragonfly and explorer automatons to the great cavern to observe the denizens and gather specimens.
* 5% cumulative chance per hour spent in the cavern of encountering an automaton.
	* d6: 1-2 dragonfly automaton; 3-4: poison dragonfly automaton; 5: basic explorer automaton; 6: bipedal explorer automaton.
		* 33% chance that the Khan is inhabiting the automaton (75% on subsequent encounters).
		* Once initially encountered, 75% chance that the automaton will reappear after a significant encounter, as the Khan will be interested in how the newcomers have fared. 

1 basic dragonfly automaton of Kerbog Khan (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 4; MV 240’ flying (Class A); HD 1+2; HP 8; #AT 0 Dmg n.a.; MR 25%. Special defenses: immune to 
cold and fire.

1 poison dragonfly automaton of Kerbog Khan (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 4; MV 240’ flying (Class A); HD 1+2; HP 8; #AT 1; Dmg poison (death, or 1-3 turns paralyzation 
with 1-4 round slow on save); MR 25%. Special attacks: poison. Special defenses: immune to cold and fire.

1 basic exploration automaton of Kerbog Khan (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 2; MV 150’; HD 4; HP 29; #AT 2; Dmg 1-4/1-4; MR 40%. Special defenses: immune to cold and 
fire.

1 bipedal exploration automaton of Kerbog Khan (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 2; MV 90’; HD 6; HP 43; #AT 2; Dmg 1-6/1-6; MR 40%. Special defenses: immune to cold and fire.

##### 3-163a: Observation Cage

* The priests of Thoth constructed a 15' high, steel observation cage here, affording them an observation and collection zone.
	* North wall small steel door (locked, +10% to pick, freshly oiled).
* The beastmen of the Long Range Cavern Patrol have stacked several boxes near the door on the north wall.
	* Dried rations, filled water skins, 6 flasks of oil, a dozen torches.
	* A pail of a noxious smelling, greyish paste (made of mushrooms and other cave detritus).  Smeared on a torch, its smell repels giant centipedes.
		* Needed as the LRCP  rappels down the cliff face at 3-163c.

##### 3-163b: Feeding Station

* A locked steel door separates 3-156a from a stone bridge (5' wide, 15' above the cavern floor) extending out into the great cavern.
	* The bridge ends in a 5’x10’ platform from which the priests used to feed the monkeys and other small animals.
		* A rickety-looking but serviceable ladder is propped against the platform.
		* The cavern floor near the platform is dense with a variety of giant mushrooms, and the air is filled with chattering of monkeys and buzzing of dragonflies. 

##### 3-163c: Cliff

* Running across the northern edge of the Great Cavern is a sheer cliff dropping 50’ to the level of the lake (3-164).
	* Rocky and relatively easy to climb (+15% to climb rolls).
	* The fungal forest paths lead right to its edge; an inattentive (or running) PC might walk or run off the edge. 
	* The cliff edge nearest to points 3-163a and 3-163b have iron stakes driven into the stone (indicated by ‘x’), used by the beastmen as rope anchors. 
	* Small caves and holes in the cliff face house albino monkeys, various small insects, and numerous giant centipedes.
		* 50% chance that climbers are attacked by 3-4 giant centipedes.
		* 33% if descending quickly on ropes.
		* The foul paste at 3-163a, or Lankios's goo, wards off the centipedes.

18 giant centipedes, in groups of 3-4: SZ S; AL N; AC 9; MV 150’; HD 1 or 2 HP; HP 2(x9), 1(x9); #AT 1; Dmg n.a. Special attacks: poison (+4 to save).

##### 3-163d: Fungal Forest

* All of the open areas, both above and below the cliff, are filled with specimens of colossal mushrooms that grow 10’ to 15’ in height.
	* All of the colossal species in the new flora appendix are found here: orange lamps, white ribs, blue trumpets, eye-openers, cloud caps, and white bulbs.
	* Paths allowing relatively normal movement are marked with dashes.
	* Outside a paths, the forest is densely packed; half movement rate.
	* In the forest direction is quite difficult to maintain (roll 6d4+2 under WIS or make a tracking check, to maintain the proper direction).
	* There is a 5’ gap between the cavern walls and the edge of the fungal forest, so it can be circumnavigated by hugging the cave walls, but the mushrooms grow right up to the cliff and water edges.

Searching the Fungal Forest: 
* Nothing of interest will be found on the path.
* For each turn foraging in the forest, 1 in 6 chance of finding something interesting:
