### 3-164: Lake

* The Seamly Run (3-230) forms a small lake of clear water before the falls at 3-164b.
	* About 130’ x 100’, its banks drop off quickly to an average depth of about 40’.
	* The ceiling is high, 40-60’ above the surface of the water. 
	* The water is cold (~55 F) and a current runs towards the falls at 3-164b.
		* Those not suspecting the current will need to paddle, row, or swim hard to reach the jetty at 3-164c (or any part of the beach).
	* A small island (3-164A) lies in its center.
	* Halfway between the two docks, at a depth of 40’, is a solid gold statuette of a Ptah with hammer raised (5,000 gp).
* Two giant crabs make their home in the lake.
	* They are hungry and have a 50% chance to attack anything moving across the lake.
	* They are intimidated by light, and can be driven away for 1d6 rounds if bright light (torch, light spell, etc.) is shined directly in their eyes.
		* The beastmen bring chum for the crabs when they cross the lake.
	* If they attack a boat, there is a 15% capsize chance, reduced to 5% if at least one person focuses only on keeping the boat upright.

2 giant crabs: SZ L; AL N; AC 3; MV 90’; HD 3; HP 24, 22; #AT 2; Dmg 2-8/2-8. Special attacks: surprise on 1-4.

X / 22
X / 24

##### 3-164a: Sandy Island

* Rising 5’ above the surface of the lake, this small island is the peak of a rock formation which has acquired a 2" deep coating of sand on top.
	* Several skeletons and a few piles of rusting metal are visible on the island.
		* The skeletons are bare.
		* Piles of metal: a badly damaged suit of splint mail (AC 6 instead of AC 4), a magic shield +2, and several useless piles of rusted armor.
		* Digging in the sand for 2-4 turns: white and green glass activation squares, a deep blue spinel (750 gp), 4 aquamarines (100 gp each), a black pearl (500 gp).
	* Each of the giant crabs has a 50% chance of resting on the isle at the time., ready to scuttle forth to attack any who land on their favored resting ground.
		* Lingering on the island attract the crabs’ attention: the first arrives in 5 rounds, and the second 3 rounds after that. They can be deterred for 1d4 rounds by bright light at this location.

2 giant crabs (50%) (see 3-164).

##### 3-164b: Falls

* The Seamly Run drops 25’ over a natural granite dam, producing noise and spray. 
	* Unsuspecting swimmers or boaters may be swept over by the current if they come within 30’ of the Falls.

##### 3-164c: Northern Dock

* Here a stone jetty extends into the dark lake.
	* Hammered into the sand-and-stone ‘beach’ near the jetty are 2 torch-holders, with fresh but un-lit torches in them.
	* Tethered to the jetty are two old and worn skiffs, with 2 oars per boat.
		* Each skiff seats five medium creatures.

##### 3-164d: Side Cave

* The ceiling of this side cave is 10’ above the surface of the lake.
* A 4’-radius hole in the ceiling of the side-cave leads up to 3-171.
* On the floor of the lake at this point, 20' below water, is a wooden chest.
	* 9,971 ancient silver pennies, a map ruined by water, a potion of waterbreathing (new), and a ring of swimming. 

##### 3-164e: Southern Dock and Rowboat 

* Identical to 3-164c, including jetty and torch-holders, but with only one skiff.

### 3-165: Rocky Island

* A rocky island rises out of the Seamly Run (3-230).
	* The island is uneven, rising about 20’ above the river (about equal to the height of the cavern floor to the north).
	* In the center is an almost shapeless statue, worn smooth by moisture and time.
		* The statue is visible from the base of the cliff opposite the river.
		* The statue's head has been knocked off and lies at its feet; the features are vaguely reptilian.
			* Next to head is a small adventurer's stash: leather sack w/ a coil of rope, 10 steel spikes, four torches, 2 smokeless torches (new), a mallet, 2 flasks of oil, and a 6”-tall, ebony statuette of feline friendship (new).
	* A pair of phase salamanders (see new monsters) lairs on the island.

2 phase salamanders (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 3 (or 6); MV 90’, 120’ swimming; HD 5; HP 32, 23; #AT 1; Dmg 2-8. Special attacks: phase (+4 to hit). Special: AC 6 if unable to phase.

X / 23
30 / 32

### 3-166: Elevated Tunnel and Cave

* The 5’-diameter mouth of a cave gapes, 25' above the Seamly Run (3-230).
	* Cave is about even with the cavern floor across the river; difficult to detect unless light is used to inspect the far wall.
	* 10% chance / Turn near the river here that a stirge is spotted flying from the cave.
* Inside are roughly hewn, wet steps leading up to a cavern.
* The cavern is uneven and filled with stalagmites and stalactites.
	* Water trickles down the walls, stairs, and drips over the cave edge into the river.
	* Light reveals a beautiful array of colors and glittering bits of mica.
		* One small stalagmite has coalesced over a sack.
			* Chipped free (noise may bring company from 3-171), it holds 52 gp.

### 3-167: Sloping Cave

* The northern end of the cave rises sharply to a point 15’ higher than the cave mouth.
	* The floor is treacherous and uneven, with flowstone and other mineral formations.
	* A sheen of water glistens when light is deployed. 
	* Close observation reveals some roughly carved steps leading north (and upwards) beneath the flowstone.
	* Secret Door (east): located behind a stone pillar, where the cave is only 5’ high.
		* Obviously worked stone, easy to detect (1 in 4), opens by pushing, but is stuck.

### 3-168: Antechamber

* This tiny room at first appears as nothing but a storage chamber, but is the antechamber to the tomb of Ythak Furl, a minor sorcerer from antiquity.
	* The walls were originally painted, but the paint has run in the humid air and the walls are covered with large, disquieting smears of moist color.
	* Six large (5’-tall) urns and a pile of rotted wood (once a ladder).
		* Urn 1: Hundreds of valueless cave pearls (2”-diameter white calcite formations).
		* Urn 2: A disgustingly soup of rotted mushrooms: -2 penalty to saves for 1 day if ingested.
		* Urn 3: appears to be full of lamp oil, but the oil’s depth is only a few inches (5 flasks), atop contaminated water.
		* Urn 4 (covered): Extremely fine black sand. 
		* Urn 5 (covered): 24 smooth wooden sticks ranging from 18” to 50” in length.
			* One of the 36”-long sticks is a troll femur carved into a flute.
				* A troll flute (new).
				* Gislu the goblin (4-2) would mistake it as the long lost scepter of the goblins (new; actually at 8-69) and seek to claim it. 
		* Urn 6: 1" of water atop gold (once liquid, now hardened; 17,500 gp, 400 lb).
	* Secret Door (east): 7' up the east wall is a a thin panel (1/2” thick, 3’ tall, and 5’ wide). It shatters easily, allowing entry to the inner tomb.

##### 3-168a: Tomb of Ythak Furl

* Ythak Furl, an eccentric sorcerer from the glory days of Arden Vul, commanded his tomb be built in this obscure location.
	* Feeling death approaching, he retired to this chamber with his four trusted servants, whom he slew before taking his own life.
* The inexpertly worked, 20’-tall chamber has developed cracks.
	* Calcite-rich water has oozed and dripped over the centuries, creating a forest of soda straws up to 5’ long and an uneven floor covered with various mineral formations.
	* The vibrant paint of the frescoes has run, forming long streaks of color on the walls.
	* Two stone statues depicting archaic spearmen stand against the west wall.  The corpses of his four servants are neatly stacked by the south wall.
		* The animated stone spearmen (new) and zombified corpses rise to confront any intruders.
		* Combat will inevitably shatter numerous stone soda straws; all should save vs. spells every other round (with a -2 penalty) to keep footing.
	* Ythak Furl’s sarcophagus rests along the east wall.
		* A relatively modest, 6’x3’x3’ stone affair, with an inexpert, vaguely cartoonish, carved image of a man with a strange headdress, too-large eyes, and long-but-wispy mustaches.
		* Inside are the moldy but inert remains of Ythak Furl.
			* 3,814 ancient silver pennies, an ebony wand of magic missiles (command word ‘shoot’ in Mithric; 20 charges), a torc of authority (new), a gilt helmet with eye holes and ear flaps (150 gp), and three potions (poison, extra healing, and fire resistance).
	* Two more large urns stand in the center of the chamber.
		* The first contains pure water; the second held finest hops, now ruined by moisture.

4 zombies: SZ M; AL N; AC 8; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 13, 11, 10, 7; #AT 1; Dmg 1-8. Special: always strike last.

2 Archontean animated constructs - spearmen (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 2; MV 60’; HD 6; HP 37, 34; #AT 1; Dmg 5-10; MR 25%. Special defenses: immune to elemental 
magic, poison, and mind-affecting spells; +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from slashing or piercing weapons.

X / 37
X / 34

### 3-169: Pool

* The walls are wet, and hundreds of soda straws hang from the ceiling.  The entrance to the cave is layered flowstone.
* Much of this room is filled with a 15’-deep, mineral-rich pool of clear water.
	* The water is potable, but tastes slightly off.
	* At the bottom of the pool is ancient, limed-over skeleton (hard to detect, due to mineral formation).
		* The corpse bears a Sortian baculus (no further enchantments; see new magic items), a pouch of 55 gp (fused together by mineral action), and a plugged steel tube containing several pieces of parchment.
			* One reads (formal, ceremonial Mithric): “To operate the floating sage, one must slowly and clearly declaim the first principle of epistemology.”  (alongside) “Dubito, ergo cogito, ergo sum” (I doubt, therefore I think, therefore I am). This is the command word for the Sortian portable sage  in area 3-33.

### 3-170: Last Stand

* A plain cave with the skeletal remains of 6 adventurers and 6 stirges.
	* All twelve sets of remains rise to confront those who stay more than 3 rounds.
	* Badly rusted chain armor; banded mail +1; 66 gp, 79 sp, 35 cp, a large moonstone (60 gp); two potions of healing; a potion of growth; a bone scroll case (25 gp) with a cleric scroll (resist fire, find traps); and a treasure map.

6 skeletons: SZ M; AL N; AC 7; MV 120’; HD 1; HP 8, 7, 6, 5, 5, 4; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special defenses: immune to sleep, charm, hold, and cold; cutting and piercing weapons do half damage.

6 skeletal stirges: SZ S; AL N; AC 7; MV 120’ flying (Class B); HD 1+1; #AT 1; Dmg 2-5. Special defenses: immune to sleep, charm, hold, and cold; cutting and piercing weapons do half damage.

### 3-171: Stirge Lair 

* This cave might be as beautiful as 3-166 if not for centuries of stirge dung covering the stalagmites and mica formations.
	* The ferocious reek of the dung becomes evident only a few steps into the cave (save vs poison or -2 attack due to the smell).
	* Combat likely draws in the skeletons in 3-170, who arrive in 1d3+1 rounds.
	* In the southern tip of the cave is a 4’ hole descending 10’ to the lake (3-164d).

12 stirges: SZ S; AL N; AC 8; MV 30’, 180’ flying (Class B); HD 1+1; HP 8, 7, 7, 6(x3), 5(x3), 4, 4, 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-3. Special attacks: drain blood; attack as 4 HD creatures.

### 3-172: Great Cavern, Southern Portion

* The ceiling of this enormous cavern averages 60-80’ in height.
	* The temperature is cool, and somewhat moist (given the lake and river).
	* Several large rock formations (3-174, 3-178, and 3-179), as well as an ancient parvis and stone chair (3-175 and 3-176), rise above the fungal forest. 
	* The cavern is not completely dark; among the colossal fungal growths are some  that emit a low orange phosphorescence.
		* The areas of the parvis (3-175 to 3-176) and lake (3-164), as well as the tops of the rock formations (3-174, 3-178, 3-179), are pretty dark.
		* Anyone emerging from 3-180, 3-184, or 3-193 will see a low orange glow emerging from a stand of enormous mushrooms (10’ to 15’ tall), above which loom shapeless formations of rock. 
	* The Great Cavern is not completely quiet.
		* There is a hum of insect activity, occasional moaning breezes, plops of liquid from mushroom caps, and an occasional thrashing  of prey being snatched.

Kerbog Khan (see SL12-25) regularly sends dragonfly and explorer automatons to the great cavern to observe the denizens and gather specimens.
* Explorers have a 5% cumulative chance per hour in the cavern to encounter one.
	* d6: 1-2 dragonfly automaton; 3-4: poison dragonfly automaton; 5: basic explorer automaton; 6: bipedal explorer automaton.
	* 33% chance that the Khan is inhabiting the automaton.
	* Once encountered, 75% the automaton will reappear after a significant encounter (provided the PCs did not destroy it!), as the Khan will be interested in how the newcomers have fared.
		* In subsequent encounters, 75% that the Khan is inhabiting the automaton.

1 basic dragonfly automaton of Kerbog Khan (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 4; MV 240’ flying (Class A); HD 1+2; HP 8; #AT 0 Dmg n.a.; MR 25%. Special defenses: immune to 
cold and fire.

1 poison dragonfly automaton of Kerbog Khan (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 4; MV 240’ flying (Class A); HD 1+2; HP 8; #AT 1; Dmg poison (death, or 1-3 turns paralyzation 
with 1-4 round slow on save); MR 25%. Special attacks: poison. Special defenses: immune to cold and fire.

1 basic exploration automaton of Kerbog Khan (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 2; MV 150’; HD 4; HP 29; #AT 2; Dmg 1-4/1-4; MR 40%. Special defenses: immune to cold and 
fire.

1 bipedal exploration automaton of Kerbog Khan (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 2; MV 90’; HD 6; HP 43; #AT 2; Dmg 1-6/1-6; MR 40%. Special defenses: immune to cold and fire.

##### 3-172a: Rockfall Trap 

* Where the eastern caves enter the Great Cavern the beastmen have set a trap.
	* A trip wire 2” off the ground sends a pile of rocks held in a net above the entrance crashing down, 3d6 damage to anyone within five feet of the entrance.
	* The beastmen will reset the trap in 1-4 days.

##### 3-172b: Fungal Forest 

* Most of the cavern is filled with groves of colossal mushrooms that grow 10’ to 15’ in height.
	* All the colossal species in the new flora appendix are found here: , including orange lamps, white ribs, blue trumpets, eye-openers, cloud caps, and white bulbs.
		* Paths are marked with dashes (relatively normal movement). 
		* Without a path, the forest is +1x difficult terrain).
		* Direction is hard to maintain (6d4+2 under WIS, or tracking skills).
	* There is a 5’-wide space between the cavern walls and the side of the fungal forest
		* It is possible to circumnavigate the cavern by hugging the cave walls.
	* The mushrooms grow right up to the cliff and water’s edge.  A careless PC could walk off or into the lake.
* Areas 3-175 and 3-176 are elevated
	* Taking the path from 3-172A to 3-164C, one encounters a 20’-tall stone edifice as they approach the latter. 

Searching the Fungal Forest
* Nothing of interest may be found on the path.
* Each turn spent blundering about in the forest, 1-in-6 chance of finding something.

D20 Result GM Notes

1-2
A head from an ancient statue: heqeti (20%), Thothian (50%), or Set (30%)

Nothing special

Corpse. Roll d10: 
* 1-2: adventurer, 3-6: beastman, 7-8: goblin, 9: varumani, 10: GM’s choice 

The corpse might have usable armor (25%), a normal weapon (25%), a bag of coins worth 10-100 gp (50%), and/or a minor magic item (5%)

5-6

only one person can engage another at a time (without hacking down some mushrooms)

legionary gear. It is most unbecoming, but he has the ear of the Basileus!  If only …. 

Could help those attempting to make the choice of Marius (see 6-154)

The southern fungal forest is home to a spore group of fungal foresters who revere Trocadero, the mad wizard (see 3-176).
* No central lair, may be encountered as random encounters, and/or in specific locations (e.g. 3-176).
* There are a total of 33 fungal foresters; any losses should be subtracted from that total.

(missile/spell defense).

### 3-173: Stirge Cave

* 40’ up the cavern wall is the opening to a small cave
	* The cave is about 4’ tall.  A stirge lair, it is a disgusting mass of feathers, dirt, and excrement.
		* They continuously forage in the Great Cavern, only 1d4 are likely to be  here at any given time. 
		* Buried in the muck is a gold Sortian eye (new), and a necklace of adaptation.

1-4 stirges: SZ S; AL N; AC 8; MV 30’, 180’ flying (Class B); HD 1+1; HP 6, 5, 4, 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-3. Special attacks: drain blood; attack as 4 HD creatures.

### 3-174: House of Ptarmis

* Atop of a rock outcropping 50’ above the floor of the great cavern sits the resting place of Ptarmis, priest of Thoth, discoverer of this cavern, and cultivator of underground flora.
	* It may be difficult for spelunkers below to notice the existence of this mausoleum.
	* The structure on top of the outcropping cannot be seen unless adventurers state they are looking up; are flying; have a way of casting light more than 40’; or possess infravision. 
	* No ladder or indentations exist to aid climbing the outcropping.
* Ptarmis’s mausoleum rises 20' from the flattened top of this outcropping.
	* The ceiling of the cavern is here about 10’ above the roof of the mausoleum.
	* A Greek-style temple 25’ long x 15’ wide with a portico of slim columns supporting the pediment
		* The lintel has elaborate neo-classical Archontean bas-reliefs of a bald priest in robes, carrying an ankh and accompanied by an ibis, moving through a variety of fungal species.
			* Close inspection reveals the bodies of large amphibians (heqeti) lying beneath the fungi.
	* The interior of the mausoleum is open to the air through the pillars
		* 8 very heavy large urns (4' diameter x 4' tall) containing earthy, pungent soil surround a large sarcophagus.
			* Four hold 3’-tall brown pitcher-shaped central flowers (assassin vines)
			* Four hold 3’-diameter brown globes of fungal matter (brown deadly puff ball mushrooms)
			* If the sarcophagus is tampered with, these plants spring to life and attack the desecrators.
			* Buried in the dirt of one of the urns is an intelligent magical short sword named Plantsbane (new).
		* Four skeletons stripped of flesh and usable equipment lie on the pavement
			* Scratched in the dust next a skeletons is ‘Beware’ (Archontean).
		* The sarcophagus is undecorated, save a large inscription on the lid (Mithric)
			* Here rests Ptarmis / loyal servant of Thoth / seeker of hidden ways / who destroyed the loathsome ones / raised his children from spores / and opened this cavern / Those who disturb his sleep / Will be returned to the mulch /from whence they came.
				* An open doors check is required to pry open the lid.
			* Inside, Ptarmis’s mummy case is nestled in four inches of dirt.
				* Elaborate, with solid gold head decorated with lapis, sapphires, and black onyx (intact 10,000 gp, broken up for gems and metal 2000 gp).
				* Inside is Ptarmis' fungal mummy (new).
					* Once the lid of the sarcophagus is moved, Ptarmis opens his case and rises to confront the intruders.
					* GM Note: Ptarmis’s fear aura might drive some intruders to run off the edge of the rock outcrop (4d6 fall damage thanks to the great mushrooms around the outcropping, softening the fall).
				* Inside the case: three gems (500 gp each), 1,079 ancient silver pennies, a pair of keys to the hematite doors (3-177), black and red glass activation squares, a jar with 3 doses of stone salve (new), and an amulet versus undead (7th level).

4 assassin vines (see new monsters): SZ S (effective); AL N; AC 8 (main plant), 4 (tendrils); HD 2 (main plant); HP 14, 13, 11, 10 (main plants), 5 (tendrils); #AT 24; Dmg special. Special attacks: drag; strangulation; digestion.

4 brown deadly puff ball mushrooms (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 10; MV 0’; HD 3 HP; HP 3, 3, 3, 3; #AT 1; Dmg special. Special attacks: spore cloud (stunning for 4-7 rounds).

Ptarmis, the fungal mummy (see new monsters): SZ M; AL LE; AC 1; MV 60’; HD 8; #AT 2; Dmg 1-10/1-10. Special attacks: cause fear in 10’ radius; spores cause madness. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; fungal flesh absorbs 2 HP dmg from each hit. Special: always act last in combat.



### 3-175: Elevated Parvis

* The paved area (parvis) rises about 20’ above the rest of the cavern.
	* Anyone on the parvis has a fairly good view over some parts of the fungal forest.
	* The parvis is made of old, cracked, chipped, and dirty white marble pavers identical to the parvis in 3-177.
	* Black hematite doors lead to 3-177 (see that location for details).
		* Speaking any of the seven secret names of Thoth (see Secreta Secretorum) produces keyholes.  See 3-177 for key location.
	* Four pairs of stone pillars that rise 30’, but do not reach the ceiling of the cavern (unlike their counterparts in 3-177). 

Note: The parvis is one destination for the one-way teleporter in UP-11.
* Arrivals find themselves on the pavement looking north at the gargantuan chair at 3-176.

### 3-176: Pavilion and Gargantuan Chair

* At the northern end of the parvis, three wide steps rise 10' (thus 30' above the cavern floor) to an imposing pavilion.
	* The sides and rear of the pavilion are 20 slim (2’-wide) black marble pillars rising 20’, but not supporting a roof.
	* In the center of the pavilion is a gargantuan seat, 10’ wide by 10’ deep by 10’ high, carved completely out of single block of red jasper.
		* Left and right of the chair are two more 20’-tall, black marble columns.
		* A human in dirty brown robes sits uneasily in the chair (Trocadero).
	* The floor of the pavilion is the same cracked white marble of the parvis, save for the impressive mosaics laid out directly in front of the chair.
		* Ptarmis of Thoth (3-174) installed 3 living mosaics on the pavilion in front of the Great Chair when he discovered this cavern.
		* Mosaic #1: shows the Long Stair near EX-11.
			* 25% chance of a group on the Stair (roll a random encounter for EX). If a beastman, 75% chance they are entering the Halls at 3-189 (EX-11).
		* Mosaic #2: shows 3-163a (a section of the Great Cavern with bars near it).
			* 15% chance of a creature in the scene.
		* Mosaic #3: shows the Glory of Thoth (3-2). 
			* 33% chance of a creature in the scene: if so, it will be 1-3: roll random encounter, 4-5: adventurers, 6: cloaked figures (Set cultists).
		* Trocadero discovered a loose marble paver and stashed his treasure there.
			* 2 potions of plant control, 2 potions of extra healing, 650 gp, an alabaster figurine of a cat (100 gp), a gaudy gold and sapphire ring (300 gp), and a large amethyst (400 gp).
			* The Diary of Trocadero of Newmarket.
			* Trocadero’s Spell Book: Charm person, comprehend languages, detect magic, enlarge, friends, read magic, shield, sleep, unseen servant; ESP, forget, invisibility, magic mouth, mirror image, pyrotechnics, stinking cloud, web; explosive runes, fireball, fly, tiny hut.

Mad Wizard
* Trocadero is a middle-aged human magic user (45 years old) who has been driven insane by the amulet that he found, now believing himself the reincarnation of Ptarmis and the natural custodian of the fungal forest.
* Trocadero spends his time walking through the forest (50%) or sitting on ‘his’ seat (50%).
* He is quite mad, but is not necessarily aggressive.
	* He refers to himself in the third person as Lord Ptarmis, and gestures grandly at his dominion.
	* He listens to petitions so long as the petitioners are polite and offer him respect and deference.
		* Only if the PCs insist on searching the pavilion, or if they show signs of having killed any fungal foresters, or if they insult “Lord Ptarmis” to his face, will Trocadero attack.
	* His first action is to ring a nonmagical silver bell, alerting the fungal foresters, to his need.  They begin arriving (one per round) after 3 rounds. He then uses his spells to maximum effect, alternating between defense and offense. A favorite strategy is to cast fly, shield, and then fireball.

Trocadero of Newmarket, 6th-level male Archontean magic user: SZ M; AL NE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 6; HP 19; #AT 1; Dmg: 1-4 (dagger). Abilities: STR 8, INT 17, WIS 11, DEX 16, CON 12, CHA 13.
* Possessions: dagger; silver bell (25 gp); wand of magic missiles (20 charges); ring of protection from normal missiles (new); scroll (mirror image); 
* The amulet of Ptarmis (new)
* Spells memorized: charm person, enlarge, shield, sleep; invisibility, web; fireball, fly.

6 fungal foresters
* The foresters begin arriving 3 rounds after Trocadero rings his silver bell, once per round in the following order: 

Rnd Type of Forester

1
Spotted fungal forester (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 6; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 4; HP 22; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12

2
Spotted fungal forester (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 6; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 4; HP 23; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12

3
Blue fungal forester (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 6; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 6; HP 34; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12. Special attacks: spore cloud (stun)

4
Yellow fungal forester (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 6; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 6; HP 35; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12. Special defenses: spore cloud (missile/spell defense)

5
Red fungal forester (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 6; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 2; HP 12; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12. Special attacks: explode for 3-18 HP damage

6
Black fungal forester (see new monsters): SZ L; AL N; AC 4; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 8; HP 59; #AT 1; Dmg 4-16. Special attacks: spore clouds (stunning, and missile/spell defense)

### 3-177: Cave of the Hematite Doors

* This large cave has been partially worked and improved.
	* The floor for 35’ in front of the doors has been smoothed and laid with large (5’x5’) pavers of white marble.
	* Six slim (4’ diameter) natural stone pillars extend to the ceiling (turning to unshaped rock at the top 10’ of height).
	* The western wall is finished, once plastered but now only a few shreds of plaster hang on the wall.
	* The east wall is unfinished rock. 
	* The north wall is fitted stone surrounding two enormous (15’) black doors.
		* The wall includes two of the stone pillars (the masonry fitted to 2 pillars).
		* The wall was originally plastered, but, like the west wall, is now entirely bare. 

The Hematite Doors
* The doors are black hematite, inscribed with arcane symbols glowing with a gentle, pulsating purple light.
	* The symbols include an ankh on each door, a feather on the western door and an ibis on the eastern.
	* An inscription runs across the top of both doors (Mithric): “Speak One of the Seven to Enter the Domain of Ptarmis.”
	* No obvious keyholes or locks, but the doors are quite immovable.
	* Anyone who passes successfully through the doors is Blessed for 1 day.
* Speaking aloud one of the seven secret names of Thoth (see Secreta Secretorum) causes a keyhole to appear in each valve.
	* Each requires a large (1’) bronze key (2-23, 3-174, 4-2, 4-158, 5-17, and 5-39).
	* Without the keys, the doors will be almost impossible to open.
	* A knock spell causes the keyholes to appear, but will not open the door.
	* The only alternative to the keys is traversing the eastern tunnels (3-180 to 3-184). 

Arcane Sigils on the Doors
* Tracing any of the sigils on the door produces a magical effect.
	* If the tracer is carries a holy symbol of Set they are blasted for 2-8 lightning.
	* Either ankh grants a blessing (+1 attack and damage for 1d3+3 hours)
	* The feather provides a +4 AC against undead for 4-6 hours
	* The ibis grants comprehend languages for 4-6 hours.
* Once a sigil is traced, it ceases to glow for 1d4 days, before it glows again and can impart its powers.

### 3-178: Accursed Pillar 

* The accursed pillar of Rimmaq-Isfet stands atop a rock formation, 40’ above the floor of the great cavern.
	* It is one of the most ancient icons of the complex, carved millennia ago during the height of heqeti dominance over the Halls.
		* GM Note: A similar pillar may be found at 9-135.
	* It may be difficult for unsuspecting cavern crawlers to notice it unless they are examining the ceiling carefully.
	* Rising 15’ above the formation and 8’ in diameter, the pillar is carved in a spiral fashion with scenes showing the triumph of the heqeti followers of Rimmaq-Isfet.
		* Many of these carvings are now worn to little more than faceless lumps.
		* The column radiates obvious and brooding evil, and a chill 5’ radius around it.
		* Touching the column gates in a keqemander demon to confront the intruders.
		* Examining the carvings causes dizziness, and possibly confusion (save vs. spells to avoid).  Those able to keep their eyes on the pillar may learn something:
			* It takes an hour of scrutiny to learn all of this information.
			* Anyone who gleans even one piece of information gains:
				* A flat 50% chance of recognizing the origin of Kauket artifacts and structures found elsewhere in Halls (e.g. pukel-manders, tears of Kauket, etc.)
				* A flat 33% chance of intuiting a relationship between Rimmaq-Isfet and Kauket.
				* Such an ability does not allow one to intuit specific uses or functions.

D10 Result

1-2
A colossal salamander fills the top of the pillar. It has multiple legs, and an enormous mouth filled with teeth and circled with a ‘beard’ of feelers/tentacles. Three lidless eyes span its massive brow.

3-4
Hopping salamander-headed bipeds wreak destruction on lizards.

5-6
Humans in chains are driven into the maw of a giant amphibian.

7-8
The boundary separating the spiraling narratives is in fact a tongue.

9-10
The heqeti and their slaves seem to be moving towards a ziggurat in a cave.
 

1 keqemander demon (see new monsters): SZ L; AL CE; AC -2; MV 90’, 150’ flying (Class D); HD 8; HP 55; #AT 3; Dmg 1-4/1-4/3-18; MR 40%. Constant abilities: dread (-1 to saves); 
infravision. Special attacks: acid spit (3-10 dmg; 30’ range, every other round); cause fear; darkness (10’ radius); exude acid with chance to degrade armor; use a symbol of discord. 
Special defenses: only hit by magic weapons; half damage from cold, electricity, fire, and gas; become invisible. Special: levitate; telekinesis (4,000 gp weight); project image; teleport without error; 50% chance to gate in either another keqemander or a Type I-IV demon.

### 3-179: Mysterious Hole, w/ access to 5-141

* The rock formation rises another 20’ in height from the accursed pillar (3-178).
	* Its pinnacle (60’ above the cavern floor, 10’ from the ceiling) has a 5’-diameter hole extending downward 80’ before opening into a small unmapped cavern.
	* This cave (20’ wide, 8’ to 15’ high) snakes over uneven rocky floors 80’ towards the north. It is cool and dry, a suitable place for resting.
		* In the extreme north corner is another 5’ hole extending down 170’ to 5-141.
		* A midnight rose plant grows next to the hole (flora).
		* The cave contains a cache of food.
			* 4 lb of dried fruit (unusual but edible), 1 lb of dried meat (now leathery), 2 orange plastic flasks of water.  Discarded beside the cache are two 1” rudishva lesser power supplies (3 charges each).
			* Carved on the wall near the cache is (Varumani Semi-glyphik) “Betrayed by the kaliyani, the varumani flee. Our Lords help us not. They are thrown down. Let us follow the thegn.” 

GM Note
* The holes that connect 3-179 to 5-141 were delved by the varumani as they sought escape from the collapse of the rudishva hegemony over the halls.
* The note points to the culpability of the kaliyani in this disaster.
* Alerting the current troll thegn (7-30) to the content and location of the inscription gives +20% initial reaction bonus, and a reward of 250 gp.

### 3-180: Damp Caverns

* The walls of these three caves are slick with moisture, and the temperature in them is about 10 degrees warmer than the surrounding caves.  The floors are muddy sand and gravel.
	* At A, the beastmen have placed a broken spear haft with a decomposing baboon head impaled on it as a warning.
	* A column of magical fire crackling merrily at B has attracted 3 fire mephits, who frolic at C. 
		* The mephits smoke sticks made of dried and pressed eye-opener mushrooms (flora). They are dressed in strange costumes: heavy purple velvet smoking jackets, orange top hats, and ankle boots with 3” heels. 
		* They have a silver case (25 gp) containing 12 eye-opener ‘cigarettes’, which  function just as the fresh variety (flora).

3 fire mephits: SZ M; AL NE; AC 5; MV 120’, 240’ flying (Class B); HD 3+1; HP 23, 22, 20; #AT 2; Dmg 2-4/2-4. Special attacks: flame shroud around body; breath weapon 3/day; heat metal 1/day; magic missile (2 missiles) 1/day; gate (25% chance, once per hour). 
* If slain, each fire mephit’s heart will coalesce into a fire opal (100 gp)
* Mephit skin may also be sold to wizards for magical research.

## Level 3: 181 - 195

### 3-181: Hidden Side Cave

* The entrance to this side cave is a 3’-diameter hole located 5’ above the tunnel floor.
	* It is easily found by those proceeding slowly or cautiously.
* The tunnel is small and narrow at first, but opens up to 5’ wide by 8’ tall before emerging in a 10’ by 10’ cave.
	* Inside the cave is the body of an elven magic user, long dead and decomposed.
		* A wooden staff capped with iron, leather pouch with a 50 gp beryl and a 100 gp aquamarine. 
	* A colony of 4 feral house cats led by the former familiar of the wizard make their nest here.
		* They prowl in 3-172 for insects and other small prey, and hide in this cave to escape larger predators. It might be possible to adopt one or more of them.
		* The familiar is female, had sex with a tomcat from the Bast temple, had kittens after the mage's death, while waiting here.

4 wild cats: SZ S; AL N; AC 5; MV 180’; HD 1; HP 6, 4, 3, 2; #AT 3; Dmg 1-2/1-2/1-2. Special attacks: rear claw rakes; surprise 3 in 6. Special defenses: only surprised 1 in 6.

### 3-182: Empty Cave

* This cave contains obvious signs of animal traffic leading towards 3-183.

### 3-183: Rock Reptile Lair

* This cave is the lair of 3 rock reptiles that enjoy hunting in the Great Cavern (3-172).
	* Their lair proper is in the western protrusion.
		* Two 10-lb silver ingots (50 gp each), a misshapen stone head of a snake-creature (one of the bas-reliefs from 3-192f), a potion of flying, and one boot from a pair of elven boots (the other is at 1-18).
	* 50% chance that some reptiles are present (d10): 1-4=1 rock reptile, 5-8=2 rock reptiles, 9-10= 3 rock reptiles.
	* The beastmen employ a testudo formation to move swiftly through this cave and  offer fresh meat as an offering to allow them to pass.

1-3 rock reptiles: SZ M (8’); AL N; AC 3; MV 60’; HD 5+8 HP; HP 42, 40, 38; #AT 1; Dmg 9-12. Special attacks: surprise on 3 in 6. Special defenses: chameleon powers.

X / 42
X / 40

### 3-184: Cave-In

* An enormous, impassable rock fall blocks the passage.
* Just beyond the cave-in is a short tunnel to 3-172, exiting 25’ above the floor of the Great Cavern.

### 3-185: Lost Goblins

* The remnant of a goblin expeditionary party lurks in this cave.
	* Only three goblins remain, under the command of the charismatic sub-chief, Bellringer (fluent in Archontean), and they are nervous and excitable.
	* They are quite willing to parlay, especially if offered food and assistance.
	* The bodies of three dead companions are stashed down the narrow passageway. 
	* 35 sp, 61 cp, and two dead giant centipedes (poison glands could be extracted).

The Goblins’ Story
* Flushed with a minor gladiatorial victory at the Arena (6-68), the team of goblins decided they were fated to discover the whereabouts of Gribble, King Weskenim’s missing brother.  They left the Arena area (6-67), climbed to 4-161, and located the stairs to 3-172 (via 4-159).
	* Gribble is currently in the prison of Set at 3-105.
* Once in the Great Cavern (3-172), Bellringer and his men were ambushed by the beastmen of the Long Range Cavern Patrol (3-154) and almost annihilated.
	* They fled east, and located this cave, where they plan their next move. They gladly trade information for food and assistance in returning to 4-159.

2 goblins: SZ S; AL LE; AC 6; MV 60’; HD 1-1; HP 5, 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6.

Bellringer, sub-chief (as hobgoblin): SZ S; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 1+1; HP 8; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (military pick). Possessions: military pick, chime of opening (3 charges).

### 3-186: Crossroads and a Giant Boulder

* A giant boulder (15' high, 22' wide) rests on the floor of this crossroads.
	* Might not be immediately obvious the boulder isn't connected to the ceiling (20-25' above).
	* Subtle chiseled footholds on the north face of the boulder allow easy access to the top of the boulder.
		* Here is a a flattened space, the cold ashes of a cooking fire, and several battered iron pots and cauldrons.
		* A small patch of aqua vitae mushrooms (flora) has taken root in some dirt and dust accumulated in a shallow depression on the rock.
			* Currently there are 8 ripe mushrooms. Every 1-3 months a new crop of mushrooms will spring up here.
		* The campsite on the boulder is relatively safe, with a good view of all approaching tunnels, and of the hematite doors at 3-177 (which are clearly visible due to the magical light there).

### 3-187: Empty Cave

* This cave is little more than a widening of the tunnel.
	* Two beastmen corpses lie moldering in the small spur to the north. 
		* Badly decomposed and carry nothing of value. 
		* 10% a carcass creeper is found here.

1 carcass creeper (10% chance): SZ L; AL N; AC 3 (head) or 7 (body); MV 120’; HD 3+1; HP 20; #AT 8; Dmg nil. Special attacks: paralysis.

### 3-188: Crossroads

* Three tunnels converge at this point, and a fourth appears to lead to the north.
	* The fourth passage leads to a small cave whose far wall has been smoothed flat and carved into a Sortian face (new), activated by placing Sortian eyes in the empty eye sockets. 
		* Combinations are standard, except:
			* Gold-Gold: Teleportation
				* All within 5’ are teleported to area 6-48
			* Gold-Sapphire: A permanent magic mouth speaks (Mithric):
				* All those with the spark must be trained, regardless of their origin. The empire will be better for it. Once you have found a suitable recruit, visit the sanctum so that training may commence. Recall that proper vision comes only with yellow or blue eyes. I, Priscus the Hekate, have spoken! Oh, and if exigency requires it, you may seek our outpost along the wall of the chasm, near where the falls crash to the floor. Do not alert the Theosophs to your passage!
					* GM Note: This message is a hint as to the original, egalitarian message of the Sortians, and especially Priscus Pulcher. The outpost is to be found at areas 9-58 to 9-64.
		* This cave is also the destination for the Sortian face in 6-48. 

### 3-189 (aka EX-11): Secret Door to Exterior

* This secret door deposits travelers outside the Halls, onto the upper reaches of the Long Stair at a point 1,150’ from the valley floor or 350’ below the plateau.
	* The door is stone, easy to discern from the inside (1 in 3).
	* It is the primary route used by the beastmen of the Long Range Cavern Patrol (3-154) to access the ruined city of Arden Vul (AV) and the valley of the Swift River. 
* Trackers will easily notice signs of traffic here, particularly of small feet (the beastmen). Much graffiti is scrawled on the walls near the secret door.

D20 Graffiti GM Notes

1-3
A random name, e.g., Jimmy Sharp-Eyes, Gaius Christopher, Azgallatu, Ceras, etc.

The GM should use names of NPCs known to (or rivals of) the PCs.
Language: varies by ethnicity of author

4
Beware the Lake. Foul things live there!

A reference to 3-164 and the giant crabs dwelling therein. 
Language: Dwarvish runes

5
Door impenetrable. Move instead to pyramid. Forge of Zhorak to find!

A reference to the legendary dwarven smith Zhorak, whose forge (8-100) modern 
dwarves would dearly love to locate.
Language: Dwarvish runes

6
Humans Go Home! (with a skull painted nearby)

Beastman propaganda (for beastmen, see 3-138 to 3-162). 
Language: large, simplistic Archontean script

7
To Gnath: walking animals be too mighty. Me take boys home. [Signed] Ragnar 

A warning about the beastmen (3-138 to 3-162) from a Wiskin adventurer. 
Language: crude, agrammatical Archontean

8
‘The Priscians have returned’ [in Archontean with big block capitals] and ‘Fool of a First
Circle apprentice. Use discretion!'

A clue that the Priscians have occupied the old Sortian outpost (see 9-58 to 9-64). 
Language: Mithric

9
Foul sorcery in the big cave. The flying fire-dealer cannot be stopped.

An opaque reference to Trocadero of Newmarket (3-176) although PCs may think it refers to a dragon.
Language: Archontean

10
Ptarmis found this cavern and built this door. May Thoth reward him.

An ancient reminder of the role of Ptarmis (now a fungal mummy at 3-174) in developing the Great Cavern (3-163 and 3-172). 
Language: Mithric

11
Nerub Null is a big fat idiot. May he choke on his silver eyes!

A reference to one of the leaders of the modern Priscian cult (9-64) and to the Sortian eyes. 
Language: Thorcin

12
Hareth: bear right through the caves and meet us by the lake.

An adventuring note, with the important clue about how to reach the Great Cavern (3-172) and lake (3-164).
Language: Thorcin

13
[a recently-painted, but crude, image of a black boar with an ibis in its mouth]

Iconography of the cult of Set (the boar) and that of Thoth (the ibis). A hint that Set is 
active again (see 3-90 and Level 4)

14
Don’t trust the beastmen. Their ‘mother’ is a witch!

Partly true, as Deino (3-158) is a dangerous sorcerer. But the beastmen (3-138 to 3-162) are lawful and generally keep their word. 
Language: Archontean

15
Those yellow-spotted blue mushrooms pack a dangerous punch! But with them we found a 
hidden door!

A reference to the eye-opener variety of giant mushrooms (see new flora). 
Language: Archontean

16
Watch out for the walking mushrooms. Some of them explode!

A reference to the red variety of fungal forester (see new monsters), which might be 
encountered in the great cavern (3-163 and 3-172). 
Language: Wiskin

17
There’s a route to the lower caverns high up on the west wall of the big cavern.

A useful hint about the route to Levels 4 and 6 viathe ledge at 3-193.
Language: Archontean

18
We have it on good information that there are three major unplundered tombs accessible from the big cavern. One is under the waters of the lake.

A reference to areas such as 3-168A, 3-174, 3-192, and 3-197. The rumor about a tomb under the lake is false. 
Language: Archontean

19
To reach the temple of Thoth, head north through the Great Hall and turn left through 
the tombs. Look for the statue.

An accurate, if general, description of the route to 3-71, via 3-123 and 3-15. 
Language: Elvish

20
The LRCP Owns These Caves!

Propaganda from the Long Range Cavern Patrol (3-154). 
Language: Archontean

### 3-190: Storage Cave

* The beastmen use this dry cave to store supplies for their patrols.
	* A coffin-sized stone container sits in the southwestern corner with an ancient wooden lid with the faint imprint of the insignia of the 3rd Cohort of the Imperial Tagmata (a mailed fist) still visible. 
		* The lid is shut with a padlock smeared with contact poison (save vs. poison or die; if save is made, still take 1-12 damage).
			* The lid could easily be easily removed by chopping off the hinges.
		* Inside: 10 javelins, 10 torches, six gourd canteens filled with water, dried food sufficient for 5 persons for a week, three glass flasks of oil, and a leather pouch with 5 dried specimens of red veil mushrooms (flora).
	* Encounter
		* 25% chance a beastman patrol is present.
		* 25% chance a carcass creeper has been attracted by the smell of prey.
		* If both are present, they will be in combat (noisy and evident to those approaching from the south).

6 beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 8, 7, 7, 6, 6, 5; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spears; short swords; short bows.

1 beastman sergeant (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 4; MV 90’: HD 2+2; HP 15; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6 or 2-5. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spear; war hammer.

 1 carcass creeper: SZ L; AL N; AC 3 (head) or 7 (body); MV 120’; HD 3+1; HP 21; #AT 8; Dmg nil. Special attacks: paralysis.

### 3-191: Empty Cave?

* First impressions suggest an empty natural cave.
	* The western wall is illusory (marked by dotted lines).
		* A tracker might (+5% chance) notice tracks leading towards the illusory wall.
		* Klisko Lightfingers, a human illusionist, was badly burned in the battle that took place in 3-192, and retreated here in shock to recuperate.
			* Most of his possessions, including 3/4 of his spell book, were destroyed in the conflagration.  He cast hallucinatory terrain to make the room appear smaller.  Behind the illusion, he applied a medicinal paste to his burned face and scalp and fell asleep on his bedroll.
			* Klisko will be cautious, backing away, mumbling vague threats and warnings about fire.
			* If cured, he pretends to join his rescuers but betrays them as soon as possible. 
			* Klisko freely relates what happened in 3-192, (including the fire trap) hoping to ingratiate himself with his rescuers.
			* He and his team knew one of the secret names of Thoth (#4: Light of Comprehension) and suspected the location of the tomb of Lycandus (3-197). He might barter this information for assistance in exiting the Halls.

Klisko Lightfingers, 5th-level male Archontean illusionist: SZ M; AL NE; MV 120’; AC 5; HD 5; HP 4 (Max 14); #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (throwing daggers). Abilities: STR 10, INT 17, WIS 14, DEX 
17, CON 11, CHA 13.
* Possessions: backpack; 1 day’s rations; empty water skin; 6 throwing daggers; bracers of defense (AC 8); a pouch with 45 gp; a bag of silver shavings (110 gp); and his badly burned spell book.
* Memorized spells: the only spell he has left is light.
* His badly burned spell book (remaining): detect invisibility, phantasmal force, and hypnotic pattern.

### 3-192: Hall of Unease

* An elaborately carved and decorated chamber predating the Archonteans, though substantially modified and redecorated on numerous occasions.
	* Originally accessed through stone doors to 3-172; they are now buried under several tons of rubble from a cave-in caused by the adventuring parties.
	* A secondary access route was gnawed or delved by unknown hands some centuries past; it leads by a twisty path to the tunnels near 3-188 and 3-191.
* The chamber contains an ancient, timeworn statue, six decapitated bas-relief figures, and five sarcophagi of more recent (but still centuries-old) vintage.
	* The statue is badly eroded by time, its features hard to discern.  Bipedal and human-sized, its head looks strangely large and nonhuman.
		* Highly faceted amber gems serve as over-sized eyes (500 gp each).
		* Touching the gems causes a roaring noise for 3 rounds before a random effect is unleashed.  Can be provoked multiple time.
	* The bas-reliefs are ancient, and extremely worn.
		* Along the eastern ell are six 2’ daises supporting bas-relief figures of salamander-like humanoids. The heads of 5 of the 6 have been struck off.
		* The sixth is intact, and represents a bipedal figure with bulbous eyes, slit nose, and an oversized mouth (a heqeti).
		* The walls featured low bas-reliefs of figures struggling in coiling, writhing masses; erosion and desecration obscure them, but they seem vaguely reptilian.
			* In a few places it seems as if large snakes or lizards are devouring multitudes of smaller figures.
			* Studying the walls for more than a few of rounds (e.g. searching for secret doors) provokes a sense of unease (-1 to saves vs fear for 1d4 hours).
	* The three sarcophagi in the center of the chamber are ancient, dating to the earliest period of the Archontean Empire (4' tall x 6' long x 3' wide).
		* All three lids were smashed long ago, and the remains dispersed.
		* The exteriors are carved in a simplistic style with rude scenes of dragons devastating an idealized countryside.
	* The two sarcophagi that against the northeast and southeast walls are more recent, dating to the attempted recolonization of the Halls some 250 years ago.
		* Plain sides and an elaborate, well-carved gisant of an imperial legionary on their top.
		* The northeastern sarcophagus is smashed open, its contents dispersed.
		* The southeastern one is intact (open doors check and a prybar open).
			* Inside is a skeleton of an Archontean legionary, still accoutered in tarnished mail and conical helm, with a serrated sword.
			* The skeleton clambers out of the sarcophagus and attacks. 
			* 6 ancient octagonal platinum coins, a bone scroll case with 3 spells (spider climb, continual light, and gust of wind), and a jade necklace worth 275 gp.
* The Hall has been the site of a destructive battle in the very recent past.
	* 9 adventurer corpses litter the room, 6 badly scorched by tremendous heat.
		* The most badly burned body lies directly in front of the statue.
		* The 3 less badly scorched corpses were crouched behind the sarcophagi in the center of the chamber when they died.
	* Two adventuring parties got into an argument.  In the midst, one thief manipulated the statue, provoking the fireball that annihilated the parties and caused the cave-in over the exit to 3-172.
	* On the dead adventurers: a total of 143 sp, 71 gp, 219 cp; a hammer +1; a dagger +2; a potion of fire resistance; a potion of climbing; usable long swords (x3), mace, daggers (x6); a lump of melted silver (56 gp, formerly a statuette); and various charred bits of equipment.

D6 Effect
* 1-2) Two bolts of electricity strike one of the PCs, inflicting 2-8 each
* 3-4) A cloud of acidic gas emerges from the ceiling. Everyone in the hall must save vs poison (1d10 on success, failed w/in 5 of the target number 2d8 damage and blindness for 1d4 turns, fail by 5 or more, take 3d8 damage and blindness for 1d4 days
* 5-6) Fireball at level 9 (9d6)

1 skeleton: SZ M; AL N; AC 7; MV 120’; HD 1; HP 7; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special defenses: immune to sleep, charm, hold, and cold; cutting and piercing weapons do half damage.

### 3-193: Set’s Landing

* Twenty-five feet up the west wall of the great cavern is a small landing leading west to a 5’-wide passageway.
	* The landing has a low balustrade of simple stone columns to which is attached a long rope ladder (coiled, but reaching the cavern floor when unrolled).
	* Three Set guardsmen with bows lounge on the landing, watching the cavern.
* The landing is the only sure way to access Level 4 (via 3-212) from the southern part of Level 3, and the priests of Set are increasingly anxious to control it.
	* If combat breaks out here, there is a 50% chance that the guardsmen in 3-195 hear and arrive to aid their comrades in 3-5 rounds.

4 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 17, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

### 3-194: Storage Chamber

* A small chamber, unpainted and rather drab.
	* Twelve large sacks line the north and south walls, containing various dried mushrooms harvested from the the Great Cavern.
		* Not worth much in absolute terms, but valuable as food and pharmacological resources to any of the intelligent communities in the Halls.
		* Recognizable as stolen from Set if sold in the Forum of Set.
	* At the bottom of one sack is a silver plaque engraved with a sheep’s head (50 gp).
		* A symbol of the 2nd legion (Sheep’s Head Rangers), which foundered in Arden Vul 250 years ago).

### 3-195: Cozy Chamber

* The narrow corridor from 3-194 ends in this large chamber, with a high ceiling painted with stars in the shape of the manta constellation.
	* By the east wall, a fireplace crackles with burning mushroom stalks.
	* Four leather easy chairs (50 gp each), a silk settee (55 gp), a plush green carpet (25 gp), a set of brass candelabra and eating utensils (35 gp total), a keg of brandy (25 gp), and two barrels of water are arranged in front of the fireplace.
		* Stephania, high priestess of Set (4-51), has furnished the room in a relatively luxurious manner as a ‘reward’ to her minions for taking up this distant and dangerous posting.
		* Still, the guardsmen posted here are jumpy and alert, with a 20% chance of fleeing to the north if they hear loud and/or ominous sounds emanating from the east.
	* Several simple wooden benches, one battered easy chair, and two barrels of water complete the chamber.

3 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

1 Set sergeant (see new monsters), as a 5th-level Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 60’; HD 5; HP 35; #AT 1, Dmg 3-8 (mace +1), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special 
defense: fanaticism. Possessions: Set armor (see Arden Vul items) and wooden shield; footman’s mace +1; spear; light crossbow with 20 bolts.

1 Set acolyte (see new monsters), as a 3rd-level Archontean cleric of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 19; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow).
* Possessions: Set armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (see new magic items); and a silver holy symbol of Set. 
* Spells prayed for: command, cure light wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good; hold person, silence 15’ radius.

## Level 3: 196 - 210

### 3-196: Empty (?) Cave

* This 35’-tall, river-carved cavern appears to be empty save for dripping stalactites and a thin layer of sand. The cave is quite damp and moist.
	* The passage to Lycandus’s tomb (3-197) is 25’ up on the south wall, concealed by an illusion (can't be dispelled by less than a 15th-level mage).
	* Past the illusion, in the south-leading tunnel, an enormous complex knot is carved on the tunnel wall (a symbol of the Sortians).
	* The door to 3-197 is worked stone without any evident keyhole.
		* GM Note: Successfully manipulating the pillars at 3-209 allows PCs to see through this illusion.
		* An invisible stalker waits here, still hoping to fulfill its Sortian master’s last wishes. It attacks intruders but won’t pursue outside the cave.

1 invisible stalker: SZ L; AL N; AC 3; MV 120’; HD 8; HP 56; #AT 1; Dmg 4-16; MR 30%. Special attacks: surprise on 1-5. Special defenses: invisibility.

X / 56

### 3-197: Tomb of Lycandus

* Both doors to the chamber are stone, with Sortian faces carved onto them.
	* A close-cropped, bearded male face of late middle age, complete with age lines, crow’s feet, blemishes, and empty sockets where the eyes should be.
	* If activated with gold and/or silver Sortian eyes, the doors unlock, and are impregnable otherwise.
* The tomb proper is a glittering rococo display of gold, silver, and precious gems.
	* Entering triggers a magic mouth to bellow (Mithric) "Lycandus, Prince of Princes, Master of the Eyes, lies here in eternal glory amid his rightful possessions.  Let him be, lest you incur the wrath of Priscus Pulcher, who protects his friends even unto death."
	* Plastered walls show gilt images of nondescript humans doing ordinary activities; with eyes of sapphires.
	* The ceiling has an elaborate fresco of winged beings cavorting in the clouds.
	* An enormous sarcophagus carved from a solid block of porphyry lies in the center of the room, 18’ long, by 9’ wide, incised with arcane symbols filled with silver.
		* Within is only a bare skeleton.
	* Stone tables on the west and south are laden with piles of gold and silver coins and  serving pieces.
	* All of these riches are illusory (powerful, -3 to saves).
		* The ancient Sortians eschewed gaudy display and hierarchy; the illusion is an obvious incongruity to any familiar with the history of the Sortians.
		* One can carry away the glamoured wealth: 15,000 ancient gold solidi, 20,000 ancient silver pennies, 10-20 pieces of silver plate, 100 small sapphires from the walls, etc.  After 24 hours this wealth turn turns to dross, glass, etc.
* For those who disbelieve the illusion, there is only a dusty stone chamber empty save for the two stone tables and a bas-relief covering the south wall.
	* The bas-relief is of a huge and sinuous dragon resting its head on the shoulder of a handsome, bearded young man dressed in Archontean garb.
	* The ‘table’ on the south wall is just bare stone.
	* The ‘table’ on the west wall is actually the sacrcophagus of Lycandus.
		* Inscription (Mithric) "A Companion of Priscus and Fellow of the Sortian League, Lycandus the Explorer lies here. His delving brought him fame, while his mastery of the Canticle brought him wisdom. Eschewing riches, Lycandus commanded this simple resting place for his earthly bones. "
		* Beneath the lid (open doors): a skeleton (not actually Lycandus) in dusty clothing, with an elaborate platinum pendant in the shape of a knot of platinum wires (400 gp).
		* Secret compartment in south end: hard to detect, a tiny stone button opens.
			* Inscribed (Mithric) on the south end is "Beware! Lycandus is watching", trapped with explosive runes (6d4+6).  (level x 10)% for mages to notice the runes, half that for thieves.
			* Inside is Lycandus' skeleton, with a platinum torc (1,750 gp) with the inscription ‘Sortian’ on it in Mithric, and a gold ring inset with a white pearl (a ring of spider climbing (new), activated by “Lycandus”).  By the skeleton’s side is an intelligent enchanted sword, with a fine troll-skin handle named Scorcher (new). 
	* The central sarcophagus real, but plain, ugly, and undecorated.
		* If Lycandus’s true tomb is opened, the skeleton within will climb from its resting place and lay a curse on the intruders.
			* It choses a target and whispers softly in Mithric to them.  Their STR drops to 3 for 12 Turns.  It follows them (within 30'), and reapplies the curses after it expires.
			* If destroyed, it reassembles after 4d6 Turns (if ground to powder, it takes 4d6 days).  Every 3 days it can teleport to the victim if more than 100 yards away.
			* Dispel magic or Remove curse at 9th level or higher ends the curse skeleton, crumbling it to dust.

### 3-198: Dry Alcove

* The damp river caves and tunnels lead past a dry alcove at this point.
	* The alcove is about 10’ above the floor of the cave and is occupied by two lizardmen.
		* They are badly lost, having somehow navigated a route from SL-4 to 4-159, and thence to 3-212a. They will be willing to do almost anything in return for directions home.
	* An odd symbol (four interlocked circles with a square’s four corners meeting at the centers of the circles) is inscribed on the southwestern wall in dull brown paint.
		* It grants protection from scrying and dampness: any who scramble into the alcove will be effectively invisible to those who pass by in the corridor (and to indirect forms of scrying), and will be dry to boot!

2 bedraggled lizardmen (10% chance): SZ M; AL N; AC 4; MV 60’, 120’ swimming; HD 2+1; HP 13, 10; #AT 1 or 3; Dmg 1-6 (club) and 1-6 (javelin), or 1-2/1-2/1-8. Possessions: clubs; 
javelins; shields.

### 3-199: Mushrooms

* The cave is damp and humid, with stalactites and stalagmites.
	* Between the rock formations are many 3’- to 10’-tall mushrooms, amid which are 3 shriekers (bright blue caps) placed by the fungal foresters of 3-202. 
		* The shriekers will alert the inhabitants of 3-202.

3 shriekers: SZ L; AL N; AC 7; MV 10’; HD 3; HP 20, 17, 13; #AT 0; Dmg nil. Special attacks: noise.

### 3-200: Colossal Crystals

* The entrance to this cavern is 10’ above the floor of the lake.
* Geothermal heat vents make the cave is extremely humid and hot (~120F, ~100% humidity).
	* As a result, it is filled with massive beams of selenite gypsum which crisscross the chamber like pick-up sticks, some are 3’ in diameter and over 25’ long.
	* The giant crystals are easily broken with iron tools, but so soft that they can be scratched by thumbnails.
* Two selenite guardians, whose crystalline speech is unintelligible without magic, confront those clambering among the crystal formations.
	* They politely demand the departure of the intruders from their ‘garden’; if ignored (or not understood), they attack.
	* The difficult terrain and hot and humid environment, gives -2 to all combat rolls while in the cave.

2 selenite guardians (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 2; MV 30’ on dirt, 60’ on selenite; HD 6; HP 41, 37, 36; #AT 2; Dmg 2-8/2-8. Special defenses: regenerate 2 HP/round near selenite; immune to fire and water; take only 1 HP from edged weapons.
* The bodies of a slain selenite guardian yields selenite crystals worth 6-600 gp.

### 3-201: Humid Mushroom Cave

* This large cave is extremely humid and warm (although not as hot as 3-200), and smells strongly of minerals. It is filled with medium-sized giant mushrooms (3’-7’ tall). 
* The tunnel northwest leads down a flight of roughly hewn stairs to a slightly wider area, lit by a faint blue light.
	* The light is emitted by a wizard’s staff of blue light stuck into the sand (new).
		* Although useful, there is no way to stop the emission of the blue light (30’ radius), short of covering the staff entirely.

### 3-202: Fungal Foresters

* This cave is warm and moist (though not as much as 3-200 or 3-201).
	* A layer of river silt has made it a natural place a large colony of giant mushrooms.
	* A small colony of 12 fungal foresters makes its home here.
		* The foresters placed the shriekers in 3-199, and move to investigate if the shriekers begin to shriek.
	* A pair of dead adventurers moulder in the eastern protrusion.
		* Long sword, rusty chainmail, shield +1, a set of gold-embellished silverware (26 pieces, 340 gp total), a few folios of parchment entitled "Description of the Inn of the Lost" (books). 
	* Secret Door (west, to the lair of the hag in 3-204): unknown to the fungal foresters, difficult to detect, opens from this side by pressing a small button on the floor.

4 spotted fungal foresters (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 6; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 4; HP 27, 25, 22, 21; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12.

2 blue fungal foresters (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 6; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 6; HP 36, 34; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12. Special attacks: spore cloud (stun).

2 yellow fungal foresters (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 6; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 6; HP 36, 35; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12. Special defenses: spore cloud (missile/spell defense).

1 red fungal forester (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 6; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 2; HP 13; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12. Special attacks: explode for 3-18 HP damage.

1 black fungal forester (see new monsters): SZ L; AL N; AC 4; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 8; HP 51; #AT 1; Dmg 4-16. Special attacks: spore clouds (stunning, and missile/spell defense).
* Possessions: a fibrous pouch (4-9 spores for exotic mushroom species (choose from flora)).

### 3-203: Sandy Cave

* The western portion of this cave features a black sand beach formed by run-off from the Seamly Run.
	* The cave rises a bit in height towards the east, where it is humid and warm.
	* The northern knob has a 15’ deep pool of clear water  connected to the Seamly Run by a small tunnel.

### 3-204: Lair of the Hag

* The underwater tunnel from 3-205 leads to a dry beach and the lair of Androsia, the greenhag.
	* The cave varies in height, from 5’ near the water tunnel, to 15’ at the eastern end. 
	* The cave is lit by smoky torches, and contains a large pile of rags, a huge cauldron bubbling with a foul brew, and a large stone chest.
		* An amethyst (75 gp) and peridot (210 gp) lie at the bottom of the cauldron.
	* A taut sheet of blood-soaked canvas is stretched between four iron stakes
		* On the sheet is tied, spread-eagle, a prisoner (50% beastman, 25% human adventurer, 25% goblin) who has been tortured to death.
	* The eyes of Nertet-Indra (the statue at 3-206) have been mounted on the wall in a vague image of a face.
		* The eyes are almond shaped, of blue glass, with a black iris painted on them. They detect vaguely as magical.
	* Scattered idly around the lair are 3,106 ancient silver pennies, 483 ancient gold solidi, 350 sp and 139 gp.
		* 5 ancient octagonal platinum coins are ground into the floor near the cauldron. 
	* Two potions of extra healing are stashed in one of the southern protuberances.
	* Finally, a bag of holding (150 cubic feet variety) has been thrown carelessly aside among other rags and scraps.
		* Inside it is a scarab of protection and 10 aquamarines (100 gp each).

Androsia
* Here in her lair (25%); on the beach at 3-206 (50%), in the cave of bones at 3-222 (15%), or walking invisibly elsewhere in the complex (10%). 
* She has attracted an entourage of dominated lesser creatures (whom she occasionally devours when other food is scarce).
* 6 famished-looking beastmen serve Androsia here in her lair
	* She also has the scrags in 3-205, more beastmen in 3-221, and the ogres in 3-223.

Androsia the greenhag: SZ M; AL NE; AC -2; MV 120’, 120’ swimming; HD 9; HP 60; #AT 2; Dmg 13-14/13-14; MR 35%. Special attacks: +3 to hit and +6 to damage from great STR; 
surprise on 5 in 6. Special defenses: only surprised on 1 in 20.
* Special, each 1/rd at 9th-level of ability: audible glamer, dancing lights, invisibility, pass without trace, change self, speak with monsters, water breathing, weakness.
* Charm monster 3x/day.

59 / 60

6 enslaved beastman troopers (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 6, 5, 5, 4, 4, 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: tactics. Possessions: ring mail and shield; spears; short swords; short bows.

### 3-205: Pool

* The Seamly Run opens into a fairly wide pool at this point, ranging from 5’ to 25’ deep, with a 10’-wide, 5’-deep ledge abutting the beach (3-206).
	* There is a tunnel to the hag’s lair 15’ below the water on the south side of the pool.
	* 3 scrags (marine trolls) dominated by Androsia the hag (3-204) dwell here.
	* They usually lurk in the center of the pool, hoping prey will float by.
		* If Androsia is present at 3-206 (50%); they will be lying in wait along the shallow shelf. At Androsia’s sign, they leap out and attack the designated prey. 
	* At the bottom of the pool is the 3’-tall middle section of the statue of Nertet-Indra (3-206).
		* It shows her upper torso, with arms folded across her chest.  A beautiful copper, pearl, and coral necklace (550 gp) is draped around the torso’s neck.

3 scrawny scrags: SZ M; AL C(E); AC 3; MV 30’, 150’ swimming; HD 5+5; HP 33, 29, 25; #AT 3; Dmg 2-4/2-5/3-12. Special defenses: regenerate 3 HP/rd while in fresh water.
* These are Androsia's daughters (not Varumani-derived trolls)

attack 18, def 17
